Effect of Lending the Marhun as Ariya
Ruling on the effect of ariya on rahn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a murtahin lends the marhun to the rahin as ariya and explain the consequences for guarantee, loss, and the survival of the rahn contract.

Core Idea
Lending the marhun as ariya suspends guarantee but does not cancel the rahn contract.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the contract of rahn (pledge): what happens when the murtahin (creditor) returns the pledged item (marhun) to the rahin (debtor) as a loan for use (ariya). The ruling clarifies how possession types interact and the legal effects on liability and the underlying pledge. Understanding this helps distinguish between guarantee and trust possession in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The murtahin gives the marhun to the rahin as ariya (loan for use), and the rahin takes possession.
2
Determine the effect on possession
The marhun leaves the murtahin's guarantee (daman) because the hand of ariya (yad al-ariya) is incompatible with the hand of rahn (yad al-rahn). The rahin now holds it as a trust (amanah).
Incompatibility: ariya is a trust possession, rahn is a guarantee possession.
3
Consequence of loss
If the marhun is destroyed in the rahin's possession, the murtahin's debt is unaffected; it remains due.
Because the guaranteed possession (qabd al-madmun) is lost.
4
Right of the murtahin
The murtahin has the right to take back the marhun into his possession because the rahn contract remains valid.
The contract of rahn continues, except now it is not under the ruling of guarantee.
5
Confirm the survival of the rahn
The underlying pledge agreement persists; only the guarantee aspect is suspended.
The rahn contract is not cancelled by the ariya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتهن مرہون کو راہن کے پاس عاریہ رکھدے تو کیا حکم ہے
قال واذا اعار المرتهن الرهن للراهن ليخدمه او ليعمل له عملا فقبضه خرج من ضمان المرتهن لمنافاة بين يد العارية ويد الرهن فان هلک فی ید الراهن هلک بغير شي لفوات القبض المضمون وللمرتهن ان يسترجعه الى يده لأن عقد الرهن باق الافى حكم الضمان في الحال
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ مرتبین نے مرہون راہن کو عاریت دید یا تا کہ مرہون را ہن کی خدمت کر کے یا اس کے لئے کچھ کام کرے پس راہن نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا تو مرہون مرتہن کے ضمان سے خارج ہو گیا قبضہ عاریت اور قبضہ رہن کے درمیان منافات کی وجہ سے نہیں اگر مرہون راہن کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو بغیر کسی شئی کے ہلاک ہو گا (یعنی مرتہن کا قرض ختم نہ ہوگا ) مضمون قبضہ کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اور مرتہن کو حق ہے کہ مرمون کو واپس اپنے قبضہ میں لے لے اس لئے کہ عقد رہن باقی ہے مگر اب ضمان کے حکم میں ( باقی نہیں ہے)۔
تشریح راہن نے مرہون کو مرتہن کے پاس رہن رکھ دیا اس کے بعد مرتہن نے اس مرہون کو راہن کو عاریہ کام کاج کے لئے دیدیا جس پر راہن نے قبضہ کر لیا تو اب مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ سے خارج ہو گیا ہے لہذا اب مرہون مرتبہن کی ضمانت میں نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اب مرہون راہن کے قبضہ میں ہے اور راہن کا قبضہ قبضہ امانت ہے اور مرتہن کا قبضہ قبضہ ضمانت ہے جن کے درمیان
What is the ruling if the murtahin gives the marhun to the rahin as a loan (ariya)? He (al-Quduri) said: And if the murtahin lends the marhun to the rahin to serve him or to do some work for him, and he takes possession, it leaves the guarantee of the murtahin due to the incompatibility between the hand of ariya and the hand of rahn. So if it is destroyed in the possession of the rahin, it is destroyed without anything (i.e., the murtahin's debt is not cancelled) because the guaranteed possession is lost. And the murtahin has the right to take it back into his possession because the contract of rahn remains, except that now it is not in the ruling of guarantee. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when the murtahin gives the marhun to the rahin as a loan (ariya) so that the marhun may serve the rahin or do some work for him, then the rahin takes possession of it, the marhun leaves the guarantee of the murtahin due to the incompatibility between the possession of ariya and the possession of rahn. If the marhun is destroyed in the possession of the rahin, it is destroyed without anything (i.e., the murtahin's debt is not cancelled) because the guaranteed possession is lost. And the murtahin has the right to retrieve it to his possession because the contract of rahn remains, except that now it is not in the ruling of guarantee. Explanation: The rahin placed the marhun as a pledge with the murtahin. Thereafter, the murtahin gave that marhun to the rahin as an ariya for work purposes, and the rahin took possession. Now the marhun has left the possession of the murtahin, so the marhun is not under the guarantee of the murtahin. Because now the marhun is in the possession of the rahin, and the rahin's possession is a possession of trust (qabd amanah), while the murtahin's possession is a possession of guarantee (qabd daman), and between them... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling from al-Quduri's text (part of the matn of Hidayah) on the scenario where the murtahin lends the marhun back to the rahin as ariya (loan for use). The key principle: the possession of ariya (yad al-ariya) is incompatible with the possession of rahn (yad al-rahn). Since the rahin now holds the property as a trust (amanah), the murtahin's guaranteed possession (qabd al-madmun) is lost. Consequently, the marhun leaves the murtahin's guarantee (daman). If the marhun is destroyed in the rahin's possession, the murtahin does not lose his right to the debt; it remains due because the guarantee is gone. The murtahin retains the right to take the marhun back into his possession because the underlying contract of rahn is still valid and remains in effect, but now the ruling of guarantee (hukm al-daman) is suspended. The commentary explains that the rahin's possession is a trust (qabd amanah), unlike the murtahin's possession which is a guarantee (qabd daman). This distinction is crucial for determining liability in case of loss. The passage is a ruling statement without explicit scriptural proof; it derives from Hanafi principles of possession and guarantee in rahn contracts.

Key Terms
عارية (ariya): A loan for use; the gratuitous transfer of possession of an item for the benefit of the borrower, without transfer of ownership.
يد العارية (yad al-ariya): The hand (possession) of ariya; a possessory status that is one of trust (amanah), not guarantee (daman).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the murtahin gives the marhun to the rahin as ariya (loan for use) and the rahin destroys it, what happens?
A) The murtahin's debt is cancelled.
B) The rahin must pay the value to the murtahin.
C) The murtahin's debt remains, and he can demand repayment.
D) The rahin must replace the marhun with another item.

Key Takeaway
Lending the marhun as ariya suspends the murtahin's guarantee but does not cancel the rahn contract; the debt remains due, and the murtahin may retrieve the item.

Two Guarantees of the Mortgagee When Destroying a Depreciated Pawn
Explains the liability of the mortgagee when destroying pawned item of decreased value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two distinct guarantees (daman al-istiblaq and daman al-itlaf) that arise when a mortgagee destroys a pawned item and calculate the mortgagee's liability and debt reduction using the values at possession and destruction.

Core Idea
The mortgagee bears two guarantees: one for possession value and one for destruction value, and the debt is reduced by the loss.

In pawn (rahn) transactions, if the mortgagee destroys the pawned item after its market value has dropped, the ruling becomes more nuanced. The mortgagee is not simply liable for the value at the time of destruction; instead, Hanafi fiqh separates liability into two components: one based on the mortgagee's possessory right (daman al-istiblaq) and one based on the act of destruction (daman al-itlaf). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and calculation, using a concrete example from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two liabilities
Start with the case: the pawn (marhoon) was worth 1000 at possession, then dropped to 500, and the mortgagee destroys it. Recognize that the mortgagee incurs two separate guarantees: (1) guarantee of possession (daman al-istiblaq) and (2) guarantee of loss/destruction (daman al-nuqsan or daman al-itlaf).
The two guarantees arise from different legal bases: possession and destruction.
2
Distinguish between the two guarantees
Daman al-istiblaq is based on the mortgagee's prior possession and is calculated using the value at the time of possession (day of contract). Daman al-itlaf is based on the act of destruction and uses the value at the time of destruction.
The text states: 'the pawn is guaranteed on the mortgagee because of the prior possession, not because of the change in price.'
3
Apply the values to the example
From the example: value at possession = 1000, value at destruction = 500 (after the drop). So daman al-istiblaq = 500 (the lower value at destruction? Actually the value on possession day was 1000, but due to drop it's now 500. But the text says 500 for istiblaq – that's the value on possession day? 4
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The rule is based on the principle that the mortgagee's possession is the basis for the first guarantee, not the change in market price. Therefore, the value at the time of possession is used. The destruction creates a second liability, which uses the value at the time of destruction.
This reasoning distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from schools that might combine both into one valuation.
5
Summarize the final ruling
The mortgagee must pay the pawner the value at possession (as a new pawn) and the debt is reduced by the amount of loss (value at destruction minus value at possession? Actually the loss is the decrease, so debt reduced by the decrease). The passage says: the debt is reduced by the amount of destruction (i.e., the loss). So net effect: the mortgagee compensates the pawner for the decrease in value by reducing the debt, and also compensates for the possession value by paying that amount as a new pawn or indemnity.
The end result: the pawner is made whole, and the mortgagee bears both the loss in value and the obligation to restore the possession value.

وہ مالک کے مثل ہے اور ہا لک کے بقدر قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا اور اس کے قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی اور مرتہن پر مرہون سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے مضمون ہے بھاؤ کے پلٹنے کی وجہ سے نہیں اور مرتہن پر باقی اتلاف کی وجہ سے واجب ہوگا اور وہ مرہون کی یوم تلف کی قیمت ہے۔
تشریح جس مرہون کو مرتہن نے ہلاک کیا ہے اگر اس کی قیمت گھٹ گئی تو کیا حکم ہے؟ تو فرمایا کہ اس کمی کا ضمان مرتہن پر پڑیگا۔ جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جس دن رہن رکھا گیا اس دن کی قیمت ہزار روپے ہیں پھر بھاؤ کے الٹ پھیر سے مرہون کی قیمت پانچ سو روپے رہ گئی اب مرتہن نے اس کو ہلاک کر دیا تو مرتہن پر دو ضمان ہوئے ایک تو ضمان استبلاک اور دوسرا ضمان نقصان لہذا ضمان استبلاک کی وجہ سے مرتہن پر پانچ سو روپے عربوں کی قیمت کے لازم ہوں گے جس کو رہن رکھدیا جائے گا اور نقصان کے پانچ سوروپے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کے قرض میں سے پانچ سوروپے ساقط ہو کر اب صرف پانچ سورہ گئے ۔ کیونکہ جب مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے اس وقت نقصان بھی مضمون ہوتا ہے ( کما مر ) لہذ ا نقصان کو ہلاکت کا درجہ دیا جائے گا اور مقدار نقصان قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ مرہون سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے مرتبہن کی زیر ضمانت داخل ہے لہذا یوم قبضہ کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی ۔ لا بستر اجع السعر الخ یعنی مرہون مرتہن کے زیر ضمان بھاؤ کی الٹ پھیر کی وجہ سے داخل نہیں ہوا بلکہ سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے مضمون ہے تو قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت مضمون ہو گی ۔ اور جو پانچ سو روپے کا ضمان واجب ہوا ہے وہ اختلاف کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے تو اس میں یوم تلف کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی ۔
He is like the owner, and to the extent of the destruction, the debt will be reduced, and the value on the day of his possession will be considered. The pawn is guaranteed on the mortgagee because of the prior possession, not because of the change in price. And what remains on the mortgagee becomes obligatory due to destruction, and that is the value of the pawn on the day of destruction.
Explanation: If the mortgagee destroyed the pawn and its price has decreased, what is the ruling? It was stated that the guarantee of this decrease falls upon the mortgagee. The detail is: The value on the day the pawn was given was one thousand rupees, then due to market fluctuation, the price of the pawn remained five hundred rupees. Now the mortgagee destroyed it. So there are two guarantees on the mortgagee: one is the guarantee of possession (daman al-istiblaq) and the second is the guarantee of loss (daman al-nuqsan). Therefore, due to the guarantee of possession, five hundred rupees, being the price on the day of possession, become obligatory on the mortgagee, which will be placed as a pawn. And due to the five hundred rupees of loss, from the mortgagee's debt, five hundred rupees are dropped, leaving only five hundred. Because when the pawn is destroyed, the loss is also guaranteed (as before), so the loss is given the status of destruction, and the amount of loss is deducted from the debt. And because the pawn is under the guarantee of the mortgagee due to prior possession, the value on the day of possession is considered. (Meaning) the pawn entered the guarantee of the mortgagee not due to the change in price, but due to prior possession, so the value on the day of possession is guaranteed. And the guarantee of five hundred rupees that became obligatory is due to destruction (itlaf), so in that, the value on the day of destruction is considered.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the liability of the mortgagee (murtaheen) when he destroys the pawned item (marhoon) after its market value has decreased. The ruling establishes that the mortgagee bears two distinct guarantees: (1) daman al-istiblaq (guarantee of possession) based on the value at the time the pawn was taken into possession, and (2) daman al-nuqsan (guarantee of loss) based on the decrease in value due to market fluctuation. The first guarantee requires the mortgagee to pay the pawner (rahin) the value at the time of possession (day of the contract), which is then placed as a new pawn. The second guarantee results in a reduction of the debt by the amount of the loss (here, 500 rupees). The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the pawn is in the mortgagee's guarantee due to his prior possessory right, not due to price fluctuation; therefore the value at possession is relevant for the first guarantee. For the destruction itself (itlaf), the value at the time of destruction is relevant. The passage clarifies that the mortgagee is liable for the decreased value as well, because the loss is treated like destruction. The Hanafi position is that the mortgagee is akin to a trustee (amin) but becomes liable upon destruction, and the basis of liability is possession.

Key Terms
مرہون (marhoon): The item given as pawn/pledge in a rahn contract.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or destruction.
قبضہ (qabdah): Possession taken by the mortgagee over the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi ruling, when the mortgagee destroys a pawn after its value has decreased, which of the following is true?
A) The mortgagee is liable only for the value at the time of destruction.
B) The mortgagee is liable for the value at the time of possession and the debt is reduced by the decrease in value.
C) The mortgagee's liability is solely based on the original value at the time of the contract.
D) The debt is increased by the value of the pawn.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee bears two independent guarantees: one for the value at possession and one for the loss in value due to destruction, with the debt reduced by the loss amount.

8 min
Effect of Mortgagee Lending Pawn as Ariyah to Pawner
Ruling with proof on mortgagee lending pawn as ariyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mortgagee lending the pawn to the pawner as ariyah, explain why the guarantee is suspended, and apply the ruling to scenarios of destruction and reclamation.

Core Idea
Returning the pawn as ariyah suspends the mortgagee's guarantee, but the pawn contract remains intact.

What happens when a mortgagee (murtaheen) gives the pawned item (marhoon) back to the pawner (rahin) as a loan for use? Does the contract end? Is the debt cancelled? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling from Quduri and its rationale based on the incompatibility of possession types. By understanding this ruling, you will grasp a key distinction between the contract itself and the possessory guarantee that accompanies it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial setup
Start by establishing that the pawn is in the mortgagee's possession with a guarantee (yad daman). The mortgagee then lends the pawn to the pawner as ariyah for service or work. The pawner takes possession.
The mortgagee is permitted to do this; it is mubah.
2
Determine the effect on possession and guarantee
Once the pawner takes possession as ariyah, the pawn leaves the mortgagee's guarantee. The reason is the incompatibility between yad al-ariyah (trust possession) and yad al-rahn (guarantee possession). They cannot coexist.
The pawner holds as a trust (amanah), so he is not liable for accidental loss.
3
Analyze the consequence of destruction
If the pawn is destroyed in the pawner's hands, since it is a trust, the pawner is not liable. And because the mortgagee's guarantee ended, he is also not liable. The debt remains unaffected.
The debt is not cancelled; the pawner still owes the original amount.
4
Recognize the contract's continuity
The pawn contract (aqd al-rahn) itself is not terminated. The mortgagee retains the right to reclaim the pawn at any time. The proof (al-tara) is: if the pawner dies before returning the pawn, the mortgagee's right takes precedence over other creditors, showing the contract remains.
The ariyah possession is not binding; the mortgagee can take back the pawn whenever he wishes.
5
Understand the return of guarantee
When the mortgagee takes back possession, the guarantee characteristic returns because possession in the pawn contract carries its original guarantee. This is analogous to the offspring of a pawned animal: the offspring becomes pawn but is not guaranteed; yet if the offspring is lost, no recompense is due, illustrating that guarantee is not an inseparable requisite.
The ruling of guarantee is conditional upon possession being with the mortgagee.

قال واذا اعار المرتهن الرهن للراهن ليخدمه او ليعمل له عملا فقبضه خرج من ضمان المرتهن لمنافاة بين يد العارية ويد الرهن فان هلک فی ید الراهن هلک بغير شي لفوات القبض المضمون وللمرتهن ان يسترجعه الى يده لأن عقد الرهن باق الافى حكم الضمان في الحال
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ مرتبین نے مرہون راہن کو عاریت دید یا تا کہ مرہون را ہن کی خدمت کر کے یا اس کے لئے کچھ کام کرے پس راہن نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا تو مرہون مرتہن کے ضمان سے خارج ہو گیا قبضہ عاریت اور قبضہ رہن کے درمیان منافات کی وجہ سے نہیں اگر مرہون راہن کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو بغیر کسی شئی کے ہلاک ہو گا (یعنی مرتہن کا قرض ختم نہ ہوگا ) مضمون قبضہ کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اور مرتہن کو حق ہے کہ مرمون کو واپس اپنے قبضہ میں لے لے اس لئے کہ عقد رہن باقی ہے مگر اب ضمان کے حکم میں ( باقی نہیں ہے)۔ تشریح راہن نے مرہون کو مرتہن کے پاس رہن رکھ دیا اس کے بعد مرتہن نے اس مرہون کو راہن کو عاریہ کام کاج کے لئے دیدیا جس پر راہن نے قبضہ کر لیا تو اب مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ سے خارج ہو گیا ہے لہذا اب مرہون مرتبہن کی ضمانت میں نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اب مرہون راہن کے قبضہ میں ہے اور راہن کا قبضہ قبضہ امانت ہے اور مرتہن کا قبضہ قبضہ ضمانت ہے جن کے درمیان
منافات ہے جس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں قبضوں کا اجتماع نہ ہو ورنہ اجتماع نقیضین لازم آئیگا۔ خلاصہ کلام ... اب مرہون مرتہن کے منمان میں نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اگر مرہون راہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو چونکہ اس کے پاس امانت ہے لہذا را ہن پر بھی منعمان نہیں ہے اور مرتہن کے قبضہ عمال سے خارج ہو چکا تھا لہذ امر تہن پر بھی ضمان نہیں ہے۔ البتہ مرتین کا قرض علی حالہ راہن کے ذمہ بر قرار ہے۔ لیکن یہ یادر ہے کہ اس عاریت کی وجہ سے مرتین کا قبضہ ختم ہوا ہے عقد ر ہن ختم نہیں ہوا بلکہ عقد ربن برقرار ہے لہذا مرتہن جب بھی چاہے مرہون کو راہن سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام عقدر من باقی ہے مگر اب حکم منمان نہیں ہے اور ضمان نہ ہونے کی وجہ گذر چکی ہے۔
الاترى انه لو هلك الراهن قبل ان يرده على المرتهن كان المرتهن احق به من سائر الغرماء ولهذا لان يد العارية ليست بلازمة والضمان ليس من لوازم الرهن على كل حال الاترى ان حكم الرهن ثابت في ولد الرهن وان لم يكن مضمونا بالهلاك واذا بقى عقد الرهن فاذا أخذه عاد الضمان لانه عاد القبض في عقد الرهن فيعود بصفته
ترجمہ کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر راہن مرہون کو مرتہن پر لوٹانے سے پہلے ہلاک ہو جائے تو مرتہن اس کا زیادہ حقدار ہو گا تمام قرض خواہوں سے اور یہ (عقد رہن کی بقاء ) اس لئے کہ عاریت کا قبضہ لازم نہیں ہے اور ضمان ہر حال میں رہن کے لوازم میں سے نہیں ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ رہن کے بچہ میں رہن کا حکم ثابت ہے اگر چہ وہ بچہ مضمون بالہلاک نہیں ہے اور جب کہ عقد رہن باقی سے پس جب مرہون کو مرتہن نے لے لیا تو ضمان لوٹ کر آ گیا اس لئے کہ عقد رہن میں قبضہ لوٹ کر آ گیا تو قبضہ اپنی صفت ( ضمان) کے ساتھ لوٹے گا۔
تشریح سوال جب مرتن کا قبضہ ختم ہو گیا تو عقد رہن باقی رہنے کی کیا دلیل ہے؟ جواب ... الاتری ال یعنی اگر راہن نے ابھی مرہون مرتہن کو واپس نہیں دیا تھا کہ راہن مر گیا اور راہن پر دوسرے لوگوں کا بھی قرض ہے جو مر ہون میں شریک ہونا چاہتے ہیں ۔ لیکن حق مرتہن مقدم ہوگا اور وہ تنہا مرہون کا حقدار ہوگا باقی قرض خواہوں کی اس میں شرکت نہ ہوگی اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عقد رہن باقی ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عاریت کا قبضہ لازم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مرتہن جب چاہے اس کو راہن سے واپس لے لے اس لئے عقد رہن کو باقی شمار کیا گیا ہے۔ سوال یہ تو آپ کی عجیب منطق ہے کہ رہن باقی ہے اور ضمان واجب نہیں ہے؟ جواب یہ کوئی ہمیشہ کے لئے لازم نہیں کہ جہاں بھی رہن ہو وہاں ضمان بھی لازم ہو جیسے مرہون ایک گھوڑی ہے اس نے بچہ دیا تو بچہ بھی مرہون ہو گیا لیکن اگر بچہ ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہے۔
He said: If the mortgagee lends the pawn to the pawner as a loan to serve him or to do some work for him, and he takes possession of it, it leaves the guarantee of the mortgagee due to the incompatibility between the hand of loan (yad al-ariyah) and the hand of pawn (yad al-rahn). If it is destroyed in the hand of the pawner, it is destroyed without anything (i.e., the debt is not cancelled) due to the loss of the guaranteed possession. The mortgagee has the right to take it back into his hand because the pawn contract remains, except that the ruling of guarantee is currently absent.
Translation: Quduri said: And when the mortgagee gives the pawn to the pawner as a loan (ariyah) to serve him or to do some work for him, and he takes possession of it, then the pawn leaves the guarantee of the mortgagee due to incompatibility between the possession of loan and the possession of pawn. If the pawn is destroyed in the hand of the pawner, it is destroyed without anything (i.e., the debt remains), because the guaranteed possession is lost. The mortgagee has the right to take it back into his hand because the pawn contract remains, except that now the ruling of guarantee is not present.
Explanation: The pawner placed the pawn with the mortgagee. Then the mortgagee gave the pawn back to the pawner as a loan for work, and the pawner took possession. Now the pawn has left the mortgagee's possession, so it is no longer under the mortgagee's guarantee. Because the pawn is now in the pawner's possession, and the pawner's possession is a trust possession (yad amanah), whereas the mortgagee's possession is a guarantee possession (yad daman). There is incompatibility between them, requiring that these two possessions cannot coexist, otherwise there would be a contradiction. In summary: the pawn is no longer in the mortgagee's guarantee. Therefore, if the pawn is destroyed with the pawner, since it is a trust, the pawner is not liable, and since it left the mortgagee's guaranteed possession, the mortgagee is also not liable. However, the mortgagee's debt remains as it was on the pawner. But note: due to this loan, the mortgagee's possession has ended, but the pawn contract has not ended; rather, the pawn contract continues. Therefore, the mortgagee can take back the pawn from the pawner whenever he wishes. In summary: the contract remains, but the ruling of guarantee is not present, and the reason for the absence of guarantee has passed.
Do you not see that if the pawner dies before returning it to the mortgagee, the mortgagee has a greater right to it than all other creditors? And this is because the possession of loan is not binding, and guarantee is not necessarily a requisite of pawn in all cases. Do you not see that the ruling of pawn is established for the offspring of the pawn, even though the offspring is not guaranteed against destruction? And when the pawn contract remains, then when he takes it, the guarantee returns because possession returns in the pawn contract, so it returns with its characteristic (guarantee).
Translation: Do you not see that if the pawner dies before returning the pawn to the mortgagee, the mortgagee has a greater right to it than all creditors? And this (continuation of the pawn contract) is because the possession of loan is not binding, and guarantee is not a requisite of pawn in every case. Do you not see that the ruling of pawn is established for the offspring of the pawn, even though that offspring is not guaranteed against destruction? And when the pawn contract remains, then when the mortgagee takes it, the guarantee returns because possession returns in the pawn contract, so it returns with its characteristic (guarantee).
Explanation: Question: When the mortgagee's possession ended, what is the proof that the pawn contract remains? Answer: Do you not see? If the pawner had not yet returned the pawn to the mortgagee and died, and the pawner had other debts, they would want to share in the pawn. But the mortgagee's right takes precedence, and he alone is entitled to the pawn; other creditors do not share. This shows that the pawn contract remains. And the reason is that the possession of loan is not binding; the mortgagee can take it back whenever he wishes. Therefore, the pawn contract is considered to remain. Question: That is strange logic: the pawn remains but guarantee is not obligatory? Answer: It is not necessary that wherever there is a pawn, guarantee is also obligatory, just as if the pawned item is a mare and she gives birth, the foal also becomes pawn, but if the foal is destroyed, its guarantee is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the situation where the mortgagee (murtaheen) returns the pawned item (marhoon) to the pawner (rahin) as a loan for use (ariyah). The ruling from Quduri states that the pawn leaves the mortgagee's guarantee because the nature of possession for loan (yad al-ariyah) is incompatible with the nature of possession for pawn (yad al-rahn). The former is a trust possession (yad amanah) while the latter is a guarantee possession (yad daman). They cannot coexist. Consequently, if the pawn is destroyed while in the pawner's hands, neither party is liable for the value: the pawner holds it as a trust (amanah) so no liability on him, and the mortgagee no longer has guarantee possession. However, the original debt remains unaffected. Importantly, the pawn contract (aqd al-rahn) itself is not terminated; only the possessory guarantee is suspended. The mortgagee retains the right to reclaim possession at any time. When possession returns, the guarantee characteristic returns as well. The passage supports this with an analogy: if the pawner dies before returning the pawn, the mortgagee's right to the pawn takes precedence over other creditors, proving the contract's continuity. Another analogy is the offspring of a pawned animal: the offspring becomes part of the pawn but is not subject to guarantee if destroyed. This shows that guarantee is not an inseparable requisite of the pawn contract. The Hanafi position is that the contract remains valid despite the temporary change in possession, and the ruling of guarantee is conditional upon possession being with the mortgagee.

Key Terms
عاریہ (ariyah): A loan for use; a contract where one person allows another to use an item for free, with the borrower responsible only for misuse.
ید العارية (yad al-ariyah): The hand/possession of a borrower in an ariyah contract, which is a trust possession.
ید الرهن (yad al-rahn): The hand/possession of the mortgagee over the pawned item, which is a guarantee possession (yad daman).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee lends the pawn back to the pawner as ariyah and it is destroyed, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt is cancelled
B) The debt remains
C) The debt is halved
D) The mortgagee must pay the pawner

Key Takeaway
The pawn contract remains valid even when possession returns to the pawner; only the guarantee is suspended, and the mortgagee can reclaim the pawn at any time.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Loan for Use (Ariyah) on the Pledge Contract
Ruling with proof on ariyah's effect on pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the effect of a mortgagee lending a pledged item to the mortgagor for use, and apply the proof that the pledge contract remains valid despite temporary suspension of liability.

Core Idea
Liability is not an inseparable part of pledge; the contract can survive without it.

In pledge transactions, the mortgagee normally holds possession and bears liability for the item. But what happens when the mortgagee returns the item to the mortgagor as a loan for use? Does the pledge dissolve? This passage from the Hidayah clarifies that the pledge contract persists, though liability is suspended temporarily. The proof is drawn from the mortgagee's continued priority over creditors and the analogy to a pledged animal's offspring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mortgagee (murtahin) gives the pledged item (marhun) to the mortgagor (rahn) as a loan for use (ariyah). The item is now back in the mortgagor's possession.
This is not a sale or return of the debt; it is a gratuitous transfer of use.
2
State the legal effect
The pledge contract ('aqd al-rahn) remains valid and does not dissolve. However, the mortgagee's liability (daman) is suspended during the ariyah period. Neither party is liable if the item perishes without negligence.
The debt remains intact; the mortgagee can reclaim the item at will.
3
Locate the primary proof
The text presents a qiyas: if the mortgagor dies before returning the item, the mortgagee has priority over other creditors for that item. This proves the pledge contract still exists, because if it were void, the mortgagee would have no special right.
Arabic phrase: 'الاترى انه لو هلك الراهن قبل ان يرده على المرتهن كان المرتهن احق به من سائر الغرماء'
4
Understand the analogy to offspring
The passage compares to a pledged mare that gives birth. The foal is also pledged but is not subject to liability if it perishes. This shows that liability is not a necessary attribute of pledge; the contract can exist without it.
The foal is part of the pledge (tab'a), yet no daman attaches.
5
Conclude with reinstatement
When the mortgagee takes back possession (reclaims the item), liability returns automatically because possession in pledge inherently carries the attribute of liability.
Upon re-possession, the item re-enters the mortgagee's guarantee.

منافات ہے جس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں قبضوں کا اجتماع نہ ہو ورنہ اجتماع نقیضین لازم آئیگا۔ خلاصہ کلام ... اب مرہون مرتہن کے منمان میں نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اگر مرہون راہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو چونکہ اس کے پاس امانت ہے لہذا را ہن پر بھی منعمان نہیں ہے اور مرتہن کے قبضہ عمال سے خارج ہو چکا تھا لہذ امر تہن پر بھی ضمان نہیں ہے۔ البتہ مرتین کا قرض علی حالہ راہن کے ذمہ بر قرار ہے۔ لیکن یہ یادر ہے کہ اس عاریت کی وجہ سے مرتین کا قبضہ ختم ہوا ہے عقد ر ہن ختم نہیں ہوا بلکہ عقد ربن برقرار ہے لہذا مرتہن جب بھی چاہے مرہون کو راہن سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام عقدر من باقی ہے مگر اب حکم منمان نہیں ہے اور ضمان نہ ہونے کی وجہ گذر چکی ہے۔ مرتین کا قبضہ ختم ہو گیا تو عقد رہن باقی رہے گا یا نہیں الاترى انه لو هلك الراهن قبل ان يرده على المرتهن كان المرتهن احق به من سائر الغرماء ولهذا لان يد العارية ليست بلازمة والضمان ليس من لوازم الرهن على كل حال الاترى ان حكم الرهن ثابت في ولد الرهن وان لم يكن مضمونا بالهلاك واذا بقى عقد الرهن فاذا أخذه عاد الضمان لانه عاد القبض في عقد الرهن فيعود بصفته ترجمہ کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر راہن مرہون کو مرتہن پر لوٹانے سے پہلے ہلاک ہو جائے تو مرتہن اس کا زیادہ حقدار ہو گا تمام قرض خواہوں سے اور یہ (عقد رہن کی بقاء ) اس لئے کہ عاریت کا قبضہ لازم نہیں ہے اور ضمان ہر حال میں رہن کے لوازم میں سے نہیں ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ رہن کے بچہ میں رہن کا حکم ثابت ہے اگر چہ وہ بچہ مضمون بالہلاک نہیں ہے اور جب کہ عقد رہن باقی سے پس جب مرہون کو مرتہن نے لے لیا تو ضمان لوٹ کر آ گیا اس لئے کہ عقد رہن میں قبضہ لوٹ کر آ گیا تو قبضہ اپنی صفت ( ضمان) کے ساتھ لوٹے گا۔ تشریح سوال جب مرتن کا قبضہ ختم ہو گیا تو عقد رہن باقی رہنے کی کیا دلیل ہے؟ جواب ... الاتری ال یعنی اگر راہن نے ابھی مرہون مرتہن کو واپس نہیں دیا تھا کہ راہن مر گیا اور راہن پر دوسرے لوگوں کا بھی قرض ہے جو مر ہون میں شریک ہونا چاہتے ہیں ۔ لیکن حق مرتہن مقدم ہوگا اور وہ تنہا مرہون کا حقدار ہوگا باقی قرض خواہوں کی اس میں شرکت نہ ہوگی اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عقد رہن باقی ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عاریت کا قبضہ لازم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مرتہن جب چاہے اس کو راہن سے واپس لے لے اس لئے عقد رہن کو باقی شمار کیا گیا ہے۔ سوال یہ تو آپ کی عجیب منطق ہے کہ رہن باقی ہے اور ضمان واجب نہیں ہے؟ جواب یہ کوئی ہمیشہ کے لئے لازم نہیں کہ جہاں بھی رہن ہو وہاں ضمان بھی لازم ہو جیسے مرہون ایک گھوڑی ہے اس نے بچہ دیا تو بچہ بھی مرہون ہو گیا لیکن اگر بچہ ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہے۔
بہر حال صورت مذکورہ میں عقد ر ہن باقی ہے اور جب عقد باقی ہے تو جب مرتہن نے مرہون کو واپس لے لیا تو ضمان بھی لوٹ کر آ گیا کیونکہ جب عقد ر ہن میں قبضہ لوٹ آئے گا تو اپنی صفت کے ساتھ لوٹ کر آئیگا اور قبضہ کرہن کی صفت ضمان ہے لہذا پھر مرہون مرتہن کی ضمانت میں داخل ہو گیا۔
There is a conflict whose requirement is that these two possessions cannot combine; otherwise, the combination of opposites would be necessary. Summary: The pledged item is not under the mortgagee's guarantee. Therefore, if the pledged item perishes with the mortgagor, since it is a trust with him, the mortgagor is not liable, and since it had left the mortgagee's possession, the mortgagee is also not liable. However, the mortgagee's debt remains due from the mortgagor. But remember: due to this loan-for-use, the mortgagee's possession ended, but the pledge contract did not end; rather, the pledge contract remains. So the mortgagee can take back the pledged item from the mortgagor whenever he wishes. Summary: The contract of pledge remains, but the ruling of liability no longer applies, and the reason for no liability has passed. When the mortgagee's possession ended, does the pledge contract remain or not? Do you not see that if the mortgagor dies before returning it to the mortgagee, the mortgagee has more right to it than other creditors? And this is because the hand of loan-for-use is not binding, and liability is not a necessary concomitant of pledge in every case. Do you not see that the ruling of pledge is established for the offspring of the pledged animal, even though it is not guaranteed against destruction? And when the pledge contract remains, then when he takes it, liability returns because possession has returned in the pledge contract, so it returns with its attribute." Translation: Do you not see that if the mortgagor dies before returning the pledged item to the mortgagee, the mortgagee has more right to it than all creditors? And this (the residue of the pledge contract) is because the possession of loan-for-use is not binding, and liability is not among the necessary concomitants of pledge in every case. Do you not see that the ruling of pledge is established for the offspring of the pledged animal, even though that offspring is not guaranteed against destruction? And when the pledge contract remains, then when the mortgagee takes the pledged item, liability returns because possession has returned in the pledge contract, so possession returns with its attribute (liability). Explanation: Question: When the mortgagee's possession ended, what is the proof that the pledge contract remains? Answer: The statement "Do you not see..." i.e., if the mortgagor had not yet returned the pledged item to the mortgagee and then died, and the mortgagor has other debts, and other creditors want to share in the pledged item, but the mortgagee's right is given priority, and he alone is entitled to the pledged item. Other creditors have no share. From this, it is understood that the pledge contract remains. And the reason is that the possession of loan-for-use is not binding; rather, the mortgagee can take it back from the mortgagor whenever he wishes. Therefore, the pledge contract is considered to remain. Question: This is strange logic: the pledge remains but liability is not obligatory? Answer: It is not always necessary that wherever there is a pledge, liability is also obligatory. For example, if the pledged item is a mare and she gives birth, the foal also becomes pledged, but if the foal perishes, its liability is not obligatory. In any case, in the mentioned scenario, the pledge contract remains. And when the contract remains, when the mortgagee takes back the pledged item, liability also returns because when possession returns in the pledge contract, it returns with its attribute, and the attribute of possession in pledge is liability. Therefore, the pledged item enters under the mortgagee's guarantee.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah commentary. It addresses the scenario where the mortgagee (murtahin) gives the pledged item (marhun) as a loan for use (ariyah) to the mortgagor (rahn). The legal consequence is that the mortgagee's possessory interest and liability (daman) are suspended, but the underlying pledge contract ('aqd al-rahn) remains valid. The proof is given from the principle that if the mortgagor dies before returning the item, the mortgagee retains priority over other creditors, indicating the pledge contract still exists. Additionally, the author compares this to the offspring of a pledged animal, which is also part of the pledge but not subject to liability. The commentary clarifies that the ariyah possession is not binding (ghayr lazim), so the mortgagee can reclaim the item at any time, and upon re-possession, liability is reinstated because possession in pledge inherently carries liability. This ruling is based on the Hanafi school's understanding that liability is not an inseparable attribute of pledge; it can be temporarily removed without nullifying the contract.

Key Terms
عقد الرهن ('aqd al-rahn): The contract of pledge; a security contract where a property is given as collateral for a debt.
عارية ('ariyah): A loan for use; gratuitous transfer of possession without transfer of ownership.
ضمان (daman): Liability for loss or destruction; the obligation to compensate if the item perishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgagee gives the pledged item as a loan for use to the mortgagor, and the item perishes with the mortgagor without any negligence, who is liable?
A) The mortgagor is liable because he had possession.
B) The mortgagee is liable because he is the original creditor.
C) Neither is liable; the debt remains unpaid.
D) Both are jointly liable.

Key Takeaway
The pledge contract remains valid even when liability is temporarily suspended through a loan for use; liability is not a necessary attribute of pledge.

Giving a Pledged Item to a Third Party with Permission
Extends previous ruling to a third party with permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pledged item is given as ariyah to a third party with the other party's permission and explain why liability is removed.

Core Idea
Permission from the other party transfers the pledged item to a trust possession, removing liability.

In the previous lesson, we learned that if the mortgagee returns the pledged item to the mortgagor as a loan for use, the mortgagee's liability ends. This lesson extends that principle: even if the item is given to a third party (ajnabi) with the other party's permission, the same ruling applies. The pledge contract remains intact, and neither the borrower nor the mortgagee is liable if the item perishes without negligence. This illustrates how the Hanafi school protects both parties' respected rights (haqq muhtaram) while accommodating practical needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the permission condition
The act is giving the pledged item as ariyah (loan for use) to a third party. The key condition is that the other party (mortgagor if mortgagee gives, or mortgagee if mortgagor gives) must have given permission. Without permission, liability would attach as in the base case.
Permission is explicit or implicit? The text states 'with permission' – it must be explicit or clearly implied.
2
Determine the ruling on liability
The text states that the ruling of liability (daman) falls (saqat). This means if the item perishes with the third party, no one is liable for compensation, provided there is no transgression (ta'addi).
This is identical to the previous ruling where the item was given to the mortgagor.
3
Analyze the reasoning (dalil aqli)
The reasoning is twofold: (1) the third party's possession is a trust (amanat) – in Hanafi law, a trustee is not liable for loss without negligence; (2) both the mortgagor and mortgagee have a respected right (haqq muhtaram) in the pledged item, so either can reclaim it and restore the pledge status.
The same reason (ما قلنا – 'what we have said') from the previous lesson applies here.
4
Note the practical consequence for the pledge contract
The pledge contract is not invalidated by this temporary transfer. Each party retains the right to demand the item back and have it pledged as before. The mortgagee's debt remains due from the mortgagor.
This protects both parties' interests while allowing temporary use by a third party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتبہن کا راہن کی اجازت سے اور راہن نے مرتہن کی اجازت سے اجنبی کے پاس عاریت رکھنے کا حکم
و کذالک لواعاره احدهما اجنبيا باذن الآخر سقط حكم الضمان لما قلنا ولكل واحد منهما ان يرده رهنا كما كان لان لكل واحد حقاً محترما فيه
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر مرہون کو ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے کسی اجنبی کو عاریت پر دید یا دوسرے کی اجازت سے تو ضمان کا حکم ساقط ہو جائے گا اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو حق ہے کہ مرہون کو حسب سابق رہن کی طرف لوٹا دے اس لئے کہ اس میں ہر ایک کا حق محترم ہے۔ تشریح اگر بجائے راہن کو عاربیت دینے کے کسی اجنبی کو عاریت دی خواہ کون سے نے دی ہومگر دوسرے ساتھی کی اجازت سے دی ہو تب بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ اب مرہون کے زیر ضمان داخل نہیں ہے اور اگر مستغیر کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو کسی پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا مستغیر پر اس لئے کہ اسکا قبضہ قبضہ امانت ہے اور امانت میں تعدی کے بغیر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور مرتہن پر اس لئے کہ مضمانتی قرض دلیل سابق کی وجہ سے ختم ہو چکا ہے۔ لہذا مرتین کا قرض راہن پر بدستور باقی رہے گا ، اور چونکہ مرہون میں را ہن دو مرتہن دونوں کا حق محترم ہے لہذا ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ مستعغیر سے مرہون کو واپس لے کر مرہون ۔ بنائے جیسے پہلے تھا۔
Ruling on the mortgagee giving the pledged item to a third party with the mortgagor's permission, and the mortgagor giving it with the mortgagee's permission.
Similarly, if one of them gives it to a third party with the other's permission, the ruling of liability falls, due to what we have said. And each of them has the right to return it as a pledge as it was, because each of them has a respected right in it.
Translation: Similarly, if one of these two gives the pledged item to a third party as a loan for use with the other's permission, the ruling of liability falls due to the same reason we have mentioned. And each of them has the right to return the pledged item to the state of pledge as before, because each of them has a respected right in it. Explanation: If instead of giving it to the mortgagor, it is given to a third party—whether by the mortgagor or the mortgagee—but with the other's permission, then the same ruling applies: the pledged item does not enter under liability. If it perishes with the borrower (musta'ir), no one is liable. The borrower is not liable because his possession is a trust possession, and in trust, liability is not obligatory without transgression. The mortgagee is not liable because the liability debt has ended due to the previous reason. So the mortgagee's debt remains due from the mortgagor. And since both the mortgagor and mortgagee have a respected right in the pledged item, each of them has the right to take it back from the borrower and make it a pledge as before.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that extends the previous principle to the case where the pledged item is given as a loan for use to a third party (ajnabi) with the permission of the other party. The ruling is identical: the liability (daman) is removed, and the pledge contract continues. The reason is that the possession of the third party is a trust (amanat), so no liability attaches. Each party (mortgagor and mortgagee) has a respected right in the item, so either can reclaim it and restore the pledge status. The commentary reinforces that neither the borrower nor the mortgagee is liable if the item perishes without negligence.

Key Terms
مستعير (musta'ir): The borrower in an ariyah contract; the third party receiving the item for use.
حق محترم (haqq muhtaram): A respected right; a right that is inviolable and must be preserved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee gives the pledged item to a third party with the mortgagor's permission, and the item perishes with the third party without negligence, who is liable?
A) The third party, because he had possession.
B) The mortgagee, because he gave it away.
C) The mortgagor, because he owns the item.
D) No one is liable for the loss.

Key Takeaway
Giving a pledged item to a third party with the other party's permission removes liability and preserves the pledge contract.

Distinction: Sale, Lease, or Gift vs. Ariyah in Pledge Transfer
Contrasts the effect of sale, lease, and gift with ariyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permanent transfers (sale, lease, gift) and temporary transfer (ariyah) in the context of a pledge, and state the Hanafi ruling that the former nullifies the pledge permanently while the latter does not.

Core Idea
Sale, lease, or gift of a pledged item permanently terminates the pledge; ariyah does not, because only permanent transfers create a binding right.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: what happens when a pledged item is transferred to a third party by the mortgagor or mortgagee with the other's permission? The answer depends on the type of contract. Permanent transfers (sale, lease, gift) nullify the pledge, while ariyah leaves it intact. This distinction has practical consequences, especially regarding the mortgagee's priority upon the mortgagor's death.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on permanent transfers
Identify that sale, lease, and gift by either party with permission permanently remove the item from the pledge. The item does not return except with a new contract.
2
Identify the contrasting case of ariyah
Ariyah (temporary loan for use) does not nullify the pledge. The item remains pledged even after the transfer.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The difference arises because sale, lease, and gift create a binding right (haqq lazim) in the property, which is incompatible with the pledge. Ariyah creates no such right.
Haqq lazim: an irrevocable right like ownership or tenancy.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the mortgagor dies after a permanent transfer, the mortgagee becomes an ordinary creditor (like other creditors). In ariyah, the mortgagee retains priority over the pledged item.
5
Evaluate the opposing view
Some might analogize all permission-based transfers to ariyah, but the Hanafi school rejects this analogy due to the binding right distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن اور مرتہن میں سے کسی نے دوسرے کی اجازت سے اجنبی کو مرہون فروخت کر دیا یا اجارہ پر دیدیا یا ہبہ کردیا تو کیا حکم ہے؟
و هذا بخلاف الاجارة والبيع والهبة من اجنبى اذا باشر احدهما باذن الأخر حيث يخرج عن الرهن فلا يعود الا بعقد مبتدأ ولو مات الراهن قبل الردالى المرتهن يكون المرتهن اسوة للغرماء لانه تعلق بالرهن حق لازم بهذه التصرفات فيبطل به حكم الرهن أما بالعارية لم يتعلق به حق لازم فافترقا
ترجمہ اور یہ (عامریت کا مسئلہ ) اجنبی کے ہاتھ اجارہ اور بیع اور ہبہ کے خلاف ہے جبکہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے دوسرے کی اجازت سے کیا ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ رہن سے خارج ہو جائے گا پس رہن نہیں لوٹے گا مگر جدید عقد سے اگر راہن مر جائے مرتہن کی جانب لوٹانے سے پہلے تو مرتہن قرض خواہوں کے برابر ہو گا اس لئے کہ مرہون کے ساتھ ان تصرفات کے سبب سے حق لازم متعلق ہو گیا تو اس حق لازم کی وجہ سے رہن کا حکم باطل ہو گیا بہر حال عاریت کی وجہ سے مرہون کے ساتھ حق لازم متعلق نہیں ہوا پس یہ دونوں
What is the ruling if one of the mortgagor or mortgagee, with the other's permission, sells, leases, or gifts the pledged item to a third party?
And this is different from lease, sale, and gift to a third party when one of them does it with the other's permission, because then it leaves the pledge and does not return except with a new contract. If the mortgagor dies before returning it to the mortgagee, then the mortgagee is like other creditors. Because a binding right (haqq lazim) becomes attached to the pledged item through these transactions, and thereby the ruling of pledge is nullified. As for ariyah, no binding right attaches to it, so they differ.
Translation: And this (the matter of ariyah) is different from the case of a third party receiving the item through lease, sale, or gift, when one of the two parties does it with the other's permission. In that case, the item leaves the pledge and will not return except with a new contract. If the mortgagor dies before returning it to the mortgagee, then the mortgagee becomes like equal to the creditors. Because a binding right has attached to the pledged item due to these transactions, and this binding right nullifies the ruling of pledge. However, in the case of ariyah, no binding right attaches to the pledged item, so the two cases differ.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage distinguishes the ruling for ariyah from three other transactions: sale (bay'), lease (ijarah), and gift (hibah). If the mortgagor or mortgagee, with the other's permission, transfers the pledged item to a third party via these contracts, the pledge contract is permanently terminated. The item can only be re-pledged with a new contract. If the mortgagor dies before returning it, the mortgagee loses his priority and becomes an ordinary creditor. The reason is that these transactions create a binding right (haqq lazim) in the property, which is incompatible with the pledge. In contrast, ariyah creates no such binding right, so the pledge remains. This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh that illustrates the principle that pledge requires the property to remain free of binding third-party rights.

Key Terms
حق لازم (haqq lazim): A binding right; a right that is irrevocable and attaches to the property, such as ownership or a tenancy right.
عقد مبتدأ ('aqd mubtada'): A new contract; the pledge would need to be re-established from scratch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee leases the pledged item to a third party with the mortgagor's permission, what is the status of the pledge?
A) The pledge continues as before.
B) The pledge is suspended until the lease ends.
C) The pledge is permanently terminated.
D) The pledge becomes void but revives automatically.

Key Takeaway
Sale, lease, and gift permanently terminate a pledge because they create a binding right; ariyah does not, so the pledge remains intact.

Return of Liability When Mortgagee Retakes Possession of Pawn
Ruling on liability returning upon retaking pawn possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the liability (dhaman) of a pawn is reinstated when the mortgagee retakes possession after a temporary removal.

Core Idea
Possession in pawn carries liability; when possession returns, liability returns.

The passage addresses a subtle issue in pawn (rahn): what happens when the mortgagee temporarily loses possession of the pawn and later retakes it? Some might think the pawn's security status is lost. The author clarifies that the pawn contract remains intact, and upon retaking possession, the liability (dhaman) automatically returns because possession in a pawn contract inherently carries the attribute of liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The pawn contract remains valid despite temporary loss of possession.
2
Identify the trigger
The mortgagee retakes possession of the pawn.
3
Identify the consequence
The liability (dhaman) returns automatically.
4
Understand the rationale
Possession in pawn inherently has the attribute of liability; when possession returns, its attribute returns.
5
Distinguish from other scenarios
If the pawn contract were terminated (e.g., by full repayment), possession would not return with liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بہر حال صورت مذکورہ میں عقد ر ہن باقی ہے اور جب عقد باقی ہے تو جب مرتہن نے مرہون کو واپس لے لیا تو ضمان بھی لوٹ کر آ گیا کیونکہ جب عقد ر ہن میں قبضہ لوٹ آئے گا تو اپنی صفت کے ساتھ لوٹ کر آئیگا اور قبضہ ک رہن کی صفت ضمان ہے لہذا پھر مرہون مرتہن کی ضمانت میں داخل ہو گیا۔
In any case, in the mentioned situation, the contract of pawn remains, and when the contract remains, when the mortgagee took back the pawn, the liability also returned because when possession returns in a pawn contract, it returns with its attribute, and the attribute of possession in pawn is liability, so again the pawn entered into the mortgagee's liability.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary. The author explains that when a pawn was temporarily removed from the mortgagee's possession (e.g., by being given to another as a trust), and then the mortgagee retakes possession, the pawn's status as a security with liability (dhaman) is restored. The key principle is that possession in a pawn contract inherently carries the attribute of liability for the debt; when possession returns, that attribute returns automatically, provided the pawn contract itself remains valid. This is because the pawn contract is not dissolved by such temporary changes in possession.

Key Terms
عقد رہن (aql rahn): The contract of pawn/mortgage, which is a contract of security for a debt.
ضمان (daman): Liability or responsibility; in this context, the attribute of possession in pawn, meaning the pawn serves as security for the debt.
قبضہ (qabdah): Possession; taking physical control of the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The liability returns automatically because the pawn contract remains.
C) The liability is extinguished permanently.
D) The liability becomes shared between mortgagee and debtor.

Key Takeaway
Temporary loss of possession does not void the pawn contract; upon retaking, liability is restored.

Giving Pawn as Ariyah to a Third Party with Permission
Ruling on giving pawn as a loan (ariyah) to an outsider with permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pawn is given as ariyah to a third party with permission and explain the consequences regarding liability and reinstatement of the pawn.

Core Idea
A pawn given as ariyah with permission loses its security status but can be reinstated; no one is liable for loss.

This lesson explores a specific scenario in the contract of pawn (rahn): what happens if the pawned item is given as a gratuitous loan (ariyah) to a third party with the permission of the other interested party (the pawnor or the mortgagee). The Hanafi ruling clarifies that the security aspect is suspended, but the debt remains and the pawn can be reinstated. This illustrates the interplay between different contracts and the protection of rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Parties and the Act
The act is giving the pawned item (al-marhun) as ariyah to a third party (ajnabi). The parties are the pawnor (rahin), the mortgagee (murtahin), and the borrower (musta'ir). Identify who is giving and who is permitting.
The permission must be from the other party, i.e., if the pawnor gives, the mortgagee must permit, and vice versa.
2
Determine the Effect on the Security (Hukm al-Daman)
The ruling states that 'the ruling of liability (daman) falls' — meaning the pawn is no longer held as security for the debt. The link between the pawn and the debt is severed as long as the item is in the hands of the third party.
This applies regardless of which party gives the ariyah, as long as permission is obtained.
3
Analyze Liability in Case of Destruction
If the item is destroyed while with the borrower, no one is liable for its value as security. The borrower is not liable because his possession is a trust (amanah) — he is an amin. The mortgagee is not liable because the security status has fallen. The pawnor remains liable for the original debt.
This is a key difference from a sale or lease, which might transfer liability.
4
Explain the Right of Reinstatement
Both the pawnor and the mortgagee have the right to demand the item back from the borrower and restore it as a pawn. This is because each has a protected right (haqq muharram) in the item.
The pawn contract is not permanently terminated; it is merely suspended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و کذالک لواعاره احدهما اجنبيا باذن الآخر سقط حكم الضمان لما قلنا ولكل واحد منهما ان يرده رهنا كما كان لان لكل واحد حقاً محترما فيه
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر مرہون کو ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے کسی اجنبی کو عاریت پر دید یا دوسرے کی اجازت سے تو ضمان کا حکم ساقط ہو جائے گا اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو حق ہے کہ مرہون کو حسب سابق رہن کی طرف لوٹا دے اس لئے کہ اس میں ہر ایک کا حق محترم ہے۔
تشریح اگر بجائے راہن کو عاربیت دینے کے کسی اجنبی کو عاریت دی خواہ کونے نے دی ہومگر دوسرے ساتھی کی اجازت سے دی ہو تب بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ اب مرہون کے زیر ضمان داخل نہیں ہے اور اگر مستغیر کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو کسی پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا مستغیر پر اس لئے کہ اسکا قبضہ قبضہ امانت ہے اور امانت میں تعدی کے بغیر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور مرتہن پر اس لئے کہ مضمانتی قرض دلیل سابق کی وجہ سے ختم ہو چکا ہے۔ لہذا مرتین کا قرض راہن پر بدستور باقی رہے گا ، اور چونکہ مرہون میں را ہن دو مرتہن دونوں کا حق محترم ہے لہذا ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ مستعغیر سے مرہون کو واپس لے کر مرہون ۔ بنائے جیسے پہلے تھا۔
And similarly, if one of them (mortgagee or pawnor) gives it as ariyah to a third party with the permission of the other, the ruling of dhaman falls due to what we have said, and each of them has the right to return it as a pawn as it was, because each has a protected right in it.
Translation: And similarly, if the pawned item is given by one of them to a stranger as a loan without compensation (ariyah) with the permission of the other, then the rule of liability falls, due to the same reason we have stated. And each of them has the right to return the pawn to its previous state, because each has a protected right in it.
Explanation: If instead of giving to the pawnor, the pawn is given as ariyah to a stranger, regardless of which of the two gives it, provided it is with the permission of the other partner, then the same ruling applies: the pawn is no longer under the liability (dhaman). And if it is destroyed in the hands of the borrower, no one is liable. The borrower is not liable because his possession is a trust (amanah), and in a trust, liability does not apply without transgression. The mortgagee is not liable because the liability for the debt has ended due to the previous reason. Therefore, the mortgagee's debt remains on the pawnor. And since both the pawnor and the mortgagee have a protected right in the pawn, each of them has the right to take it back from the borrower and make it a pawn as before.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement followed by its explanation. The key point: if either the pawnor or the mortgagee gives the pawned item to a third party as a gratuitous loan (ariyah) with the permission of the other, the pawn ceases to be held as security (dhaman falls). This is because the possession of the borrower is a trust, and the pawn's connection to the debt is severed. If the item is destroyed while with the borrower, neither the borrower nor the mortgagee is liable; the debt remains intact between pawnor and mortgagee. However, each party (pawnor and mortgagee) retains the right to demand the return of the item from the borrower and re-establish it as a pawn, since both have a protected interest in it. This is a key distinction from transactions like sale or lease, which transfer ownership or create irrevocable rights.

Key Terms
عاریت (ariyah): A contract of gratuitous loan for use; the borrower does not pay rent and must return the item.
ضمان (حکم الضمان) (hukm al-daman): The legal ruling of liability; here meaning the status of the pawn as security for the debt.
قبضہ امانت (qabd amanat): Possession as a trust; the possessor is not liable for loss without negligence.
حق محترم (haqq muharram): A protected right that is respected by the law, giving the holder the ability to reclaim or enforce it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the pawned item given as ariyah with permission is destroyed in the hands of the borrower, who is liable for its value as security?
A) The pawnor (rahin)
B) The mortgagee (murtahin)
C) The borrower (musta'ir)
D) No one

Key Takeaway
A pawn given as ariyah with permission is not terminated; its security function is suspended, and both parties can reinstate it, while no one bears liability for loss in the borrower's trust possession.

Contrast: Sale, Lease, Gift vs. Ariyah on Pawn
Ruling that sale, lease, and gift of pawn with permission permanently end the pawn contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between transactions that create an irrevocable right (haqq lazim) and those that do not, and state the effect on the pawn contract.

Core Idea
Sale, lease, or gift of a pawn with permission ends the pawn permanently; ariyah does not.

In Hanafi pawn law, certain transactions involving the pawned item with the other party's permission have dramatically different effects. While a loan for use (ariyah) temporarily suspends the pawn without ending it, a sale, lease, or gift creates a permanent, irrevocable right in a third party, thereby terminating the pawn contract once and for all. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining the mortgagee's rights, especially if the pawnor dies before the pawn is returned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key distinction
Recognize that the crucial factor is whether the transaction creates an irrevocable right (haqq lazim) in a third party. Sale, lease, and gift do; ariyah does not.
Haqq lazim means a right that cannot be unilaterally revoked.
2
Analyze the effect of transactions creating haqq lazim
When the pawnor or mortgagee, with the other's permission, sells, leases, or gives the pawn to a stranger, the pawn leaves the pawn contract permanently. It cannot be reinstated except by a new contract.
The transaction itself is valid, but it destroys the pawn relationship.
3
Trace the consequence if the pawnor dies
If the pawnor dies before the pawn is returned to the mortgagee, the mortgagee loses his priority over other creditors. He becomes 'uswat lil-ghurama' (equal to other creditors) and shares the pawn's value proportionally.
This is because the pawn contract no longer exists to give him a security interest.
4
Contrast with ariyah
If the pawn is given as a loan for use (ariyah) with permission, no irrevocable right attaches. The pawn contract continues; the pawn can be returned and the pawn restored.
Ariyah is a non-binding contract (ghayr lazim) and can be revoked anytime.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Test your understanding: Suppose the mortgagee lends the pawn to a friend with the pawnor's permission. The friend later returns it. Does the pawn contract revive automatically? Answer: Yes, because ariyah creates no haqq lazim.

Source Text

و هذا بخلاف الاجارة والبيع والهبة من اجنبى اذا باشر احدهما باذن الأخر حيث يخرج عن الرهن فلا يعود الا بعقد مبتدأ ولو مات الراهن قبل الردالى المرتهن يكون المرتهن اسوة للغرماء لانه تعلق بالرهن حق لازم بهذه التصرفات فيبطل به حكم الرهن أما بالعارية لم يتعلق به حق لازم فافترقا
ترجمہ اور یہ (عامریت کا مسئلہ ) اجنبی کے ہاتھ اجارہ اور بیع اور ہبہ کے خلاف ہے جبکہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے دوسرے کی اجازت سے کیا ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ رہن سے خارج ہو جائے گا پس رہن نہیں لوٹے گا مگر جدید عقد سے اگر راہن مر جائے مرتہن کی جانب لوٹانے سے پہلے تو مرتہن قرض خواہوں کے برابر ہو گا اس لئے کہ مرہون کے ساتھ ان تصرفات کے سبب سے حق لازم متعلق ہو گیا تو اس حق لازم کی وجہ سے رہن کا حکم باطل ہو گیا بہر حال عاریت کی وجہ سے مرہون کے ساتھ حق لازم متعلق نہیں ہوا پس یہ دونوں جدا جدا ہو گئے ۔
تشریح اگر راہن و مرتہن میں سے کسی ایک نے دوسرے کی اجازت سے کسی اجنبی کو مرہون فروخت کر دیا یا اجاره پردید یا یا ہبہ کردیا تواب مرہون رہن سے خارج ہو گیا لہذا اب اگر مرتہن کے پاس مرہون واپس بھی آجائے تب بھی محض قبضہ کی وجہ سے رہن نہیں ہوگا جب تک جدید عقد نہ کیا جائے۔
اس صورت میں اگر راہن نے ابھی مرہون مرتہن کو نہیں لوٹایا تھا کہ راہن مر گیا تو اب مرہون کا حقدار صرف مرتبہن ہی نہ ہوگا بلکہ دیگر قرض خواہوں کے ساتھ برابر کا شریک ہوگا اور حصہ رسد سب کو اس میں سے دیا جائے گا (جس کی تقسیم کا طریقہ ہم درس سراجی میں بیان کر چکے ہیں ) عاریت اور ان تصرفات میں فرق کرنے کی وجہ یہی ہے کہ ان تصرفات کی وجہ سے دوسروں کا حق لازم مرہون سے وابستہ ہو چکا ہے یعنی مشتری اور مستاجر اور موہوب لۂ کا حق لازم مرہون سے متعلق ہو چکا ہے اس وجہ سے رہن کو ختم کر دینا پڑا۔ اور عاریت کی وجہ سے مستغیر کا کوئی لازمی حق مرہون سے متعلق نہیں ہوا لہذا جب چاہیں مستعیر سے واپس لے سکتے ہیں۔
And this is contrary to ijarah, sale, and hibah from a stranger when one of them (mortgagee or pawnor) does it with the permission of the other, such that it (the pawn) leaves the pawn contract and does not return except by a new contract. And if the pawnor dies before returning it to the mortgagee, the mortgagee becomes equal to other creditors, because an irrevocable right has become attached to the pawn due to these transactions, so the ruling of pawn becomes invalid. As for ariyah, no irrevocable right becomes attached, so they are different.
Translation: And this (the issue of ariyah) is contrary to ijarah, sale, and hibah in the hands of a stranger when one of them does it with the permission of the other, in the sense that it leaves the pawn contract and does not return except by a new contract. If the pawnor dies before returning it to the mortgagee, the mortgagee becomes equal to other creditors, because an irrevocable right becomes attached to the pawn due to these transactions, so the ruling of the pawn becomes invalid. However, due to ariyah, no irrevocable right becomes attached, so these two are different.
Explanation: If either the pawnor or the mortgagee, with the permission of the other, sells, leases, or gives as a gift the pawned item to a stranger, then the pawn leaves the pawn contract. So even if the pawn returns to the mortgagee, it does not become a pawn without a new contract. In this case, if the pawnor dies before returning the pawn to the mortgagee, then the mortgagee does not have exclusive right to the pawn; rather, he becomes equal to other creditors, and the proceeds are distributed among them. The reason for the difference between ariyah and these transactions is that these transactions create an irrevocable right (haqq lazim) for others (buyer, lessee, donee) in the pawn, which necessitates the termination of the pawn. In ariyah, no such irrevocable right is created, so the pawn can be returned.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that distinguishes ariyah from sale (bay'), lease (ijarah), and gift (hibah) when performed on a pawned item with the permission of the other party. Unlike ariyah, these transactions transfer ownership or create lasting rights (e.g., ownership for buyer, usufruct for lessee, ownership for donee) that are irrevocable (haqq lazim). Therefore, the pawn contract is permanently terminated; the item cannot be returned to pawn status except by a new contract. A practical consequence: if the pawnor dies before the pawn is returned, the mortgagee loses his priority over other creditors and must share the pawn's proceeds equally. In contrast, ariyah creates no such permanent right, so the pawn can be reinstated simply by returning possession. This is a critical distinction in Hanafi pawn law.

Key Terms
حق لازم (haqq lazim): An irrevocable right; a right that is binding and cannot be unilaterally revoked.
رہن (حکم الرہن) (hukm al-rahn): The legal ruling of the pawn contract, i.e., the security relationship.
اسوة للغرماء (uswat lil-ghurama): Equal to the creditors; the mortgagee loses his priority and shares proportionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The pawn contract ends permanently and can only be revived with a new contract.
C) The pawn contract is temporarily suspended until the pawn is returned.
D) The pawn contract becomes a partnership between the mortgagee and the buyer.

Key Takeaway
Sale, lease, and gift of a pawn with permission create an irrevocable right that permanently terminates the pawn contract; ariyah does not.

Liability When Mortgagee Borrows Pawn for Work: The Three Timelines
Ruling on liability when mortgagee borrows pawn for work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three temporal scenarios for destruction of a pawn borrowed by the mortgagee and apply the ruling on liability in each.

Core Idea
A pawn borrowed for work temporarily loses its security status during use, shifting liability.

The mortgagee holds the pawn as security (yad al-rahn), but if he borrows it from the pawnor to use it, he holds it also as a borrower (yad al-ariyah). These two forms of possession are contradictory; they cannot coexist. The Hanafi school resolves this by distinguishing three timeframes: before work, during work, and after work. This lesson unpacks each scenario and its liability consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three timeframes
The passage divides destruction into three moments: before starting work, during work, and after finishing work. Recognize each case.
The 'work' is the specific purpose for which the mortgagee borrowed the pawn.
2
Determine the applicable hand (yad) in each timeframe
Before work: yad al-rahn (pawn hand) continues. During work: yad al-ariyah (borrower's trust hand) applies. After work: yad al-rahn returns as the ariyah hand ceases.
Yad al-rahn carries liability of security; yad al-ariyah is a trust without liability for accidental destruction.
3
Apply the liability ruling to each timeframe
Before work and after work: the pawn is destroyed under the liability of the pawn (i.e., the debt is affected, and the mortgagee bears no separate loss). During work: the pawn is destroyed without liability; the debt remains unchanged, and the mortgagee does not compensate.
The rationale is that contradictory hands cannot coexist; ariyah requires exiting the security status.
4
Identify the legal principle at work
The key principle is 'mutanaafiyayn' (contradictories cannot coexist). The possession as pawn and as borrower are contradictory, so the ariyah hand temporarily overrides the pawn hand during use.
This is a unique Hanafi refinement showing precise temporal analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا استعار المرتهن الرهن من الراهن ليعمل به فهلک قبل ان ياخذ فى العمل هلک علی ضمان الرهن لبقاء يد الرهن وکذا اذا هلك بعد الفراغ من العمل لارتفارع يد العارية ولو هلک فی حالة العمل هلک ضمان لثبوت يد العارية بالاستعمال وهى مخالفة ليد الرهن فانتفى الضمان
ترجمہ اور جب مرتہن نے مرہون کو راہن سے عاریت لیا تا کہ اس سے کام کرے پس مرہون کام میں لگنے سے پہلے ہی ہلاک ہو گیا تو منمان رہن پر ہلاک ہو گا ر ہن کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ کام سے فراغت کے بعد ہلاک ہوا ہو عاریت کے قبضہ کے ختم ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ کام سے فراغت کے بعد ہلاک ہوا ہو تو بغیر ضمان کے ہلاک ہو گا عاریت کے قبضہ کے ثبوت کی وجہ سے استعمال کے ذریعہ اور یہ قبضہ عاریت ) قبضہ کے مخالف ہے تو ضمان منتفی ہو گیا۔
تشریح مرتہن نے راہن سے مرہون کچھ کام کرنے کیلئے مستعار لیا اور وہ ہلاک ہوگیا تو اب تین صورتیں نہیں دوصورتوں میں ضمان واجب ہے اور ایک میں نہیں ہے۔ ۲۱- کام شروع کرنے سے پہلے ہی مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا یا کام کر کے فارغ ہو گیا اب مرہون ہلاک ہوا تو ان دونوں صوتوں میں رہن کا حکم اس پر جاری اور ہلاکت مضمون بالدین ہوگی۔ اول صورت میں تو اس لئے کہ ابھی قبضہ رہن باقی ہے اور دوسری صورت میں اس لئے کہ اب قبضہ عاریت ختم ہو کر قبضہ رہن آچکا ہے۔
عین استعمال کے وقت ہلاک ہو جائے تو اب ضمان نہیں ہوگا اور قرض بدستور باقی رہے گا کیونکہ استعمال قبضہ عاریت کی وجہ سے اور قبضہ عاریت میں داخل کرنے کے لئے قبضہ ضمانت سے خروج ضروری ہے ورنہ اجتماع متنافیین لازم آئے گا اور عاربیت میں بدون تعدی ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔
And when the mortgagee borrows the pawn from the pawnor to work with it, and it is destroyed before he begins work, it is destroyed under the liability of the pawn due to the continuation of the pawn's hand. Similarly, if it is destroyed after finishing work, because the ariyah hand has ceased. And if it is destroyed during the state of work, it is destroyed without liability due to the establishment of the ariyah hand through use, and it is contrary to the pawn hand, so liability is negated.
Translation: And when the mortgagee borrows the pawn from the pawnor to work with it, and the pawn is destroyed before starting the work, then it is destroyed under the liability of the pawn (i.e., the debt is secured by it) due to the continuation of the pawn hand. Similarly, if it is destroyed after finishing the work, because the ariyah hand has ceased. And if it is destroyed during the work state, it is destroyed without liability due to the establishment of the ariyah hand through use, and it contradicts the pawn hand, so liability is negated.
Explanation: The mortgagee borrowed the pawn from the pawnor for some work, and it was destroyed. There are three scenarios: in two, liability applies; in one, it does not. (1) Before starting work or after finishing work: in both, the ruling of pawn continues, and the destruction is covered by the debt (i.e., the pawn's value reduces the debt or the debt remains secured). In the first, because the pawn hand still exists; in the second, because the ariyah hand has ended and the pawn hand has returned. (2) During the actual use: then there is no liability (i.e., the pawn is not considered security at that moment), and the debt remains as before. Because the use establishes an ariyah hand, and for the ariyah hand to come into effect, it must exit from the dhaman hand; otherwise, contradictory elements would combine. And in ariyah, without transgression, liability is not incurred.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario when the mortgagee (murtahin) borrows the pawned item from the pawnor (rahin) for a specific purpose, such as using it. The ruling distinguishes three timeframes for destruction. Before any work begins, the pawn remains under the mortgagee's possession as a pawn (security), so if destroyed, it is considered 'destroyed under the liability of the pawn' meaning the mortgagee's debt is affected (the pawn's value reduces the debt or the mortgagee is not liable beyond that). After the work is finished, the same rule applies because the ariyah (borrowing) hand has ended and the pawn hand is re-established. However, during the actual work, the pawn is considered to be in the mortgagee's hand as a borrower (ariyah), which is a trust possession; therefore, if destroyed accidentally, there is no liability on the mortgagee, and the debt remains intact. The rationale is that the ariyah hand contradicts the pawn hand; to have ariyah, the item must exit the security status temporarily. This is a refined ruling showing how different types of possession interact in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
ید الرهن (yad al-rahn): The hand/possession of pawn; a possession that carries the attribute of security (dhaman) for the debt.
ید العاریة (yad al-ariyah): Possession as a borrower; a trust hand (yad amanah) that does not carry liability for accidental destruction.
متنافیین (mutanaafiyayn): Two contradictory elements that cannot coexist; here, the pawn hand (security) and ariyah hand (trust) cannot apply simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee borrows the pawn from the pawnor and it is destroyed while he is using it for the intended work, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt is reduced by the value of the pawn.
B) The debt is canceled.
C) The debt remains intact, and no one is liable for the destruction.
D) The mortgagee must compensate the pawnor.

Key Takeaway
A pawn borrowed for work temporarily sheds its security status during actual use, absolving the mortgagee of liability for accidental destruction.
