⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرہون کو کوئی عیب پہنچا تو اسی حساب سے قرض ساقط ہوگا و کذالک ان اصابه عيب ذهب من الدين بحسابه ووجب مثله لرب الثوب على الراهن على مابيناه وان كانت قيمته اقل من الدين ذهب بقدر القيمة وعلى الراهن بقية دينه للمرتهن لانه لم يقع الاستيفاء بالزيادة على قيمته وعلى الراهن لصاحب الثوب ماصار به موفيا لما بيناه ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر مر ہون کو کوئی عیب پہنچا ہو تو اس کے حساب سے قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا اور راہن کے اوپر کپڑے والے (معیر ) کے لئے اس کے مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر مرہون کی قیمت قرض سے کم ہو تو قیمت کے بقدر قرض ختم ہو جائے گا اور راہن پر مرتین کا بقیہ قرض لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ قیمت سے زیادہ کی وصولیابی دافع نہیں ہوئی اور راہن پر کپڑے والے کے لئے وہ مقدار واجب ہوگی جس مقدار کے ذریعہ وہ قرض کو ادا کرنے والا ہوا ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح اگر مرتہن کے پاس کمبل میں کچھ عیب پیدا ہو گیا مثلا تھا پانچ سوروپے اور اتناہی مثلا مرتین کا قرض ہے اب مرتہن کے پاس کمبل آگ لگنے کی وجہ سے اس میں عیب پیدا ہو گیا جس کی وجہ سے اب اس کی قیمت تین سو روپے رہ گئی تو اسی حساب سے قرض بھی ساقط ہو گا یعنی اب مرتہن کے قرض میں سے دو سوروپے ساقط ہو گئے اور صرف تین سوروپے باقی رہے تو مستغیر بھی معیر کو اتنی ہی رقم ادا کر یگا یعنی دوسو کیونکہ مستعبیر نے معیر کے کمبل سے اتنا ہی قرض ادا کیا ہے اور یہ بھی گذر چکا کہ مغیر کے مال سے جتنا قرض وہ ادا کر لگا اتنا ہی ممان مستعغیر پر واجب ہوگا۔ یہ گفتگو تو جب ہے جبکہ کمبل کی قیمت قرض کے برابر یا قرض سے زیادہ ہو اور اگر کم ہومثلا یہ قرض پانچ سوروپے ہے اور میل کی قیمت مورد پے ہے اور کمبل مرتہن کے پاس بلاک ہو جائے تو مرتہن کے قرض میں سے صرف سوروپے ساقط ہوئے باقی چارسورا ہن کے ذمہ باقی ہیں تو اس صورت میں مستغیر مغیر کو صرف سوروپے دے گا کیونکہ مستعمیر نے معیر کے مال سے اتنا ہی قرض ادا کیا ہے۔
Similarly, if the pledged item suffers a defect, the debt reduces proportionally, and the equivalent becomes due to the owner of the garment (mu'ir) from the rahin, according to what we have explained. And if its value is less than the debt, the debt extinguishes to the extent of the value, and the remaining debt of the murtahin remains due from the rahin, because recovery beyond the value did not occur, and the mu'ir is entitled to that amount from the rahin by which he became a repayer, for the reason we have explained. Explanation: If the blanket at the murtahin's develops a defect—for example, it was worth five hundred rupees and the murtahin's debt was also five hundred—and due to fire, the blanket's value drops to three hundred, then the debt reduces proportionally: two hundred of the debt is extinguished, leaving three hundred. The musta'ir will give that same amount to the mu'ir, i.e., two hundred, because the musta'ir has paid off that much debt with the mu'ir's blanket. This is when the blanket's value equals or exceeds the debt. If it is less, e.g., debt five hundred, blanket value one hundred, and it is destroyed, then only one hundred of the debt is extinguished, remaining four hundred on the rahin. The musta'ir gives only one hundred to the mu'ir.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling from total destruction to partial damage of the pledged borrowed item. The principle is that any reduction in value due to a defect results in a proportional reduction of the debt. The rahin remains liable to the murtahin for the remaining debt, but must also compensate the mu'ir for the amount by which the debt was effectively paid using his property. The author provides a numerical example: a blanket worth 500 with a 500 debt; after fire damage, it becomes worth 300, so the debt reduces to 300 (200 extinguished). The musta'ir (borrower) owes the mu'ir 200. If the blanket's value is only 100, only 100 of the debt is extinguished, and the musta'ir owes the mu'ir 100. This illustrates the proportional nature of the rule.

Key Terms
عیب ('aib): A defect or damage that reduces the value of the pledged item.
قیمت (qimat): The market value of the pledged item at the time of the damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a borrowed blanket pledged for a debt of 300 rupees is damaged and its value drops to 200 rupees, what is the amount of debt that is extinguished?
A) 300 rupees
B) 200 rupees
C) 100 rupees
D) None

Key Takeaway
The debt reduces proportionally to the loss in value; the rahin compensates the mu'ir for that amount.

The Mu'ir's Right to Redeem the Pledge
Ruling on redemption by the original owner of the pledge when the pledgor cannot pay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the mu'ir's redemption of a pledge when the rahin is insolvent, and distinguish between a mu'ir and a stranger in terms of the murtahin's compulsion.

Core Idea
The murtahin must accept redemption only if the payer is not a volunteer (mutabarri').

This lesson addresses a practical scenario in the contract of pledge (rahn): the pledgor (rahin) is insolvent and cannot redeem the pledge. The original owner of the pledged item (mu'ir) steps in to pay the debt and recover his property. The key question is whether the lender (murtahin) can refuse. The Hanafi ruling, grounded in the concept of voluntariness (tabarru'), provides a clear answer and distinguishes the mu'ir from a stranger. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the correct legal consequences in similar transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
What is the legal ruling when the mu'ir wants to redeem the pledge? State that the murtahin cannot refuse and must hand over the pledge once paid.
2
Recognize the Condition
Note the condition: the rahin is insolvent and the value of the pledge equals the debt. Why is this condition important? It sets the stage for the mu'ir's intervention.
If the rahin could pay himself, the mu'ir would have no standing.
3
Understand the Key Principle
The principle is that compulsion on the murtahin depends on whether the payer is a volunteer (mutabarri') or not. A volunteer has no personal stake, so the murtahin can refuse.
The word 'mutabarri' comes from tabarru' (voluntary charity).
4
Apply the Principle to Mu'ir vs. Stranger
The mu'ir is not a volunteer because he is reclaiming his own property. A stranger is a volunteer because he has no ownership interest. Therefore, the murtahin is compelled to accept from the mu'ir but not from a stranger.
5
Identify the Consequence for the Mu'ir
After paying, the mu'ir has recourse against the rahin for the amount paid. This further shows he is not a volunteer, as he expects reimbursement.
This recourse is evidence that he is not acting out of pure charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن غریب ہو جو مر ہون کو چھڑانے سے عاجز اور مجبور ہو تو کیا ہے؟ ولو كانت قيمته مثل الدين فاراد المعيران يفتكه جبر اعن الراهن لم يكن للمرتهن اذا قضى دينه ان يمتنع لانه غير متبرع حيث يخلص ملكه ولهذا يرجع على الراهن بما ادى فاجبر المرتهن على الدفع بخلاف الاجنبي اذا قضى الدين لانه متبرع اذهو لا يسعى فى تخليص ملكه ولا في تفريغ ذمته فكان للطالب ان لا يقبله ترجمہ اور اگر مستعار مرہون کی قیمت قرض کے برابر ہو پس راہن کی تنگدستی کی وجہ سے معیر نے مرہون کو چھڑانا چاہا تو مرتہن کو منع کرنے کا حق نہیں ہے جبکہ اس کا قرض ادا کر دیا جائے اس لئے کہ معیر تبرع کرنے والا نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ اپنی ملک چھڑا رہا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے ادا کی ہوئی مقدار را بہن سے واپس لیگا تو مرتہن کو دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا بخلاف اجنبی کے جبکہ وہ قرض ادا کردے اس لئے کہ اجنبی تتبرع کرنے والا ہے اس سے کہ اجنبی اپنی ملک چھڑانے میں سعی نہیں کر رہا ہے اور نہ اپنے ذمہ کو فارغ کرنے میں تو طالب ( مرتہن ) کو حق ہوگا کہ اس کی ادائیگی کو قبول نہ کرے۔ تشریح را من غریب ہے جو مر ہون کو چھڑانے سے معذور و مجبور ہے معیر نے خود قرض ادا کر کے اپنا کمبل مرتبین کے پاس سے چھڑانا چاہا تو مرتین کو یہ حق نہیں کہ وہ انکار کر دے لہذا اس پر جبر کیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ اگر اس کام کو متبرع کرے تو مرتہن پر جبر نہیں ہوگا اور اگر ادا کرنے والا متبرع نہ ہو تو جبر ہوگا اب ہم نے غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ معیر اب تبرع نہیں ہے یعنی اگر چہ وہ عاریت دینے میں متبرع تھا لیکن چھڑانے میں تبرع نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ اپنا مال چھڑا رہا ہے اور متبرع شہونے کی یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ اس قرض کو معیر راہن سے واپس لیتا ہے۔
And if the value of the borrowed (pledged) item equals the debt, and the mu'ir wishes to redeem it due to the rahin's insolvency, the murtahin does not have the right to refuse when his debt is paid, because the mu'ir is not a volunteer (mutabarri') as he is reclaiming his own property. Hence he recovers what he paid from the rahin, and the murtahin is compelled to hand it over, unlike a stranger (ajnabi) who pays the debt, because the stranger is a volunteer, as he is not striving to reclaim his own property nor to free his own liability, so the claimant (murtahin) has the right not to accept his payment. Explanation: The rahin is insolvent and unable to redeem. The mu'ir wants to pay the debt and take his blanket from the murtahin. The murtahin does not have the right to refuse, so he is compelled. The principle is: if the payer is a volunteer, the murtahin is not compelled; if he is not a volunteer, he is compelled. Here, the mu'ir is not a volunteer, even though he was a volunteer in lending, but in redeeming he is not; rather, he is reclaiming his property. And evidence of his not being a volunteer is that he takes back this debt from the rahin.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage addresses a situation where the pledgor (rahin) is insolvent and cannot redeem the pledged item. The lender of the borrowed item (mu'ir) steps in to pay the debt and recover his property. The key ruling is that the murtahin cannot refuse the mu'ir's payment because the mu'ir is not acting as a volunteer (mutabarri')—he is protecting his own ownership rights. This is contrasted with a stranger who pays the debt: the stranger is a volunteer, and the murtahin may refuse his payment because the stranger has no personal interest. The mu'ir will then have recourse against the rahin for the amount he paid. The author emphasizes the principle: compulsion on the murtahin applies only when the payer is not a volunteer. The mu'ir, though he voluntarily lent the item, does not voluntarily redeem it; he does so to reclaim his property, which is a right, not a charity.

Key Terms
متبرع (mutabarri'): A volunteer who acts without any personal interest, doing a charitable act.
جبر (jabr): Legal compulsion; here, the court can compel the murtahin to hand over the pledge to the mu'ir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the mu'ir (lender of the borrowed item) compel the murtahin to accept his payment and release the pledge, while a stranger cannot?
A) Because the mu'ir is the original owner of the pledged item.
B) Because the mu'ir is not a volunteer (mutabarri') and is reclaiming his property.
C) Because the mu'ir is more trustworthy than a stranger.
D) Because the mu'ir's debt is senior to others.

Key Takeaway
The murtahin can be compelled to accept redemption only when the payer is not a volunteer; the mu'ir redeems to reclaim his own property, so he is not a volunteer and the murtahin must accept.

Debt Reduction upon Diminution of Pawn Value
Explains proportional debt reduction when pawn value drops.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a pawn's depreciation proportionally extinguishes the debt, distinguishing between cases where the pawn value equals/exceeds the debt and where it is less.

Core Idea
A pawn's value drop proportionally reduces the debt; only the actual value is applied.

When a pawned item held by the creditor suffers a defect or is destroyed, its reduced value does not leave the debt untouched. Instead, the debt automatically decreases to match the diminished worth. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on this proportional reduction and its implications when the pawner had borrowed the item from a third party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Extract the legal consequence: the debt is extinguished only to the extent of the pawn's current value after the defect/destruction.
Not the original value, but the value at the time of the event.
2
Distinguish two scenarios
Compare when the pawn's value equals or exceeds the debt versus when it is less. In the first, the debt reduces fully to the new value; in the second, only the reduced value is extinguished.
The remaining debt is still owed by the rahin.
3
Incorporate the borrowed-pawn scenario
If the pawner (musta'ir) had borrowed the item from a lender (mu'ir), the musta'ir must pay the mu'ir an amount equal to the debt reduction achieved using that item.
This is because the mu'ir's property was used to discharge the debt.
4
Trace the rationale
Understand the underlying principle: the pawn serves as a collateral up to its value; any excess debt is still the responsibility of the rahin. The musta'ir's liability mirrors the benefit he derived from the mu'ir's item.
The text says 'due to the proof we have stated' – reference to earlier discussion on liability.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴ بقدر قرض ختم ہو جائے گا اور راہن پر مرتین کا بقیہ قرض لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ قیمت سے زیادہ کی وصولیابی دافع نہیں ہوئی اور راہن پر کپڑے والے کے لئے وہ مقدار واجب ہوگی جس مقدار کے ذریعہ وہ قرض کو ادا کرنے والا ہوا ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح اگر مرتہن کے پاس کمبل میں کچھ عیب پیدا ہو گیا مثلا تھا پانچ سوروپے اور اتناہی مثلا مرتین کا قرض ہے اب مرتہن کے پاس کمبل آگ لگنے کی وجہ سے اس میں عیب پیدا ہو گیا جس کی وجہ سے اب اس کی قیمت تین سو روپے رہ گئی تو اسی حساب سے قرض بھی ساقط ہو گا یعنی اب مرتہن کے قرض میں سے دو سوروپے ساقط ہو گئے اور صرف تین سوروپے باقی رہے تو مستغیر بھی معیر کو اتنی ہی رقم ادا کر یگا یعنی دوسو کیونکہ مستعبیر نے معیر کے کمبل سے اتنا ہی قرض ادا کیا ہے اور یہ بھی گذر چکا کہ مغیر کے مال سے جتنا قرض وہ ادا کر لگا اتنا ہی ممان مستعغیر پر واجب ہوگا۔

Book of Pledge. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 14. It will be extinguished to the extent of the debt, and the remaining debt of the pledgee will be binding on the pledger, because recovery exceeding the value is not a prevention, and the amount by which he repaid the debt will be obligatory on the pledger for the cloth-owner, due to the proof we have stated. Explanation: If a defect occurs in the blanket with the pledgee, e.g., it was worth five hundred rupees and the pledgee's debt is equal, then due to fire the blanket's value drops to three hundred rupees, then the debt reduces proportionally: two hundred rupees are extinguished, three hundred remain. The borrower (musta'ir) will pay the lender (mu'ir) two hundred rupees because he repaid that much debt using the lender's blanket. This rule applies when the blanket's value equals or exceeds the debt. If the value is less, e.g., debt is five hundred, blanket value three hundred, and it is destroyed, then only three hundred are extinguished; the borrower pays the lender three hundred.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on what happens when a pawned item (marhun) held by the pledgee (murtahin) decreases in value due to a defect or destruction, and the pawner (rahin) had borrowed it from a lender (mu'ir). The key point: the debt reduces proportionally to the decrease in value. For example, if the pawn was worth 500 rupees and the debt is 500, and the pawn is damaged so its value drops to 300, then 200 of the debt is extinguished. The borrower (musta'ir) must pay the lender 200 rupees because he used the lender's property to repay that much debt. If the pawn's value is less than the debt, only the actual value is extinguished, and the borrower pays that amount to the lender. The reasoning is that the borrower only repaid the debt to the extent of the pawn's value.

Key Terms
مرهون (marhun): The item given as pledge/pawn.
مرتہن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pawn.
راہن (rahin): The debtor who gives the pawn.
معیر (mu'ir): The lender of an item that was then pawned by the borrower.
مستعیر (musta'ir): The borrower of an item who then pawns it to a third party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 0
B) 200
C) 300
D) 500

Key Takeaway
The debt reduces proportionally to the current value of the pawn; the musta'ir must compensate the mu'ir for the amount of debt discharged using the borrowed item.

Mu'ir Redeeming the Pawn When the Pledgor is Insolvent
Ruling with rational proof distinguishing mu'ir from ajnabi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a mu'ir who redeems the pawn is not mutabarri', so the murtahin is compelled to accept, and distinguish this from an ajnabi who is mutabarri' and may be refused.

Core Idea
The mu'ir who redeems the pawn recovers his property, making him non-mutabarri' and compelling the pledgee to accept.

In this passage, the author explains the special position of the mu'ir (the original owner who lent the item that was pawned). When the rahin is insolvent, the mu'ir may step in to pay the debt and reclaim his property. The pledgee cannot refuse because the mu'ir is not acting gratuitously. An outsider, however, is a volunteer and may be refused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The mu'ir pays the debt to redeem the pawn when the rahin is insolvent. The ruling: the murtahin must accept the payment and hand over the pawn; he has no right to refuse.
The act is valid and enforceable.
2
Understand tabarru' and its effect
Tabarru' is a voluntary, gratuitous act. A mutabarri' (volunteer) cannot compel the beneficiary to accept. The mu'ir is not mutabarri' because he reclaims his own property.
This is the key distinction.
3
Analyze the proof
The mu'ir will recover the amount paid from the rahin, proving his act is not gratuitous. This rational inference (dalil aqli) establishes that he is not mutabarri'.
The proof is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Contrast with the ajnabi
An outsider (ajnabi) pays the debt with no personal interest; he is mutabarri'. Therefore, the murtahin may refuse his payment.
The difference hinges on intent and recourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن غریب ہو جو مر ہون کو چھڑانے سے عاجز اور مجبور ہو تو کیا ہے؟
ولو كانت قيمته مثل الدين فاراد المعيران يفتكه جبر اعن الراهن لم يكن للمرتهن اذا قضى دينه ان يمتنع لانه غير متبرع حيث يخلص ملكه ولهذا يرجع على الراهن بما ادى فاجبر المرتهن على الدفع بخلاف الاجنبي اذا قضى الدين لانه متبرع اذهو لا يسعى فى تخليص ملكه ولا في تفريغ ذمته فكان للطالب ان لا يقبله
ترجمہ اور اگر مستعار مرہون کی قیمت قرض کے برابر ہو پس راہن کی تنگدستی کی وجہ سے معیر نے مرہون کو چھڑانا چاہا تو مرتہن کو منع کرنے کا حق نہیں ہے جبکہ اس کا قرض ادا کر دیا جائے اس لئے کہ معیر تبرع کرنے والا نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ اپنی ملک چھڑا رہا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے ادا کی ہوئی مقدار را بہن سے واپس لیگا تو مرتہن کو دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا بخلاف اجنبی کے جبکہ وہ قرض ادا کردے اس لئے کہ اجنبی تتبرع کرنے والا ہے اس سے کہ اجنبی اپنی ملک چھڑانے میں سعی نہیں کر رہا ہے اور نہ اپنے ذمہ کو فارغ کرنے میں تو طالب ( مرتہن ) کو حق ہوگا کہ اس کی ادائیگی کو قبول نہ کرے۔
تشریح را من غریب ہے جو مر ہون کو چھڑانے سے معذور و مجبور ہے معیر نے خود قرض ادا کر کے اپنا کمبل مرتبین کے پاس سے چھڑانا چاہا تو مرتین کو یہ حق نہیں کہ وہ انکار کر دے لہذا اس پر جبر کیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ اگر اس کام کو متبرع کرے تو مرتہن پر جبر نہیں ہوگا اور اگر ادا کرنے والا متبرع نہ ہو تو جبر ہوگا اب ہم نے غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ معیر اب تبرع نہیں ہے یعنی اگر چہ وہ عاریت دینے میں متبرع تھا لیکن چھڑانے میں تبرع نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ اپنا مال چھڑا رہا ہے اور متبرع شہونے کی یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ اس قرض کو معیر راہن سے واپس لیتا ہے۔
اگر کوئی اجنبی اس کام کو کرنے لگے یعنی راہن کا قرض ادا کر کے مرہون کو چھڑائے تو یہاں مرتہن کو دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ متبرع ہے اور متبرع ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجنبی کا مقصد نہ اپنی ملک کو چھڑانا ہے اور نہ اپنے اوپر سے قرض کو ادا کرتا ہے۔ تنبیه جبرا عن الراهن یہ عبارت اس کتاب کے مغلقات میں سے ہے۔ امام محمد نے بجائے اس کے یہ عبارت ارشاد فرمائی ہے حسین اعسر الراهن شمس الائمہ سمری فخر الاسلام بزدوی وغیرہ نے ایسا ہی ذکر کیا ہے اس لئے بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ جبرا عن الراهن کاتب یا قاری کی غلطی ہے اور بعض حضرات نے اس کی تفسیر بغیر رضاہ کے ساتھ کی ہے تفصیل کے لئے دیکھئے۔ (نتائج الافکار )
What if the pledger is insolvent, unable to redeem the pawn? And if its value equals the debt and the lender (mu'ir) wants to redeem it by compelling the pledger, the pledgee may not refuse when his debt is paid, because the lender is not a volunteer (mutabarri') since he is recovering his property. Therefore he takes back from the pledger what he paid, so the pledgee is compelled to hand over, unlike an outsider (ajnabi) who if he pays the debt, the pledgee is not compelled because the outsider is a volunteer, as he is not seeking to recover his own property nor to free his own liability, so the claimant (pledgee) may refuse to accept. Explanation: If the pledger is insolvent and the lender wants to redeem his blanket by paying the debt, the pledgee has no right to refuse; he is compelled. The principle: if the payer is a volunteer, the pledgee is not compelled; if not a volunteer, he is compelled. The lender is not a volunteer because he is recovering his own property, as evidenced by the fact that he recovers the amount from the pledger. If an outsider does this, the pledgee is not compelled because the outsider is a volunteer, since his aim is not to recover his own property nor to free his own liability. Note: The phrase 'jabran 'an al-rahin' (compelling the pledger) is among the obscure phrases of this book. Imam Muhammad said instead 'husayn a'sar al-rahin' [؟]; scholars like Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi mentioned similarly. Some say it is a scribal error; others interpret it as 'without his consent'. For details see Nata'ij al-Afkar.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where the pawner (rahin) is insolvent and unable to redeem the pawn. The lender (mu'ir) who originally lent the item that was pawned may step in to pay the debt and recover his property. In this case, the pledgee (murtahin) is compelled to accept the payment and return the pawn, because the mu'ir is not acting gratuitously (tabarru')—he is protecting his own property. The proof is that he will claim the amount back from the rahin. Conversely, if an outsider (ajnabi) pays the debt, the pledgee may refuse, because the outsider is a volunteer doing a favor, with no personal interest. The note clarifies a textual issue in Hidayah regarding the phrase 'jabran 'an al-rahin', suggesting possible corruption or alternative interpretation.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary, gratuitous act without expectation of return.
اجنبي (ajnabi): A third party not connected to the pawn or debt.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion applied by the court to force the murtahin to accept payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the mu'ir (lender) considered not mutabarri' when redeeming the pawn?
A) Because he is the original owner of the pawn.
B) Because he expects a reward.
C) Because he will take back the amount from the rahin.
D) Because he is a relative of the rahin.

Key Takeaway
The mu'ir's redemption is not a donation, so the pledgee must accept; an outsider's payment is a donation and may be refused.

No Liability for Borrowed Cloth Before Pledge or After Redemption
States absence of liability for borrowed item destroyed before pledge or after redemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no liability (daman) falls on the rahin when a borrowed item is destroyed before the pledge or after redemption, and explain why the cause of liability (using the item to repay debt) is absent.

Core Idea
Liability on the rahin arises only if the borrowed item was used to repay the pledge debt; otherwise, no daman.

In the previous lesson, we learned that the rahin becomes liable for a borrowed item when it is destroyed while in pledge because he benefits by discharging his debt. But if the item is destroyed before he hands it over as collateral or after he redeems it, the benefit is absent. This lesson establishes that in those two scenarios, the rahin bears no liability, as the operative cause (illah) is missing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
There are two scenarios: (a) the borrowed item is destroyed while still with the rahin before he pawns it to the murtahin; (b) it is destroyed after he redeems it from the pledge but before returning it to the owner (mu'ir).
In both, the item is not being used to secure the debt at the moment of destruction.
2
Recall the general principle for destruction while in pledge
Earlier in the chapter, it was established that if the borrowed item is destroyed while in the possession of the murtahin (pledgee) or while with the rahin after pawning, the rahin is liable because he benefits by repaying his debt through the item's value.
The cause of liability (wajib al-daman) is the benefit of using the item to discharge the debt.
3
Apply the cause to the two scenarios
In both scenarios, the rahin has not yet used the item to repay his debt (before pledge) or has already redeemed and thus no longer benefits from the pledge (after redemption). Therefore, the cause of liability is absent.
The absence of the cause negates the ruling.
4
State the ruling
Hence, there is no liability (damn) on the rahin for the destruction in these two cases.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
5
Contrast with destruction while in pledge
If the destruction occurs while the item is in pledge, the rahin is liable. This contrast shows that the ruling is conditional on the benefit of debt repayment.
The practical implication: timing matters for determining liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستعار کپڑا راہن کے پاس رہن رکھنے سے پہلے یار ہن چھڑانے کے بعد ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضمان ہے یا نہیں
ولو هلك الثوب العارية عند الراهن قبل ان يرهنه او بعد ما افتكه فلاضمان عليه لانه لا يصير قاضيا بهذا وهو الموجب على ما بيناه
ترجمہ اور اگر مستعار کپڑا راہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا رہن رکھنے سے پہلے یا اس کو چھڑانے کے بعد تو را ہن پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ را ہن اس سے اپنے قرض کو ادا کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور عمان کا موجب یہی ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح مستغیر نے معیر سے جو کمیل عاریت لیا ہے اگر وہ راہن کے پاس رہن دینے سے پہلے یا رہن کو چھڑانے کے بعد ہلاک ہو جائے تو چونکہ راہن نے اس کمبل سے اپنا قرض ادا نہیں کیا اس لئے راہن پر اس کا ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور ضمان کا سبب اس سے قرض کی ادائیگی تھی جو نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔ معیر اور مستغیر ، میں یا رہن سے پہلے یا رہن چھڑانے کے بعد اختلاف ہو تو کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا ولو اختلفا في ذالك فالقول للراهن لانه ينكر الايفاء بدعواه الهلاك في هاتين الحالتين
ترجمہ اور اگر معیر اور مستعغیر دونوں اس میں اختلاف کریں تو راہن کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ راہن قرض کی ادائیگی کا منکر ہے ان دونوں حالتوں میں اپنے دعوی ہلاک کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح یعنی اگر معیر اور مستغیر میں اختلاف ہو جائے معیر کہتا ہے کہ مستعار بوقت رہن لہلاک ہوا ہے اور مستغیر کہتا ہے کہ رہن سے پہلے یا رہن چھڑانے کے بعد ہلاک ہوا ہے تو راہن کا قول معتبر ہوگا لیکن اگر معیر گواہ پیش کر دے تو پھر معیر کا قول معتبر ہوگا ۔ مستعیر کا قول کیوں معتبر ہے؟
اس لئے کہ معیر دعویٰ کرتا ہے کہ راہن کے ذمہ پر حق لازم آتا ہے اور مستغیر اس سے منکر ہے اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے اس لئے مستعغیر کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
If the borrowed cloth is destroyed with the rahin before he pawns it or after he redeems it, is there liability? And if the borrowed cloth is destroyed with the rahin before he pawns it or after he redeems it, then no liability on him, because he does not become a repayer of debt through it, and that is the cause of liability as we have explained. Explanation: The musta'ir borrowed a blanket from the mu'ir; if it is destroyed while with the rahin before pawning or after redeeming, since the rahin did not repay his debt through this blanket, no liability is owed. The cause of liability was debt repayment, which is absent. And if the mu'ir and musta'ir dispute regarding this, then the word of the rahin is accepted because he denies the repayment, claiming destruction in these two states. Explanation: If the mu'ir and musta'ir differ—mu'ir says the borrowed item was destroyed at the time of the pledge, and musta'ir says it was destroyed before the pledge or after redemption—then the rahin's word is accepted. But if the mu'ir brings witnesses, his word prevails. Why is musta'ir's word accepted? Because mu'ir claims that a right is due on the rahin, and musta'ir denies it, and the word of the denier is accepted.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage covers two sub-rulings: (1) If the borrowed item (musta'ar) is destroyed while in the possession of the rahin (who borrowed it from mu'ir) either before he pawns it to a third party or after he redeems it from the pledge, then no liability (daman) falls on the rahin. The reason is that liability in this context arose only from the rahin using the item to repay his debt to the murtahin. Since that repayment did not occur in these two scenarios, there is no cause for liability. (2) If there is a dispute between mu'ir and musta'ir about the timing of destruction, the rahin's word is accepted because he is denying any liability, and the principle is that the word of the denier is believed (with an oath). The mu'ir can only prevail with witnesses.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.
مستعار (musta'ar): The item given as a loan for use ('ariyah).
عارية (ariyah): Loan for use, where the item is returned after use.
موجب الضمان (mujib al-daman): The cause that makes liability obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the rahin NOT liable for the destruction of a borrowed item in the context of rahn?
A) When the item is destroyed while in the hands of the murtahin.
B) When the item is destroyed before the pledge or after redemption.
C) When the item is destroyed due to the rahin's negligence.
D) When the item is destroyed during the pledge period.

Key Takeaway
The rahin's liability for a borrowed item in rahn depends on whether he used it to repay his debt; if destruction occurs before or after that use, there is no daman.

Dispute Between Mu'ir and Musta'ir: Whose Word is Accepted?
Procedural ruling on whose word is accepted in dispute over timing of destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi procedural rule that in a dispute over the timing of destruction of a borrowed item, the rahin's word is accepted (with oath) because he denies liability.

Core Idea
The rahin's word is taken in a dispute because he denies liability; the onus is on the claimant (mu'ir) to prove.

In the previous lesson, we learned that the rahin is not liable if the borrowed item is destroyed before pledge or after redemption. But what if the owner (mu'ir) claims the destruction happened during the pledge (making the rahin liable), while the rahin claims it happened before or after? Who is believed? This lesson explains that the rahin's word is accepted, as he is the denier, unless the mu'ir brings witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The mu'ir (lender) claims the borrowed item was destroyed while in pledge (so rahin liable). The musta'ir (borrower/rahin) claims it was destroyed before pledge or after redemption (so no liability).
This dispute over timing determines liability.
2
Determine who is claimant (mudda'i) and who is denier (munkir)
The mu'ir is claiming liability (affirmative claim), so he is the claimant. The rahin denies liability, so he is the denier.
In Hanafi procedure, the burden of proof is on the claimant; the denier's word is accepted with an oath.
3
Apply the procedural rule
Since the rahin is the denier, his word is accepted (with an oath) regarding the timing of destruction. Therefore, the ruling is that he is not liable.
The mu'ir can only overcome this by providing witnesses (bayyinah).
4
Note the exception
If the mu'ir brings two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses to prove that the destruction occurred during the pledge, then his claim prevails, and the rahin becomes liable.
The rule of bayyinah overrides the denier's oath.
5
Understand the rationale
The principle is: 'The claimant must prove; the denier must swear.' Here, the rahin denies any debt or liability, so his word is taken. Also, the default assumption is that no liability exists until proven.
This is a standard Hanafi procedural maxim.

Source Text

Key Terms
مدع (mudda'i): Claimant; the one who asserts a right or liability.
منكر (munkir): Denier; the one who denies the claim.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Stranger Redeeming the Pawn: Mortgagee Not Forced
Ruling: mortgagee not compelled when stranger redeems pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a stranger pays the pawner's debt and explain why the mortgagee is not forced to hand over the pawn.

Core Idea
A volunteer cannot compel the mortgagee to release the pawn.

In pawn transactions, only the debtor or his authorized agent can demand the pawn from the mortgagee. But what happens if a stranger steps in and offers to pay off the debt? This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a third-party redeemer, clarifying that the mortgagee may lawfully refuse because the stranger acts gratuitously.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what the stranger is doing (paying the pawner's debt and demanding the pawn) and the legal consequence: the mortgagee is not compelled to hand it over.
2
Locate the rational evidence (dalil aqli)
Find the evidence given in the text: the stranger's intention is neither to redeem his own property nor to discharge a personal debt, proving he is a volunteer.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the evidence supports the ruling: because the stranger has no legal right in the pawn and no personal obligation to pay, his action is voluntary, and a volunteer has no power to compel the mortgagee.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
Check whether other schools differ: the Hanafi position is clear; some may differ, but the ruling stands on established principle.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
Appreciate the logic: the mortgagee's right of retention is protected until payment by the debtor; a stranger's intervention does not create an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر کوئی اجنبی اس کام کو کرنے لگے یعنی راہن کا قرض ادا کر کے مرہون کو چھڑائے تو یہاں مرتہن کو دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ متبرع ہے اور متبرع ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجنبی کا مقصد نہ اپنی ملک کو چھڑانا ہے اور نہ اپنے اوپر سے قرض کو ادا کرتا ہے۔
If a stranger begins to do this work, i.e., pays off the pawner's debt and redeems the pawned item, then here the mortgagee will not be forced to give it because this is a volunteer (mutabarri'), and the evidence of being a volunteer is that the stranger's intention is neither to redeem his own property nor to pay off a debt from himself.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage states the ruling when a third party (ajnabī) intervenes to pay off the pawner's (rāhin) debt and redeem the pawned item (marhūn). The mortgagee (murtahin) is not compelled to hand over the pawn because the third party is acting as a volunteer (mutabarri'). In Hanafi law, a volunteer has no right to compel the mortgagee since he has no legal claim to the pawn nor any obligation to pay the debt. The evidence for his volunteer status is that his aim is neither to reclaim his own property nor to discharge a personal debt. Therefore, the mortgagee may lawfully refuse to release the pawn. This ruling is based on the general principle that the mortgagee's right to retain the pawn until payment of the debt is protected, and only the debtor or his authorized agent can compel release.

Key Terms
اجنبی (ajnabī): A stranger or third party not directly involved in the pawn transaction.
متبرع (mutabarri'): Volunteer; one who acts gratuitously without legal obligation.
راهن (rāhin): The pawner/debtor who pledges an item.
مرتهن (murtahin): The mortgagee/creditor who takes the pawn.
مرهون (marhūn): The pawned item.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a volunteer redeemer cannot compel the mortgagee to release the pawn; the mortgagee has the right to refuse.

Liability for Borrowed Cloth Destroyed Before or After Pawn
Ruling on destruction of borrowed cloth before or after pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a pawner is not liable for a borrowed item destroyed before pawning or after redemption, and explain the rationale based on the absence of the cause (sabab) of debt payment.

Core Idea
No liability on pawner for borrowed item unless used to pay the debt.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in pawn (rahn) transactions: a person borrows an item (e.g., a cloth) intending to pawn it to secure a debt. If the cloth is destroyed while in the pawner's possession either before he pawns it or after he redeems the pawn, the question arises whether the pawner is liable (daman) to the lender. The Hanafi school rules that no liability attaches in these two cases because the pawner did not apply the item toward satisfying his debt, which is the very cause of liability. Understanding this principle clarifies the boundaries of responsibility in pawn arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage: a borrowed cloth perishes with the pawner before pawn or after redemption. The ruling is that there is no liability (la daman) on the pawner.
Two distinct timings: before pawning and after redemption.
2
Understand the cause (sabab) of liability in pawn
Liabillity in pawn arises from using the pawned item to pay off the debt. The passage states 'he does not become a payer through this, and that is the cause of liability.' Identify that the sabab is the pawner's act of paying his debt with the item.
Sabab is the effective cause in Hanafi jurisprudence.
3
Apply the absence of cause to the scenarios
In both scenarios (before pawn and after redemption), the pawner has not used the borrowed cloth to pay his debt. Therefore, the cause is absent, and no liability follows.
Cause-effect relationship: existence of cause leads to liability; absence negates it.
4
Conclude the ruling and its basis
The Hanafi position is clear: no liability. The proof is rational (dalil aqli): liability is contingent on using the item for debt payment; if that use does not occur, liability does not arise.
This ruling is consistent across the madhhab (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستعار کپڑا راہن کے پاس رہن رکھنے سے پہلے یار ہن چھڑانے کے بعد ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضمان ہے یا نہیں
ولو هلك الثوب العارية عند الراهن قبل ان يرهنه او بعد ما افتكه فلاضمان عليه لانه لا يصير قاضيا بهذا وهو الموجب على ما بيناه
ترجمہ اور اگر مستعار کپڑا راہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا رہن رکھنے سے پہلے یا اس کو چھڑانے کے بعد تو را ہن پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ را ہن اس سے اپنے قرض کو ادا کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور عمان کا موجب یہی ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح مستغیر نے معیر سے جو کمیل عاریت لیا ہے اگر وہ راہن کے پاس رہن دینے سے پہلے یا رہن کو چھڑانے کے بعد ہلاک ہو جائے تو چونکہ راہن نے اس کمبل سے اپنا قرض ادا نہیں کیا اس لئے راہن پر اس کا ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور ضمان کا سبب اس سے قرض کی ادائیگی تھی جو نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔
And if the borrowed cloth perishes with the pawner before he pawns it or after he redeems it, then there is no liability upon him because he does not become a payer through this, and that is the cause of liability according to what we have explained. Translation: And if the borrowed cloth perishes with the pawner before pawning or after redemption, then the pawner is not liable because the pawner does not pay his debt with it, and the cause of liability is that, according to the detail we have explained. Explanation: The musta'ir (borrower) took a blanket as a loan from the mu'ir (lender); if that blanket perishes with the pawner before pawning or after redemption, then because the pawner did not pay his debt with this blanket, so liability is not incumbent upon him, and the cause of liability was payment of debt with it, which is not found.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This section addresses when a pawner borrows an item to use it as a pawn. If the borrowed item is destroyed while in the pawner's possession either before he pawns it or after he redeems the pawn, the pawner is not liable (daman) to the lender. The reason is that liability in pawn transactions arises from the pawner using the item to satisfy his debt. Since in these two scenarios the pawner did not apply the item toward paying off his debt, the cause of liability is absent. Thus, the lender cannot claim compensation from the pawner for the destroyed item. This ruling is consistent with the general principle that liability attaches only when the pawn is used for debt satisfaction.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or responsibility to compensate for loss or damage.
عاریت ('āriyah): Loan for use; a gratuitous loan of a tangible item.
مستعیر (musta'īr): The borrower in a loan for use (ariyah).
معیر (mu'īr): The lender in a loan for use.
سبب (sabab): Cause; the effective cause that triggers a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A pawner is not liable for a borrowed item destroyed before pawn or after redemption because the cause of liability—using the item to pay the debt—is absent.

Dispute Between Lender and Borrower on Timing of Destruction
Procedural ruling on burden of proof in pawn disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi procedural rule that the denier's word is accepted in disputes over pawned property, and identify the exception when evidence is presented.

Core Idea
The borrower's word is accepted because he denies liability; the lender must prove his claim.

In transactions involving pawned items, disputes often arise about when the item was destroyed—before, during, or after the pawn period. The Hanafi school resolves such disputes through a fundamental procedural principle: the word of the denier is taken unless the claimant provides evidence. This lesson examines that principle in action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and claims
Lender (mu'ir) claims the item was destroyed while pawned, making borrower liable. Borrower (musta'ir) claims destruction occurred before pawning or after redemption, denying liability.
The borrower is also the pawner (raahin) in this context.
2
Determine claimant and denier
The lender is the claimant (mudda'i) because he asserts a right (daman) against the borrower. The borrower is the denier (munkir) because he denies any obligation.
In Hanafi procedure, the burden of proof lies on the claimant.
3
Apply the maxim 'al-qaul li al-munkir'
Since the borrower denies liability, his word is accepted without proof, unless the lender brings evidence (bayyinah) to support his claim.
The maxim means 'the statement is for the denier'.
4
Note the exception
If the lender produces credible witnesses that the item was destroyed during the pawn period, then the lender's claim prevails and the borrower becomes liable.
Evidence overrides the default acceptance of the denier's word.
5
State the practical outcome
In the absence of evidence, the borrower is not liable and his version of events is upheld.
This ruling protects the borrower from unfounded claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اختلفا في ذالك فالقول للراهن لانه ينكر الايفاء بدعواه الهلاك في هاتين الحالتين
ترجمہ اور اگر معیر اور مستعغیر دونوں اس میں اختلاف کریں تو راہن کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ راہن قرض کی ادائیگی کا منکر ہے ان دونوں حالتوں میں اپنے دعوی ہلاک کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح یعنی اگر معیر اور مستغیر میں اختلاف ہو جائے معیر کہتا ہے کہ مستعار بوقت رہن لہلاک ہوا ہے اور مستغیر کہتا ہے کہ رہن سے پہلے یا رہن چھڑانے کے بعد ہلاک ہوا ہے تو راہن کا قول معتبر ہوگا لیکن اگر معیر گواہ پیش کر دے تو پھر معیر کا قول معتبر ہوگا ۔ مستعیر کا قول کیوں معتبر ہے؟ اس لئے کہ معیر دعویٰ کرتا ہے کہ راہن کے ذمہ پر حق لازم آتا ہے اور مستغیر اس سے منکر ہے اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے اس لئے مستعغیر کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
And if they differ in that, then the word is of the pawner because he denies payment by his claim of destruction in these two situations. Translation: And if the mu'ir (lender) and musta'ir (borrower) differ in this, then the pawner's statement is accepted because the pawner denies payment due to his claim of destruction in these two states. Explanation: That is, if mu'ir and musta'ir differ - mu'ir says the borrowed item was destroyed at the time of pawn, and musta'ir says it was destroyed before pawning or after redemption - then the pawner's word is accepted. But if mu'ir brings witnesses, then mu'ir's word is accepted. Why is the musta'ir's word accepted? Because mu'ir claims that a right becomes incumbent upon the pawner, and musta'ir denies that, and the word of the denier is accepted; therefore, musta'ir's word is accepted.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
When the lender (mu'ir) and the borrower (musta'ir) dispute over when the borrowed item was destroyed, the pawner's (musta'ir's) statement is credited. The reason: the lender claims that the pawner owes liability (daman), which the pawner denies. In Hanafi legal procedure, the denier's word is accepted unless the claimant produces evidence. Thus, the pawner's claim that the item was destroyed before being used for pawn (or after redemption) is accepted, and he is not liable. However, if the lender brings witnesses to prove destruction during the pawn period, the lender's claim prevails.

Key Terms
قول (qawl): Statement or word; in legal disputes, the claim or testimony.
منکر (munkir): Denier; one who denies a claim.
مدعی (mudda'ī): Claimant; one who brings a legal claim.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence or witnesses that shift the burden of proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The borrower's word is never accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule in pawn disputes is that the denier's word is accepted unless the claimant provides evidence, protecting the borrower from unfounded liability.

Dispute Over Pawn Amount: Lender's Word Accepted
Ruling with proof via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whose word is accepted in a dispute over the authorized pawn amount and explain the qiyas (analogy) reasoning from the denial of the loan origin.

Core Idea
Lender's word prevails in both denying the loan and denying the amount authorized for pawn.

In transactions, disputes often arise over what was agreed. When a lender and borrower disagree on the amount for which a pawn was authorized, who should be believed? This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi ruling: the lender's word is accepted. We will trace the legal reasoning (qiyas) that links this to the stronger principle: the lender's denial of the entire loan is always believed. By the end, you will see how a contractual description follows the same logic as the contract's origin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the dispute
The lender (mu'ir) and borrower (musta'ir) disagree on the amount the lender authorized for the pawn. The lender claims a lower amount; the borrower claims a higher one.
This is a dispute over a contractual term (wasf), not the existence of the contract itself.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling is: the lender's word is accepted (قول المعير معتبر).
This means the lender is believed in court or arbitration.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling is derived by analogy to a stronger case: if the lender had denied giving permission for the pawn altogether (denial of the origin asl), his word would be accepted. Since the amount is a description (wasf) of that permission, the same principle applies.
The illa (effective cause) is that both are denials of a right claimed by the borrower.
4
Verify the logic with the textual variant
The text mentions a scribal issue: some manuscripts read 'kama' (as) instead of 'wa law' (and if). The correct reading is 'wa law' because 'kama' would invert the analogy, making the borrower's word accepted instead.
This shows the importance of accurate transmission in legal texts.
5
Apply the rule
In practice, if a lender says 'I authorized 300' and the borrower says '500', the lender's statement is taken as true unless the borrower brings evidence.
This prevents the borrower from expanding his liability beyond what was agreed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما لو اختلفا في مقدار ما امره بالرهن به فالقول للمعير لان القول قوله فى انکار اصله فكذا في انکار وصفه.
ترجمہ جیسا کہ اگر یہ دونوں اختلاف کریں اس مقدار میں جس کے بدلہ میں معیر نے رہن کا حکم دیا تھا تو معیر کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ مغیر کا قول معتبر ہے اصل عقد عاریت کے انکار میں ، پس ایسے ہی (اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا ) وصف عقد کے انکار میں۔ تشریح مغیر اور مستعیر میں اختلاف ہوا مغیر کہتا ہے کہ میں نے تم کو کہا تھا کہ پانچ سو میں رہن رکھنا اور مستعغیر کہتا ہے کہ آپ نے تین سو میں کہا تھا تو یہاں معیر کا قول معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ اگر وہ سرے سے ہی یوں کہہ دے کہ میں نے تجھے رہن رکھنے کی اجازت نہیں دی تھی تو میر کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے لہذا مقدار تو اس عقد کا ایک وصف ہوا تو وصف کے انکار میں بھی اسی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ تنبیہ یہاں ہدایہ کے نسخوں میں کما ہے لیکن یہ ناشین کا سہو ہے ورنہ درست ولو ہے ورنہ کما کی صورت میں مطلب غلط ہو جاتا ہے حالانکہ مسئلہ میں مستعیر کا قول معتبر ہوا ہے اور یہاں مغیر کا تو تشبیہ صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر معیر اور مستعیر سے قطع نظر کرتے ہوئے منکر ہونے کے اعتبار سے تشبیہ ملحوظ ہو تو تشبیہ درست ہو سکتی ہے۔
Just as if they differ about the amount for which he ordered him to pawn, then the word is of the mu'ir (lender), because his word is accepted in denial of the origin (of the contract), so too in denial of its description. Translation: Just as if these two differ about the amount for which the lender ordered the pawn, then the lender's word is accepted because the lender's word is accepted in denial of the origin of the contract of loan, so similarly (his word is accepted) in denial of its description. Explanation: The lender and borrower differed; the lender said 'I told you to pawn it for five hundred,' and the borrower said 'you said three hundred.' Here the lender's word is accepted because if he had outright said 'I did not permit you to pawn it at all,' his word would be accepted. So the amount is a description of the contract, so in denying the description, his word is also accepted. Note: In copies of the Hidaya it is 'kama' (as), but this is a scribal error (sahw); the correct is 'wa law' (and if). Otherwise, with 'kama' the meaning becomes incorrect because in that case the musta'ir's word is accepted, and here the mu'ir's word is accepted, so the analogy would not be correct. However, if we consider the analogy disregarding mu'ir and musta'ir, and only from the perspective of the denier, then the analogy can be correct.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage deals with a dispute between the lender (mu'ir) and borrower (musta'ir) over the amount for which the pawn was authorized. The lender's word is accepted because the authority to pawn is a contractual term (description) of the loan (ariyah). Since the lender's word would be accepted if he denied giving permission altogether, it is also accepted when he denies the specific amount. The commentary also addresses a textual issue: some manuscripts of al-Hidayah read 'kama' (as), but the correct reading is 'wa law' (and if) to maintain the logical analogy. If 'kama' is kept, the ruling would incorrectly imply that the borrower's word is accepted, which contradicts the given rule.

Key Terms
اصل (aṣl): Origin or root; here, the contract of loan (ariyah) itself.
وصف (waṣf): Description or attribute; here, the amount authorized for pawn.
سہو (sahw): Error or oversight; here, a scribal error in the manuscript.
قول المعير معتبر (qawl al-mu'ir mu'tabar): The lender's statement is accepted (as credible).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Lender
B) Borrower
C) Neither
D) Both

Key Takeaway
The lender's word is accepted in disputes over the authorized pawn amount by analogy to denial of the loan itself.

Liability for a Promised Debt in Pawn
Ruling on pawn pledged for a future loan that is destroyed before the loan is given

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a promised debt is like an existing debt to determine liability when a pawn perishes before the loan is given.

Core Idea
A promised debt is treated as existing for liability if the pawn perishes before the loan is given.

This lesson explores a nuanced ruling in the Hanafi school: when someone pawns an item for a promised loan, and the item is destroyed before the loan is disbursed, the mortgagee becomes liable for the promised amount. The reasoning rests on the principle that a promise can have legal effect akin to an actual debt. Understanding this ruling sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi fiqh balances contractual expectations with practical contingencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key parties and their roles
In the scenario, there are at least three parties: the owner of the item (mu'ir), the borrower (musta'ir) who pawns the item, and the mortgagee who promises a loan. Clarify each role and their relationship.
The musta'ir borrows the item specifically to pawn it.
2
Confirm the legal status of the promised debt
The promised debt (dayn maw'ud) is not yet given, but the Hanafi rule 'al-maw'ud ka al-mawjud' treats it as existing for liability purposes. Verify that this principle applies here.
This is a qiyas-based extension, not a direct text.
3
Apply the ruling to the pawn's destruction
If the pawn perishes in the mortgagee's possession before the loan is given, the mortgagee must pay the promised amount (if equal to the pawn's value). Link this to the principle: had the loan been given, the debt would be discharged; since it wasn't, the mortgagee's liability substitutes.
If the named amount and value differ, further rules apply (not covered here).
4
Trace the recourse between parties
The owner (mu'ir) can claim the pawn's value from the borrower (musta'ir/pawner), who then recovers from the mortgagee. Understand why: the owner's right is against the pawner, and the pawner then seeks indemnity from the mortgagee.
This ensures the owner is compensated regardless of the mortgagee's default.

And if the musta'ir pawns the borrowed item for a promised debt, and that is that he pawns it so that the mortgagee would lend him such and such, then it perishes in the hand of the mortgagee before the loan, and the named amount and value are equal, then he becomes liable for the amount of the promised named amount, because we have explained that the promised is like the existing. And the mu'ir has recourse against the pawner for its equivalent because his recovery of the pawn's value from the mortgagee is like its safety due to the pawner being freed from liability. Translation: And if the musta'ir pawns the borrowed item for a promised debt, i.e., he pawns it so that the mortgagee will give him such a loan, then the pawn perishes in the mortgagee's possession before the loan is given, and the named amount and value are equal, then the mortgagee is liable for the amount of the named promise because we have explained that the promised is like the existing. And the mu'ir will have recourse against the pawner for its equivalent because the pawner's recovery of the pawn's value from the mortgagee is like its safety due to the pawner's freedom from liability. Explanation: Khalid borrowed Zayd's blanket to pawn it. Then Khalid and Bakr conversed: Bakr said, 'Pawn the blanket, and I will lend you 1000 rupees.' Khalid pawned it, but Bakr had not yet given the 1000 rupees; it was only a promise. This is a promised debt. It has passed in the first chapter that the promised is like the existing. Coincidentally, the blanket's value is also 1000 rupees. The blanket perished with Bakr. So the mortgagee will give 1000 rupees in liability to the pawner because if Bakr had given the loan already and the pawn perished, the debt would be discharged. Here it is not discharged, so the mortgagee must pay it because the promised is in the rank of the existing.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage addresses when a borrower (musta'ir) uses a borrowed item as a pawn for a promised loan (dayn maw'ud). The ruling: if the pawn perishes before the loan is given, the mortgagee is liable for the amount promised. The basis is the principle that 'the promised is like the existing' (al-maw'ud ka al-mawjud) in terms of liability. Consequently, the lender (mu'ir) can claim the value of the item from the pawner, who then recovers from the mortgagee. The example: a person borrows a blanket to pawn for a promised loan of 1000. Before the loan is given, the blanket is destroyed. The mortgagee must pay 1000 because if the loan had been given, the debt would have been discharged; since not, the mortgagee owes the value. This shows the rigorous logic of Hanafi contract law.

Key Terms
دین موعود (dayn maw'ūd): A promised debt; a future obligation not yet given.
كالموجود (ka al-mawjūd): Like the existing; a principle that a promise can have legal effect similar to an existing fact.
مسمى (musammā): Named or stipulated amount; the specific sum promised.
قیمت (qīmah): Value; market value of the pawned item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The pawner
B) The borrower (musta'ir)
C) The mortgagee
D) The lender (mu'ir)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats a promised debt as existing for liability if the pawn perishes before the loan is given, imposing payment on the mortgagee.

Equivalence of Bara'at and Istifa' in Rahn
Explains equivalence of bara'at and istifa' in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that bara'at min al-dayn and istifa' min al-murtahin are equivalent in discharging the debtor's liability.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, discharging a debt and recovering from a pledge are legally identical in effect.

This lesson clarifies a subtle point in the contract of pledge (rahn). The author explains that whether the debtor is acquitted of the debt (bara'at) or the creditor recovers his due from the pawn (istifa'), the debtor's liability is discharged in both cases. The only difference is procedural.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal concepts
Recognize that bara'at min al-dayn means acquittal from debt (the debtor is freed from liability), and istifa' min al-murtahin means recovery of the debt from the pledgee (the creditor gets his money from the pawn or its value).
These are the two processes being compared.
2
Understand the scenario
Consider a debtor (rahin) who pawns an item with a pledgee (murtahin) as security for a loan from a third party. The example in the text: Zayd pawns an item with Bakr for a loan from Khalid.
The pawn is held by a different person from the lender.
3
Recognize the equivalence
The author states that there is no difference between bara'at and istifa' — both result in the debtor's liability being discharged. The ruling (hukm) is one and the same.
The phrase 'لان سلامة مالية الرهن' (because the monetary value of the pawn is intact) supports this.
4
Note the procedural difference
The only difference is the method: istifa' occurs when the creditor recovers from the pledgee (e.g., by selling the pawn), while bara'at occurs when the debtor pays directly. Both achieve the same legal end.
In the example, if the pawn perishes, the debtor still owes the debt; similarly, if the debtor pays, he is acquitted.
5
Apply the ruling
When advising on a real case, you determine that the debtor's obligation is cleared whether the debt is paid directly or the pawn is used to satisfy it. The equivalence is fundamental in mu'amalat.
This principle ensures consistency in financial transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پھر زید خالد سے یہ ہزار روپے لیگا کیونکہ اگر قرض دینے کے بعد مرہون بکر کے پاس ہلاک ہوتا تب بھی زید خالد سے ہزار روپے لیتا ایسے ہی اب بھی لیگا۔ خلاصہ کلام راہن کی برائت من الدین اور استیفاء من المرتھن میں کوئی فرق نہیں دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے۔ مصنف نے اسی براءت اور استیفاء کی مساوات کو اس عبارت میں بیان فرمایا ہے لان سلامة مالية الرهن الخ یعنی مرہون کی مالیت دونوں صورتوں میں راہن کے پاس صحیح سالم رہی بس فرق اتنا ہے کہ یہاں مرتین سے وصولیابی کے طریقہ پر ہے اور بعد الا قرض براءت ذمہ کے طریقہ پر ہے۔
Then Zayd will take these one thousand rupees from Khalid because if after giving the loan the pawned item perished with Bakr, even then Zayd would take one thousand rupees from Khalid. Similarly, now he will take. Summary: There is no difference between the acquittal of the debtor from the debt and the recovery from the pledgee; the ruling of both is one. The author has expressed this equality of bara'at and istifa' in this statement: 'because the safety of the monetary value of the pawn...' i.e., the monetary value of the pawn remains safe and sound with the debtor in both cases. The only difference is that here it is by way of recovery from the pledgee, and after payment it is by way of acquittal of liability.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the equivalence of two legal situations in the contract of pledge (rahn). The author explains that whether the debtor is acquitted from debt (bara'at min al-dayn) or the creditor recovers his debt from the pledgee (istifa' min al-murtahin), the effect is the same: the debtor's liability is discharged. The difference is merely procedural. The example given: if Zayd pawns an item with Bakr as security for a loan from Khalid, and the item perishes, Zayd still owes Khalid. Similarly, if Zayd pays off the loan, he is acquitted. The author cites the phrase 'li ann salāmata māliyati al-rahn' (because the monetary value of the pawn is intact) from the matn to support this. This is a clarification of a subtle point in fiqh al-mu'amalat.

Key Terms
برائت من الدین (bara'at min al-dayn): Acquittal from debt; discharge of the debtor's liability.
استیفاء من المرتھن (istifa' min al-murtahin): Recovery of the debt from the pledgee (the creditor who holds the pawn).
راہن (rahin): The debtor who gives the pawn.
مرتھن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pawn as security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Pledgee's Options When Lender Frees a Pawned Borrowed Slave
Ruling on the pledgee's options when the lender frees a borrowed slave that is pawned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a lender frees a pawned borrowed slave and explain why the pledgee is given two distinct options with their underlying reasoning.

Core Idea
Manumission by the owner is valid, but the pledgee may choose between the debtor or the lender for recovery.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where two contracts intersect: a loan for use (ariyah) and a pledge (rahn). The owner-lender (mu'ir) frees a slave that he had lent and is now pawned to a third party (murtahin). The Hanafi school rules that the manumission is valid, but the pledgee does not lose his security interest. Instead, he is given a choice between two remedies. Understanding this ruling illustrates how Hanafi fiqh balances ownership rights with contractual security.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the transaction
Recognize the three parties: the lender (mu'ir, owner of the slave), the debtor (rahin, who borrowed the slave and then pawned it), and the pledgee (murtahin, the creditor holding the slave as collateral). The slave is originally borrowed (ariyah) and then pledged (rahn).
2
State the validity of the manumission
The manumission is valid because the lender (mu'ir) still owns the slave (malik al-raqaba). Ownership is not transferred by the loan or pledge.
The manumission (itq) is an act of ownership.
3
List the pledgee's two options
The pledgee may either: (1) demand his debt directly from the debtor (rahin), or (2) hold the lender (mu'ir) liable for the slave's market value and keep that value as a substitute pledge until the debt is paid.
These are rights, not obligations; the pledgee chooses.
4
Explain the reasoning (talil) for each option
Option 1: The debt remains due from the debtor who has not fulfilled it. Option 2: The pledgee's right was attached (ta'alluq) to the slave with the lender's consent; by freeing the slave, the lender destroyed that right, so he must compensate. The compensation value takes the place of the pawned object.
The reasoning is based on the principle that destroying a pledged item triggers liability.
5
Note the consequence of retrieving the value
The pledgee holds the value as a pledge until the debt is paid, then returns it to the lender. This is because the value stands in the place of the original pawned object ('ayn).
The legal effect is that the value substitutes the object, and ownership of the value returns to the lender after the debt is satisfied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عاریت غلام کو معیر آزاد کر دے تو کیا حکم ہے ولو كانت العارية عبداً فاعتقه المعير جاز لقيام ملك الرقبة ثم المرتهن بالخيار إن شاء رجع بالدين على الراهن لانه لم يستوفه وان شاء ضمن المعير قيمته لان الحق قد تعلق برقبته برضاه وقد اتلفه بالاعتاق وتكون رهنا عنده الى ان يقبض دينه فيردها الى المعير لان استرداد القيمة كاسترداد العين ترجمہ اور اگر عاریت غلام ہو پس معیر نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو عشق جائز ہے ملک رقبہ کے قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر مرتبن کر اختیار ہے اگر چاہے راہن سے قرض واپس لے اس لئے که مرتهن نے قرض وصول نہیں کیا اور اگر چاہے معیر کے غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن بنادے اس لئے که حق مرتهن غلام کی گردن کے ساتھ معیر کی رضامندی سے متعلق ہوا ہے حالانکہ حق کو معیر نے آزاد کر کے تلف کر دیا ہے اور قیمت مرتہن کے پاس رہن رہے گی یہاں تک کہ وہ اپنے دین پر قبضہ کرے پس مرتہن اس کو معیر کی جانب واپس کر دیگا اس لئے کہ قیمت کو واپس لینا عین کو واپس لینے کے مثل ہے۔ تشریح مستعار بجائے کمبل کے غلام ہے جو بکر کے پاس رہن ہے زید نے (معیر نے ) اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو چونکہ زید اس کا مالک ہے اس لئے عشق صحیح ہو گیا اب مرتہن ( بکر) کیا کرے تو فرمایا کہ اس کو دو اختیار ہیں۔ -1 ا خالد سے ( راہن) اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کرے کیونکہ غلام کے اعتماق کی وجہ سے بکر نے اپنا حق وصول نہیں پایا لہذا اس کا حق برقرار ہے تو راہن سے اپنا قرض واپس لے لے۔ ۲- زید (معیر ) سے غلام کی قیمت کا تاوان لے کر وہ قیمت اپنے پاس رہن رکھے جب خالد اس کا قرض ادا کر دے اس وقت یہ قیمت زید ( معیر ) کو دے دی جائے۔ اب رہی یہ بات کہ معیر سے ضمان کیوں؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مرتہن کا حق غلام کی گردن سے معیر کی رضا مندی سے متعلق ہوا ہے اور معیر نے غلام کو آزاد کر کے مرتہن کا حق تلف کر دیا لہذا امر تین معیر سے قیمت کا تاوان لے سکتا ہے اب رہی یہ بات کہ معیر قیمت کو بعد اداء دین کیوں واپس لیگا ؟ تو اس کا جواب دیالان استرداد.... الخ سے یعنی اگر عین مرہون موجود ہوتا تو بعد اداء دین مرہون کو معیر واپس لیتا ایسے ہی قیمت جو عین کا قائم مقام ہے اس کو بھی معیر واپس لیگا۔
Rule: If the borrowed item is a slave, and the lender (mu'ir) frees him, then the manumission is valid due to the establishment of ownership of the slave. Then the pledgee (murtahin) has an option: if he wishes, he may go back to the debtor (rahin) for the debt because he has not received it; and if he wishes, he may hold the lender liable for the slave's value, because the right (of the pledgee) was attached to the slave with the lender's consent, and the lender destroyed it by manumission. And the value will remain as a pledge with him until he receives his debt, then he returns it to the lender, because retrieving the value is like retrieving the object itself. Explanation: The borrowed slave is a slave that is pawned with Bakr. Zayd (the lender) freed him. Since Zayd owns him, the manumission is valid. Now what does the pledgee (Bakr) do? The author says he has two options: (1) Demand his debt from Khalid (the debtor) because due to the manumission Bakr has not received his right, so his right remains, so he takes his debt from the debtor. (2) Take the value of the slave from Zayd (lender) as compensation, and keep that value as a pledge with himself. When Khalid pays off his debt, then he gives this value to Zayd. Why is the lender liable? Because the pledgee's right was attached to the slave with the lender's consent, and the lender destroyed it by freeing. So the pledgee can take compensation. Why does the lender get the value back after the debt is paid? Because if the pawned object were present, after payment the lender would get it back. Similarly, the value, which stands in place of the object, will be returned to the lender.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a specific scenario in pledge transactions. When a borrowed slave is pawned, and the lender (mu'ir) who owns the slave frees him, the manumission is valid because the lender owns the slave. However, this act destroys the pledgee's security interest. Therefore, the pledgee is given a choice between two remedies: either demand the debt from the original debtor (rahin), or hold the lender liable for the slave's market value and keep that value as a pledge until the debt is paid. The reasoning is that the pledgee's right was attached to the slave with the lender's permission, and the lender's act of manumission is a destruction of that right. The value substitutes for the pawned object. This illustrates the Hanafi principles of guarantee (daman) and the effect of manumission on existing rights.

Key Terms
معیر (mu'ir): The lender in a contract of loan (ariyah).
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave.
خیار (khiyar): Option; here the pledgee's right to choose between two courses of action.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; the lender becomes liable for the value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only demand debt from the debtor.

C) Either demand debt from debtor or demand value from lender.
D) The pledge has no recourse.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling protects the pledgee's security while respecting the owner's right to manumit, giving the pledgee a choice between two remedies.

Liability of a Borrower Who Violates Then Returns to Agreement
Ruling on liability when borrowed item is used before pledging, then pledged, then perishes after debt payment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a trustee who violates and then returns to agreement is discharged from liability.

Core Idea
Violation followed by return to agreement discharges trustee liability.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the Hidayah: a borrower uses a borrowed item before pawning it, but then pawns it as intended. After the debt is paid, the item perishes. Despite the initial violation, the borrower is not liable. Why? Because he returned to the agreement. This illustrates a key Hanafi principle: a trustee who violates and then corrects his action is no longer liable.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the borrower (musta'ir), the item, and the sequence: borrow → use → pawn → pay debt → item perishes.
2
Identify the initial violation
Recognize that using the item before pawning is transgression (ta'addi), which normally triggers liability.
Trustees (amin) become liable when they commit ta'addi.
3
Identify the return to agreement
Note that pawning the item as intended constitutes return to agreement (muwafaqat).
4
Apply the principle
Apply the established rule: 'If a trustee violates and then returns to agreement, he is discharged from liability.' This removes the liability.
The principle is stated in the text: اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ جب امین مالک کی مخالفت کرے اور پھر موافقت کرے تو اس پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا.
5
Understand the thamarah (result)
Conclude that the borrower (now pawner) is not liable for the perished item, even though he had committed ta'addi earlier.
The liability is not revived after discharge.

غلام یا چوپایہ کو مستعار لیا رہن رکھنے کے لئے اور ان سے خود انتفاع کر لے تو کیا حکم ہے ولو استعار عبدا اودابة ليرهنه فاستخدم العبد اوركب الدابة قبل ان يرهنهما ثم رهنهما بمال مثل قيمتهما ثم قضى المال فلم يقبضهما حتى هلكا عند المرتهن فلاضمان على الراهن لانه قد برئ من الضمان حين رهنهما فانه كان امينا خالف ثم عاد الى الوفاق ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے غلام یا چوپایہ مستعار لیا تا کہ اس کو رہن رکھے پس مستعیر نے غلام سے خدمت لی یا چوپایہ پر سوار ہوا ان دونوں کو رہن رکھنے سے پہلے پھر اس نے ان دونوں کو رہن رکھا ایسے مال کے بدلہ میں جو ان دونوں کی قیمت کے مثل ہے پھر راہن نے قرض ادا کر دیا پس ( ابھی ) ان دونوں پر قبضہ نہیں کیا یہاں تک کہ وہ دونوں مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئے تو راہن پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ضمان سے بری ہو چکا ہے۔ جبکہ اس نے دونوں کو رہن رکھ دیا اس لئے کہ وہ ایسا امین تھا جس نے مخالفت کی تھی پھر موافقت کی جانب لوٹ گیا۔ تشریح اگر مستعار نے رہن کے لئے غلام یا گھوڑا مستعار لیا ہو اور پھر رہن رکھنے سے پہلے غلام سے خدمت کی ہو یا گھوڑے پر سوار ہوا ہو ۔ پھر ان کو رہن رکھدیا پھر مرتہن کا قرض ادا کر دیا لیکن ابھی قبضہ نہیں کر پایا تھا کہ غلام یا گھوڑا مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا تو اب راہن پر ضمان نہ ہو گا کیونکہ اس نے معیر کے مال سے اپنا قرض ادا نہیں کیا۔ سوال قرض ادا نہیں کیا لیکن ان سے خدمت لیکر اس نے تعدی تو کی ہے اس تعدی کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان واجب ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ امانت میں بعد تعدی ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے؟ جواب جب مستعغیر نے ان کو رہن رکھدیا تو اب وہ ضمان سے بری ہو گیا ۔ کیونکہ اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ جب امین مالک کی مخالفت کرے اور پھر موافقت کرے تو اس پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور یہاں یہی صورت ہے لہذا ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
If he borrowed a slave or an animal to pawn it, and he used the slave or rode the animal before pawning them, then he pawned them for an amount equal to their value, then he paid off the debt, but did not take possession of them until they perished with the pledgee, then there is no liability on the pawner (rahin) because he is exempt from liability when he pawned them. For he was a trustee who violated (the trust) but then returned to agreement. Explanation: If the borrower borrowed a slave or horse to pawn, and before pawning he used the slave or rode the horse, then pawned them, then paid off the pledgee's debt, but before taking possession the slave or horse perished with the pledgee, then there is no liability on the pawner because he did not pay off the debt with the lender's property. Objection: He did not pay off the debt, but he committed transgression (taddi) by using them. Due to this transgression, liability should be wajib, because after transgression in trust, liability becomes wajib. Answer: When the borrower pawned them, he became exempt from liability. Because the established principle is that when a trustee violates the owner's trust but then returns to agreement, liability is not wajib upon him. This is the case here, so liability is not wajib.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario in the Hanafi school about the liability of a borrower (musta'ir) who uses a borrowed item before fulfilling the purpose for which it was borrowed (pledging). The borrower initially commits a transgression (taddi) by using the item without permission. However, he later returns to agreement by pawning the item as intended. The ruling is that after pawning, the previous transgression is effaced, and he becomes exempt from liability. This is based on the legal principle: 'If a trustee violates and then returns to agreement, he is discharged from liability.' The text also addresses an objection: why isn't he liable for the transgression? The answer is that once he returns to the proper course (pawning), the violation is overlooked. This illustrates the Hanafi emphasis on the restoration of trust through corrective action.

Key Terms
مستعیر (musta'ir): The borrower in a contract of loan (ariyah).
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or unauthorized use of the borrowed item.
موافقت (muwafaqat): Returning to agreement; acting in accordance with the owner's consent.
ضمان (daman): Liability; here, the financial liability for the perished item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must pay compensation for the violation.
B) He must return to agreement by acting according to the owner's consent.
C) The owner must forgive him.
D) The item must be returned before perishing.

Key Takeaway
A trustee who violates trust but then returns to the intended purpose is discharged from liability for subsequent loss.
