Liability after Redemption: Borrower Becomes Depositary
Ruling on borrower who redeems pledge then uses it and it perishes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a borrower's liability after redeeming a pledge and using it, and explain the legal transition from musta'ir to mudi'.

Core Idea
After redemption, the borrower becomes a depositary and is not liable for accidental loss.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the law of pledge (rahn): what happens if a borrower who has been using a pledged item redeems it (returns the loan), continues to use it, and then the item perishes due to no fault of his? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on a change in legal status. Understanding this ruling clarifies when liability attaches and when it does not after the redemption of a pledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage carefully: the borrower (musta'ir) redeemed the pledge (fakk al-rahn), then used the animal or slave. The item did not perish during that use. Later, it perished on its own, without any act by the borrower.
The timing of destruction is critical: after redemption and after the use that did not cause harm.
2
Determine the legal status change
Upon redemption, the borrower ceases to be a musta'ir (borrower of the use). The text says he becomes like a mudi' (depositary). This status change is the key to the ruling.
The term mudi' refers to a trustee who holds property on trust without usage rights.
3
Understand the reasoning
The ruling of 'ariyah (loan for use) ends with redemption. Once the loan is repaid, the borrower's permission to use the item in that capacity terminates. However, if the owner permits continued possession, the borrower becomes a depositary. As a depositary, he is a trustee (amin) and not liable for accidental loss.
The reasoning is based on the principle that trustees are only liable for negligence or transgression (ta'addi).
4
Apply the trustee liability rule
Since the destruction occurred without fault after the status change, the borrower is not liable. The condition is that the destruction is not caused by his prior use (which did not cause harm) or any subsequent act.
If the destruction had occurred during the unauthorized use, he would be liable as a transgressor.
5
Note cross-madhhab disagreement
Some other schools may hold the borrower liable even after redemption if he uses the item without fresh permission. The Hanafi school relies on the termination of the borrowing contract and the return to compliance.
This disagreement (ikhtilaf) does not affect the Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستغیر کیلئے مرہون کو چھڑا کر استعمال کرے تو کیا حکم ہے
وكذا اذا افتك الرهن ثم ركب الدابة او استخدم العبد فلم يعطب ثم عطب بعد ذالك من غير صنعه لا يضمن لانه بعد الفكاك بمنزلة المودع لا بمنزلة المستعير لانتهاء حكم الاستعارة بالفكاك وقد عاد الى الوفاق فيبرا عن الضمان
ترجمہ: اور ایسے ہی جبکہ مستعغیر نے رہن کو چھڑالیا نہو پھر وہ چوپایہ پر سوار ہوا ہو یا غلام سے خدمت کی ہو پس وہ ہلاک نہیں ہوا پھر اس کے بعد بغیر اس کے کچھ کئے وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو مستغیر ضامن نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ چھڑانے کے بعد مستعغیر مودع کے درجہ میں ہے ستعغیر کے درجہ میں نہیں ہے چھڑانے کی وجہ سے عاریت کا حکم ختم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ لوٹ گیا موافقت کی جانب تو وہ ضمان سے بری ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح: مستعیر نے مرہون کو چھوڑا کر اس کو استعمال کیا جس میں وہ ہلاک نہیں ہوا پھر اس کے بعد مرہون خود بخود ہلاک ہو گیا تو بھی مستغیر ضامن نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ مستعغیر نے جب رہن چھڑالیا تو اب وہ مستغیر نہیں رہا بلکہ مودع بن گیا اور مودع اور امین کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ مخالفت کے بعد ہلاکت سے پہلے موافقت مالک کرے تو اس پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔
And similarly, if he redeemed the pledge, then rode the animal or used the slave, and it did not perish, then after that it perished without his act, he is not liable because after redemption he is like a depositary, not like a borrower, because the ruling of borrowing ends with redemption, and he has returned to agreement, so he is freed from liability.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage addresses a second scenario: the borrower has already redeemed the pledged item (fakk al-rahn). After redemption, he uses the item—riding or employing—but it does not perish during his use. Later, the item perishes on its own, without any fault of the borrower. The ruling is that he is not liable for this destruction. The reason given is that upon redemption, the borrower's status changes: he is no longer a musta'ir (borrower) but rather a mudi' (depositary). The ruling of 'ariyah (loan for use) terminates with redemption. The borrower has now returned to compliance with the owner's consent. As a depositary, he is a trustee, and trustees are not liable for accidental loss. The Urdu commentary reinforces this, stating that if a trustee opposes the owner (through unauthorized use) but then returns to compliance before the destruction, liability is removed.

Key Terms
مودع (mudi'): A depositary, one who keeps an item on trust without usage rights.
مستعیر (musta'ir): A borrower, one who receives the use of an item without payment.
فكاك (fakk): Redemption; the act of repaying the loan and reclaiming the pledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because after redemption he is a depositary
C) Yes, because he was a borrower initially

Key Takeaway
After redeeming a pledge, the borrower becomes a depositary and is not liable for accidental loss, provided he returns to compliance with the owner's consent.

Two Types of Borrowers in Pledge Transactions: The Liability Distinction
Definition and distinction between two types of musta'ir in pledge transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the musta'ir fil-rahn and the ordinary musta'ir, and explain why the former is not liable for destruction after pledging the item.

Core Idea
The borrower for pledge is not liable because his pledging achieves the owner's purpose, making his possession constructive ownership.

In Hanafi law, the term 'musta'ir' (borrower) covers two distinct cases: one who borrows to use the item for himself, and one who borrows specifically to pledge it as security for a debt. Though both involve borrowing, their liability for destruction differs fundamentally. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind that difference, focusing on the concept of constructive possession (yad hukmi) and the owner's purpose (maqsud al-amir).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Types of Musta'ir
From the text, extract the two categories: (1) musta'ir fil-rahn (borrower for pledge) and (2) musta'ir for personal use. Note their different legal consequences.
The text uses 'musta'ir' and 'musta'ghir' interchangeably.
2
Understand the Nature of Possession (Yad)
For the ordinary borrower, his hand is 'yad nafsihi' — his own independent possession. For the pledge borrower, his possession is linked to the owner's purpose.
Yad nafsihi means the owner's constructive possession is not achieved until physical return.
3
Analyze the Owner's Purpose (Maqsud al-Amir)
The owner (mu'ir) who lends the item for pledge intends that the item serve as collateral. When the borrower pledges it, he fulfills that purpose, creating constructive possession in the owner.
The text says the borrower 'yuhassilu maqsud al-amir' — he achieves the owner's objective.
4
Contrast the Liability Outcomes
After pledging, the borrower for pledge is deemed to have returned the item to the owner (hukman). Thus, if the pledge is destroyed, he is not liable. The ordinary borrower remains liable because his possession is independent.
The key is whether the owner's constructive possession is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستغیر کی کتنی قسمیں ہیں
وهذا بخلاف المستعير لان يده يد نفسه فلابد من الوصول الى يد المالك اما المستعير في الرهن فيحصل مقصود الأمر وهـو الـرجـوع عليه عند الهلاك وتحقق الاستيفاء
ترجمہ: اور یہ متغیر کے خلاف ہے اس لئے کہ مستغیر کا قبضہ اس کا ذاتی قبضہ ہے تو مالک کی جانب وصول ضروری ہے بہر حال مستعغیر رہن تو آمر کے مقصود کو حاصل کراتا ہے اور وہ مقصود را ہن مستغیر پر رجوع ہے ( مرتہن کے پاس ) ہلاکت کے وقت اور وصولیابی کے محقق ہونے کے وقت ۔
تشریح: مستغیر کی دو قسمیں ہیں ۔
- وہ مستغیر جو رہن کے لئے عاریت لے۔
-۲ وہ مستعغیر جو اپنے کام کیلئے عاریت لے دونوں کا حکم جدا گانہ ہے۔
مستغیر رہن کا حکم تو وہ ہے جو مذکور ہوا کہ وہ مخالفت کے بعد موافقت کرے تو بعد موافقت ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وہ مودع کے درجہ میں ہے ۔ اور مودع اور امین نے جب موافقت کرلی تو گویا حکماً اب امانت پر مالک کا قبضہ ہو گیا اور جب حکماً مالک کا قبضہ ہو گیا تو اب ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور خالص مستغیر کا قبضہ اپنا ذاتی قبضہ ہے لہذاوہاں حکما ما لک کا قبضہ نہیں ہوا بلکہ مالک کا قبضہ تب ہی ہوگا جبکہ وہ مستعار مالک کے حوالہ کر دے لہذا اگر اس کی جانب سے تعدی کے بعد بھی مستعار ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اور مستعغیر رہن پر نہ ہوگا۔
اب رہی یہ بات کہ مستعغیر رہن میں حکما آمر کا قبضہ کیسے مانا گیا ہے؟
تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مستغیر رہن جو کچھ کر لگا یعنی مرتہن کے پاس رہن رکھنا وہ آمر کے مقصود کی تحصیل کیلئے کرتا ہے کیونکہ آمر (معیر ) کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ اگر مرہون مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے جس سے مرتہن قرض کو وصول پانے والا قرار دیا جائے تو اس وقت معیر کو حق ہوگا کہ راہن سے ضمان لے لے کیونکہ اس وقت راہن نے اس کے مال سے اپنے قرض کو ادا کیا ہے۔
بہر حال ان وجوہات کی وجہ سے ان دونوں مستبیوں میں فرق کیا گیا ہے۔
And this is unlike the borrower (in general), because his hand is his own hand, so it is necessary for it to reach the hand of the owner. As for the borrower in the context of pledge, he fulfills the purpose of the command, which is to have recourse to him (the borrower) at the time of destruction and the realization of recovery.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two types of borrowers: (1) the musta'ir who borrows specifically to pledge the item (musta'ir fil-rahn), and (2) the ordinary musta'ir who borrows for his own use. The key difference lies in the nature of their possession (yad). For the ordinary borrower, his hand is his own hand (yad nafsihi), meaning his possession is independent, so the owner's constructive possession is not achieved unless the item is physically returned to the owner. In contrast, the borrower for pledge, by pledging the item to the pledgee, achieves the owner's objective—that is, providing security for a debt. Hence, his act of pledging is considered a constructive delivery to the owner (mu'ir) because it serves the owner's purpose: if the pledge is destroyed, the owner can claim compensation from the pledgor, since the pledgor has used the owner's property to pay off his debt. Thus, the borrower for pledge, after pledging, is deemed to have returned the item to the owner in a constructive sense (hukman). This is why he is not liable for subsequent destruction, unlike the ordinary borrower.

Key Terms
ید نفسه (yad nafsihi): One's own hand/possession, indicating independent control.
مقصود آمر (maqsud al-amir): The purpose of the one who commands (here, the owner/lender).
مستعیر رہن (musta'ir fil-rahn): The borrower who borrows an item specifically to pledge it as collateral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he pays rent
B) Because his pledging achieves the owner's purpose, creating constructive possession
C) Because the pledge is more valuable
D) Because he is more trustworthy

Key Takeaway
The musta'ir fil-rahn is not liable for destruction after pledging because his action achieves the owner's purpose, establishing constructive possession.

Pledgor's Transgression: Liability for Destroying Pledgee's Right
Ruling that the pledgor's damage to the pledged property is liable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pledgor's damage to the pledged property and explain the qiyas used to derive the liability.

Core Idea
A pledgor cannot destroy his own pledge because the pledgee's right makes him liable as a stranger.

You might assume an owner can do what he wants with his own property, but once it is pledged, an inviolable right of the pledgee attaches. This passage from al-Hidayah explains that any transgression by the pledgor against the pledged property is liable (madhmun), and proves it through qiyas to two similar situations where a property owner is restricted by another's right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the subject
Locate the initial statement: 'The transgression of the pledgor against the pledge is liable.' Note that the subject is the pledgor's act (jinaya) and the ruling is liability (daman).
Liability means compensation for the value or repair.
2
Extract the illa (rationale)
The text gives the reason: 'because it is a destruction of a necessary, respected right.' The illa is that the pledgor is destroying a right (haqq lazim muhtaram) of the pledgee that is attached to the property.
The term 'lazim' indicates the right is binding; 'muhtaram' indicates it is protected.
3
Examine the first qiyas: terminal illness
The text analogizes to the case of a terminally ill person whose property is encumbered by the heirs' right. Just as the ill person cannot give away more than one-third because of the heirs' right, the pledgor cannot destroy the pledge because of the pledgee's right.
In both cases, the owner is like a stranger (ajnabi) concerning liability.
4
Examine the second qiyas: bequeathed services of a slave
If a slave's services are bequeathed and the heirs destroy the slave, they must pay the full value to buy a replacement. This shows that when someone has a right to specific property, destruction by the owner triggers liability.
The right here is a right to services, just as the pledgee has a right to hold the property as security.
5
Synthesize the principle
The common element (illa) in all three cases is that a binding right of another person is attached to property, making the owner liable for damaging it as if he were a stranger.
This establishes the Hanafi rule that the pledgor's jinaya on the pledge is mithmun.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن کی مرہون پر جنایت مضمون ہے
قال وجناية الراهن على الرهن مضمونة لانه تفويت حق لازم محترم و تعلق مثله بالمال يجعل المالك كالاجنبى فى حق الضمان كتعلق حق الورثة بمال المريض مرض الموت يمنع نفاذ تبرعه فيما وراء الثلث والعبد الموصى بخدمته اذا أتلفه الورثة ضمنوا قيمته ليشتري بها عبد يقوم مقامه
He said: The transgression of the pledgor against the pledge is liable, because it is a destruction of a necessary, respected right. And the attachment of the like of this right to property makes the owner like a stranger with respect to liability, just as the attachment of the right of heirs to the property of a person terminally ill prevents the execution of his bequest beyond one-third, and the slave whose services are bequeathed, if the heirs destroy him, they are liable for his value to purchase a slave to take his place.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage establishes that if a pledgor (rahin) deliberately damages or destroys the pledged property (rahn), he is liable (madhmun) for compensation. The reason given is that the pledgee (murtahin) has a necessary (lazim) and respected (muhtaram) right over the property. By destroying the property, the pledgor extinguishes this right. The text draws an analogy (qiyas) to two cases: (1) during terminal illness (marad al-mawt), the estate's right attaches to the property, restricting the validity of bequests beyond one-third; the owner in such a state cannot freely donate beyond the limit because the heirs' right is attached. Similarly, the pledgee's right attached to the pledged property makes the pledgor like a stranger (ajnabi) regarding liability—he cannot damage it without consequence. (2) If a slave whose services have been bequeathed (al-'abd al-musi bi-khidmatihi) is destroyed by the heirs, they must pay its full value to purchase a replacement slave. This shows that when someone has a right over a specific property, its destruction by the owner triggers liability. The Urdu commentary (not present in the window) would elaborate on these analogies.

Key Terms
جنایت (jinaya): Transgression or damage caused by the pledgor to the pledged property.
حق لازم محترم (haqq lazim muhtaram): A necessary and respected right, here the pledgee's right over the pledged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the property belongs to the pledgee
B) Because it destroys the pledgee's necessary right
C) Because it is a sin
D) Because the pledgee is a stranger

Key Takeaway
The pledgor's intentional damage to pledged property is liable because it destroys the pledgee's attached binding right, and this is proven through qiyas to cases where owners are restricted by others' rights.

Ruling on the Musta'ir of a Pledge: Compliance and Liability
Ruling on liability after compliance for a borrower of a pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two types of musta'ir in rahn and state the Hanafi ruling on liability when the musta'ir rahn complies after violation.

Core Idea
After compliance, the musta'ir rahn becomes a depositee and is not liable for loss.

This passage from the Hidayah clarifies a subtle point about liability in borrowing for a pledge. The author distinguishes between a borrower who uses the item as a pledge (musta'ir rahn) and one who borrows for personal use. The key is whether the borrower's possession is deemed the owner's possession after compliance. Understanding this distinction prevents misapplication of liability rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of musta'ir
Read the passage to find the two categories: musta'ir who borrows to pledge (musta'ir rahn) and musta'ir who borrows for personal use (pure musta'ir). Recognize that the ruling differs between them.
The pure musta'ir remains a bailee for his own benefit.
2
State the ruling for musta'ir rahn after compliance
The ruling is that if the musta'ir rahn violates (e.g., uses the item) but then returns it to the owner before loss, he is not liable for any subsequent loss.
This is the core legal principle derived from the text.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas) with the depositee
The author compares the musta'ir rahn to a depositee (mudi') who, after violation, complies before loss. In both cases, compliance legally restores the owner's possession, making the holder a trustee (amin).
The illa (effective cause) is the restoration of owner's possession in law.
4
Contrast with the pure musta'ir
For a pure musta'ir, his possession is his own; compliance does not legally transfer possession to the owner until physical return. Hence, if loss occurs after compliance but before physical return, he remains liable.
The distinction hinges on the purpose of the borrowing.
5
Apply the principle to a scenario
Given a scenario involving a musta'ir rahn, determine liability step by step: identify the borrower type, check for violation, note compliance, then apply the ruling.
Practice cements the analytical chain.

Source Text

مستغیر رہن کا حکم تو وہ ہے جو مذکور ہوا کہ وہ مخالفت کے بعد موافقت کرے تو بعد موافقت ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وہ مودع کے درجہ میں ہے ۔ اور مودع اور امین نے جب موافقت کرلی تو گویا حکماً اب امانت پر مالک کا قبضہ ہو گیا اور جب حکماً مالک کا قبضہ ہو گیا تو اب ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور خالص مستغیر کا قبضہ اپنا ذاتی قبضہ ہے لہذاوہاں حکما ما لک کا قبضہ نہیں ہوا بلکہ مالک کا قبضہ تب ہی ہوگا جبکہ وہ مستعار مالک کے حوالہ کر دے لہذا اگر اس کی جانب سے تعدی کے بعد بھی مستعار ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اور مستعغیر رہن پر نہ ہوگا۔ اب رہی یہ بات کہ مستعغیر رہن میں حکما آمر کا قبضہ کیسے مانا گیا ہے؟
تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مستغیر رہن جو کچھ کر لگا یعنی مرتہن کے پاس رہن رکھنا وہ آمر کے مقصود کی تحصیل کیلئے کرتا ہے کیونکہ آمر (معیر ) کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ اگر مرہون مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے جس سے مرتہن قرض کو وصول پانے والا قرار دیا جائے تو اس وقت معیر کو حق ہوگا کہ راہن سے ضمان لے لے کیونکہ اس وقت راہن نے اس کے مال سے اپنے قرض کو ادا کیا ہے۔
بہر حال ان وجوہات کی وجہ سے ان دونوں مستعبیروں میں فرق کیا گیا ہے۔
The musta'ir (borrower) will not be a guarantor because when the musta'ir redeems the pledge, he is no longer a borrower; rather he becomes a depositee, and the ruling of the depositee and trustee is that if he complies with the owner after violation but before loss, then no guarantee is obligatory upon him. How many types of musta'ir are there? This is contrary to the (pure) borrower because his possession is his own possession, so reaching the owner's hand is necessary. As for the borrower in the context of a pledge, he achieves the purpose of the orderer, which is recourse against him at the time of loss and realization of receipt. Translation: And this is contrary to the borrower because the borrower's possession is his personal possession, so delivery to the owner is necessary. However, the borrower of a pledge achieves the purpose of the orderer, and that purpose is the orderer's recourse against the borrower (at the possession of the pledgee) at the time of loss and when receipt is realized. Explanation: The musta'ir has two types: (1) the musta'ir who borrows for the sake of the pledge, and (2) the musta'ir who borrows for his own work. The ruling of each is separate. The ruling of the musta'ir for a pledge is as mentioned: if he complies after violation, then after compliance he is not liable for loss because he is in the position of a depositee. And when the depositee and trustee have complied, then it is as if the owner's possession has been established over the trust legally. And when the owner's possession is established legally, then loss does not necessitate guarantee. And the pure musta'ir's possession is his own personal possession, so legal possession of the owner is not established there; rather the owner's possession is only established when he hands over the borrowed item to the owner. Therefore, if after his transgression the borrowed item is lost, then guarantee is obligatory upon him, but not upon the musta'ir of a pledge. Now the question is: how is the orderer's possession legally recognized in the musta'ir of a pledge? The answer is that whatever the musta'ir of a pledge does, i.e., placing the pledge with the pledgee, he does it to achieve the purpose of the orderer. Because the purpose of the orderer (the lender) is that if the pledge is lost with the pledgee, so that the pledgee is deemed to have recovered the debt, then at that time the orderer has the right to recover the guarantee from the pledgor, because the pledgor has repaid his debt with the orderer's property. In any case, due to these reasons, a distinction is made between these two types of borrowers.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
The passage explains the ruling on a musta'ir (borrower) in the context of a pledge (rahn). The author first states the ruling: a musta'ir who redeems the pledge (i.e., returns it to the owner) is not liable for any subsequent loss, even if he previously violated the terms, because he becomes like a mudi' (depositee) or amin (trustee). The proof is that after compliance, the owner's possession is legally deemed to have been restored. The passage then distinguishes two types of musta'ir: (1) one who borrows the item specifically to use it as a pledge (musta'ir rahn) and (2) one who borrows for his own personal use. The ruling for the first is as stated: after compliance, he is not liable. The second type (pure musta'ir) retains personal possession; therefore, even if he complies after violation, the owner's possession is not legally restored until the item is physically handed back. Hence, if loss occurs after compliance but before physical return, the pure musta'ir remains liable. The rationale is that the musta'ir rahn acts on behalf of the lender (the 'amir/mu'ir) to achieve the lender's purpose: securing recourse against the pledgor if the pledge is lost. Thus, the lender's possession is legally deemed to exist through the musta'ir rahn. This distinction is based on qiyas (analogy) with the case of a depositee.

Key Terms
مستغیر (musta'ir): A borrower who takes an item for temporary use; in this passage, distinguished between borrowing for the purpose of rahn and for personal use.
مودع (mudi'): Depositee, one who receives property for safekeeping.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability to compensate for loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The musta'ir rahn is not liable after compliance, unlike the pure musta'ir, because his possession is deemed the owner's through the pledge purpose.

Ruling on Rahin's Transgression: Owner's Liability on Pledged Property
Ruling with qiyas proof establishing owner's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the rahin must compensate for damage to the marhun and explain the qiyas proof using the concept of haqq lazim.

Core Idea
A pledgor who damages the pledged item must compensate because the pledgee's binding right makes the pledgor a stranger regarding liability.

It is a general principle that an owner is not liable for damaging his own property. However, the Hanafi school establishes an exception: when another person's binding right (haqq lazim) attaches to the property, the owner is treated as a stranger and must compensate for any loss caused. This lesson explores the ruling on the pledgor's transgression against the pledged item, and its justification through qiyas with two analogous cases from inheritance and bequest.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The passage opens with 'Jinayat al-rahin ala al-rahn madhmunah' - the rahin's transgression against the pledge is guaranteed. Identify this as the core ruling.
The ruling applies whether the damage is intentional or accidental, as it focuses on the right destroyed.
2
Identify the proof method
The text provides a proof ('li-annahu tafwit haqq lazim...') and then a qiyas analogy ('ka-ta'alliq haqq al-warathah...'). The ruling is based on qiyas, not direct text.
The proof is aqli (rational) via analogy.
3
Analyze the qiyas structure
The first asl is the terminally ill person's property where heirs have a right preventing bequest beyond one-third. The illa is the attachment of a binding right (haqq lazim). The far' is the marhun with the pledgee's right. Therefore, the owner (rahin) becomes like a stranger and is liable.
The illa is jaliyyah (clear), extracted by tanqih al-manat.
4
Apply to the second case
A second analogy: a slave whose service is bequeathed; if heirs destroy him, they must pay compensation. This reinforces the principle, showing consistency across different rights.
Both analogies illustrate the same illa.
5
Extract the general principle
The commentary states a general principle: whenever a binding right attaches to property, the owner becomes like a stranger in terms of liability. This is the key legal takeaway.
The principle extends beyond rahn to all cases where haqq lazim exists.

قال وجناية الراهن على الرهن مضمونة لانه تفويت حق لازم محترم و تعلق مثله بالمال يجعل المالك كالاجنبى فى حق الضمان كتعلق حق الورثة بمال المريض مرض الموت يمنع نفاذ تبرعه فيما وراء الثلث والعبد الموصى بخدمته اذا أتلفه الورثة ضمنوا قيمته ليشتري بها عبد يقوم مقامه
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور راہن کی جنایت مرہون پر مضمون ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ( جنایت ) ایسے حق لازم کی تفویت ہے جو محترم ہے اور اس کے مثل کا مال کے ساتھ تعلق مالک کو اجنبی کے مثل کر دیتا ہے ضمان کے حق میں جیسے مریض مرض الموت کے مال کے ساتھ حق ورثاء کا تعلق ثلث کے علاوہ میں اس کے تبرع کے نفاذ کو روک دیتا ہے اور جیسے وہ غلام جس کی خدمت کی وصیت کی گئی ہو جب اس کو ورثاء نے تلف کر دیا ہو تو وہ اس کی قیمت کے ضامن ہوں گے تا کہ اس قیمت سے ایک غلام خریدا جا سکے جو اس کے قائم مقام ہو سکے ۔
تشریح اگر مرہون پر راہن نے کوئی جنایت کی تو راہن کو اس کا تاوان ادا کرنا پڑے گا۔
جناب یہ تو عجیب سی منطق ہے کہ مالک سے بھی ضمان لیا جائے؟ جی ہاں! بعض صورتوں میں مالک اجنبی کے مثل ہو جاتا ہے اور اس پر ممان واجب ہو جاتا ہے اس کے لئے اصول کلی یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کے مال کے ساتھ کسی کا حق لازم ہو گیا تو اب مالک اجنبی کے مثل ہو گا۔
لہذا اگر کوئی شخص مرض الموت کا مریض ہے وہ اپنے مال کا مالک ہے لیکن اس کے مال کے ساتھ ورثاء کا حق متعلق ہو دیکا ہے اس لئے ثلث سے زیادہ میں اس کے تبرعات صدقہ وصیت وغیرہ نافذ نہ ہوں گے یعنی ثلث سے زیادہ میں وہ اجنبی کے مثل ہو گیا ہے اسی طرح اگر کسی نے وصیت کی میرا فلاں غلام خالد کی خدمت کیا کریگا اور اس کے بعد ورثاء نے اس غلام کو کسی بھی طریقہ پر تلف کر دیا تو ان پر اس کی قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوگا تا کہ اس قیمت سے دوسرا غلام خریدا جا سکے اور وہ خالد کی خدمت کیا کرے۔ حالانکہ ورثا اس کے مالک تھے لیکن موصی لہ کا حق لازم اس کے ساتھ متعلق تھا اس لیے مالکین کو اجنبی کے درجہ میں اتار کر ضمان واجب کر دیا گیا ہے اسی طرح راہن کے اوپر بھی ممان واجب ہوگا۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And the rahin's transgression against the pledge is guaranteed because it is a destruction of a binding respected right, and the attachment of something like it to property makes the owner like a stranger in the matter of guarantee, just as the attachment of the heirs' right to the property of a person suffering from terminal illness prevents the enforcement of his gift in excess of one-third, and just as a slave whose service is bequeathed, if the heirs destroy him, they are liable for his value to buy a slave who will perform that service. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the rahin's transgression against the pledge is guaranteed because this (transgression) is the destruction of a binding right that is respected, and the attachment of its like to property makes the owner like a stranger regarding guarantee, just as the attachment of the heirs' right to the property of a terminally ill person prevents the enforcement of his charitable disposals beyond one-third, and just as the slave whose service is bequeathed, when the heirs destroy him, they are liable for his value to buy a slave who can take his place. Explanation: If the rahin commits any transgression against the pledged item, then the rahin must pay compensation for it. Sir, this is strange logic: can the owner also be held liable? Yes! In some situations, the owner becomes like a stranger, and guarantee becomes obligatory upon him. The general principle for this is: if someone's binding right attaches to any property, then the owner becomes like a stranger. Therefore, if a person is terminally ill, he is the owner of his property, but the heirs' right is attached to his property, so his gifts, charity, bequests, etc. beyond one-third are not enforceable; i.e., beyond one-third he has become like a stranger. Similarly, if someone bequeaths that a certain slave should serve Khalid, and then the heirs destroy that slave by any means, they are liable for his value so that another slave may be purchased with that value and perform Khalid's service. Although the heirs were the owners, the legatee's binding right was attached to the slave; therefore, the owners were brought down to the level of strangers and guarantee was made obligatory. Similarly, guarantee is obligatory upon the rahin.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the rahin (pledgor) is liable for damaging the marhun (pledged item). The proof is qiyas (analogy) with two cases: (1) a terminally ill person's right of heirs prevents him from making gifts beyond one-third, and (2) a slave whose service is bequeathed; if the heirs destroy him, they must pay compensation. In both cases, the owner (or heirs) are treated as strangers regarding liability because a binding right (haqq lazim) of another person is attached to the property. Similarly, the pledgee's right is attached to the pledged item, making the rahin liable for destroying that right. The commentary emphasizes the general principle: whenever a binding right attaches to property, the owner becomes like a stranger in terms of liability.

Key Terms
جنایت (jinayat): Transgression or wrongful act causing damage, here specifically damage to the pledged item.
مضمون (madhmun): Guaranteed, meaning the perpetrator must compensate.
حق لازم (haqq lazim): A binding right that must be fulfilled, such as the pledgee's right over the pledged item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He must pay compensation because the pledgee's right is attached.
C) The pledgee must pay compensation.
D) The pledge is forfeited.

Key Takeaway
The rahin is liable for damaging the marhun because the pledgee's binding right makes him a stranger regarding guarantee.

Debtor's Liability for Damaging the Pledge
Ruling with proof via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the debtor is liable for damage to the pledge and explain the qiyas (analogy) that establishes this liability.

Core Idea
A debtor must pay for damaging the pledge because the creditor's right makes him like a stranger.

You might think that the owner of a pledged item cannot be held responsible for damaging it, since it is his own property. However, the Hanafi school rules that the debtor is indeed liable. This ruling is derived through qiyas (analogical reasoning) based on cases where a third party's right is attached to property. In this lesson, we will unpack the reasoning behind this ruling and see how it applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the explicit ruling from al-Quduri: the debtor's criminal act on the pledge is liable (madhmun). This means he must pay compensation (damān).
The ruling is wajib in the sense of financial obligation.
2
Understand the Attached Right
Identify the creditor's right (haqq lazim) that is attached to the pledged property. This right makes the pledge inviolable (muhtaram) with respect to the debtor.
The right is the debt itself, which is secured by the pledge.
3
Recognize the Principle
When a third party's right is attached to property, the owner is treated like a stranger (ajnabī) regarding that property. The owner loses the usual immunity from liability for damaging his own property.
This is a general Hanafi principle applicable in several chapters.
4
Follow the Qiyas (Analogy)
The text provides two analogous cases: (1) a terminally ill person's property subject to heirs' rights, where donations beyond one-third are blocked; (2) a bequeathed slave destroyed by heirs, where they must pay his price. The common illa (effective cause) is the attachment of a third-party right. Apply this to the pledge scenario.
The qiyas is khafī (subtle) because the analogy is not directly on the surface.
5
Apply to a New Scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., debtor accidentally crashes the pledged car), determine liability by checking if a third-party right is attached and if the debtor's act caused destruction.
Consider if the act is a jinaya (criminal/offensive) or merely accidental – the principle covers both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور راہن کی جنایت مرہون پر مضمون ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ( جنایت ) ایسے حق لازم کی تفویت ہے جو محترم ہے اور اس کے مثل کا مال کے ساتھ تعلق مالک کو اجنبی کے مثل کر دیتا ہے ضمان کے حق میں جیسے مریض مرض الموت کے مال کے ساتھ حق ورثاء کا تعلق ثلث کے علاوہ میں اس کے تبرع کے نفاذ کو روک دیتا ہے اور جیسے وہ غلام جس کی خدمت کی وصیت کی گئی ہو جب اس کو ورثاء نے تلف کر دیا ہو تو وہ اس کی قیمت کے ضامن ہوں گے تا کہ اس قیمت سے ایک غلام خریدا جا سکے جو اس کے قائم مقام ہو سکے ۔
تشریح اگر مرہون پر راہن نے کوئی جنایت کی تو راہن کو اس کا تاوان ادا کرنا پڑے گا۔
جناب یہ تو عجیب سی منطق ہے کہ مالک سے بھی ضمان لیا جائے؟ جی ہاں! بعض صورتوں میں مالک اجنبی کے مثل ہو جاتا ہے اور اس پر عمان واجب ہو جاتا ہے اس کے لئے اصول کلی یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کے مال کے ساتھ کسی کا حق لازم ہو گیا تو اب مالک اجنبی کے مثل ہو گا۔
لہذا اگر کوئی شخص مرض الموت کا مریض ہے وہ اپنے مال کا مالک ہے لیکن اس کے مال کے ساتھ ورثاء کا حق متعلق ہو دیکا ہے اس لئے ثلث سے زیادہ میں اس کے تبرعات صدقہ وصیت وغیرہ نافذ نہ ہوں گے یعنی ثلث سے زیادہ میں وہ اجنبی کے مثل ہو گیا ہے اسی طرح اگر کسی نے وصیت کی میرا فلاں غلام خالد کی خدمت کیا کریگا اور اس کے بعد ورثاء نے اس غلام کو کسی بھی طریقہ پر تلف کر دیا تو ان پر اس کی قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوگا تا کہ اس قیمت سے دوسرا غلام خریدا جا سکے اور وہ خالد کی خدمت کیا کرے۔ حالانکہ ورثا اس کے مالک تھے لیکن موصی لہ کا حق لازم اس کے ساتھ متعلق تھا اس لیے مالکین کو اجنبی کے درجہ میں اتار کر ضمان واجب کر دیا گیا ہے اسی طرح راہن کے اوپر بھی منمان واجب ہوگا۔
The translation of Quduri said: The criminal act of the debtor on the pledge is liable, because it is a destruction of a necessary right that is respected, and its like's connection with property makes the owner like a stranger in terms of guarantee. Just as the right of heirs in the property of a terminally ill person prevents the execution of his donations beyond one-third. And just as a slave whose service has been bequeathed, when the heirs destroy him, they will be liable for his price so that a slave can be purchased who can take his place. Explanation: If the debtor commits a crime on the pledge, he will have to pay compensation. This is strange logic that even the owner is held liable? Yes! In some cases the owner becomes like a stranger and compensation becomes obligatory. The general principle is: If a right becomes attached to someone's property, then the owner becomes like a stranger. So if a person is terminally ill, he is owner of his property but the right of heirs is attached, so his donations beyond one-third are not effective. Similarly, if someone bequeaths that his slave should serve Khalid, and the heirs destroy the slave, they are liable for his price. Although the heirs were owners, the right of the legatee was attached, so they are treated as strangers and liable. Likewise, the debtor will be liable.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Quduri's matn. The author states that the debtor's criminal act on the pledged property is liable (madhmun). The reason is that the act destroys a right (haqq lazim) that is respected (muhtaram). The analogy is with two scenarios: (1) A terminally ill person's property is subject to the right of heirs, so his donations beyond one-third are not effective; (2) A slave whose services are bequeathed, if the heirs destroy him, they must pay his price. In both cases, the owner is treated like a stranger because a third party's right is attached. Similarly, because the creditor (murtahin) has a right (the debt) attached to the pledge, the debtor acts against his own interest and is liable for the damage. This is an example of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مضمون (madhmun): liable, subject to guarantee
محترم (muhtaram): respected, inviolable
تفویت (tafwit): destruction, loss

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the debtor liable for damage to the pledged property?
A) Because the pledge is owned by the creditor.
B) Because the creditor has a right attached to the pledge, making the debtor like a stranger.
C) Because the debtor is always liable for any damage he causes.
D) Because the pledge is considered a trust in the debtor's hands.

Key Takeaway
The debtor's liability for damaging the pledge arises because the creditor's right makes the debtor effectively a stranger to the property.

Creditor's Criminal Act on Pledge and Reduction of Debt
States that creditor's act on pledge reduces his debt or becomes new guarantee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the creditor's act on a pledge and apply the condition of sameness of type to determine whether the debt is reduced or a separate guarantee attaches.

Core Idea
The creditor's damage to the pledge cancels debt only if both are of the same type; otherwise, a new guarantee is created.

In this passage from Quduri's al-Mukhtasar, we learn the legal effect when a creditor (murtahin) damages the pledged item (marhun). The ruling distinguishes between cases where the debt and the damage are of the same type and where they differ. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the law of pledge (rahn) in financial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Consider the creditor's act (jinaayah) on the pledge. What is the legal consequence? The passage states that it cancels the debt by the amount of the damage, but this depends on the type.
The act is a transgression (ta'addi) because the pledge is the debtor's property.
2
Understand the condition of sameness of type
The debt is reduced only if the debt and the damage are of the same type (jins), e.g., both cash or both wheat. If they differ, the debt remains unchanged, and the creditor becomes liable for a separate guarantee (daman).
The explanation clarifies: 'if the debt is, for example, of standard measure or weight items, then the debt will not be cancelled.'
3
Trace the reasoning (talil)
The passage gives the rationale: the pledge is the property (milk) of the debtor, and the creditor has transgressed upon it. Hence, he must compensate the owner.
This is a form of qiyas: transgression on property creates liability.
4
Determine the practical outcome for the debtor
If the debt is reduced, the debtor owes less. If a separate guarantee is created, that guarantee becomes an additional pledge. When the debtor repays the original debt, he retrieves both the original pledge and the additional guarantee.
This ensures the debtor is fully compensated for the damage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتہن کی مرہون پر جنایت بقدر جنایت دین کو ساقط کر دے گی
قال وجناية المرتهن عليه تسقط من دينه بقدرها ومعناه ان يكون الضمان على صفة الدين وهذا لان العين ملک المالك وقد تعدى عليه المرتهن فيضمنه لمالكه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرہون پر مرتہن کی جنایت بقدر جنایت اس کا قرض ساقط کر دے گی اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ ممان دین کی صفت پر ہوگا اور یہ اس لئے کہ عین مالک کی ملک ہے حالانکہ عین پر مرتبین نے تعدی کی ہے تو وہ اس کے مالک کے لئے اس کا ضامن ہو گا۔
تشریح اگر مرتہن نے مرہون پر جنایت کی تو جنایت کے بقدر قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا یعنی جبکہ قرض اور ضمان ایک جنس کے ہوں اور اگر قرض مثلا الکیلی یا موزونی اشیاء ہوں تو قرض ساقط نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مرتہن پر اس کا ضمان واجب کر کے اس مضمان کو بھی مرہون کر دیا جائے گا۔ پھر جب راہن قرض ادا کر دے تو راہن مرتہن کے پاس سے مرہون مع ضمان کے واپس لے لے۔ اور مرتہن پر ضمان واجب ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مرہون راہن کی ملک ہے جس پر مرتہن نے تعدی کی ہے تو اس تعدی کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
The creditor's criminal act on the pledge will cancel his debt by the amount of it. And its meaning is that the guarantee will be of the same quality as the debt. And this is because the property is the owner's possession, and the creditor has transgressed upon it, so he is liable to its owner. Explanation: If the creditor commits a crime on the pledge, the debt will be cancelled by the amount of the crime, meaning when the debt and the guarantee are of the same type. If the debt is, for example, of standard measure or weight items, then the debt will not be cancelled; rather, the creditor will be liable for its guarantee and that guaranteed amount will also become part of the pledge. Then when the debtor pays the debt, he will take back the pledge along with the guarantee. The reason the creditor is liable is that the pledge is the property of the debtor, which the creditor has transgressed upon, so he is liable.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling from Quduri's matn that if the creditor (murtahin) commits a criminal act on the pledged property, his debt is reduced proportionally. The guarantee shares the same quality as the debt. The explanation clarifies that this applies when the debt and guarantee are of the same type (e.g., both in dirhams). If they are different (e.g., debt of wheat, guarantee of cash), the debt is not cancelled; instead, the liability becomes a separate guarantee that is added to the pledge as another security. When the debtor repays the original debt, he retrieves the pledge along with this added guarantee. The rationale is that the creditor has unlawfully acted on the debtor's property, so he must compensate.

Key Terms
تسقط (tasquṭ): cancels, reduces
ضمان (ḍamān): guarantee, liability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The debt is completely cancelled.
B) The debt is reduced by the amount of damage, but only if both are of the same type.
C) The debtor's debt increases.
D) The creditor is not liable.

Key Takeaway
The creditor's liability for damaging the pledge either reduces his debt (same type) or creates a separate guarantee (different types).

Pledge's Criminal Act: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability of slave-pledge's criminal act against debtor/creditor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a pledged slave's criminal act according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
A slave-pledge's act against his owner (debtor) is void; against the creditor, Sahibayn consider it, but Abu Hanifa says void.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the liability of a pledged slave's criminal act. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how ownership and rights affect liability in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text claim
Read Quduri's statement in the source: 'The criminal act of the pledge on the debtor and creditor and on their property is void.' This is the starting point that Abu Hanifa agrees with.
The base text does not mention the Sahibayn's exception.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that all acts of the pledged slave against the debtor, creditor, or their property are void (hadar) — no financial liability arises.
For intentional killing, qisas is separate (not financial liability).
3
State Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn say the act against the creditor is considered (mubra) — it creates liability. Their proof is an analogy (qiyas): just as the act of usurped property against the usurpee is considered (because the usurpee is not the owner), so the slave's act against the creditor (who is not the owner) should be considered.
The analogy is based on the illa (cause) of acting against a non-owner.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy. The slave is fully owned by the debtor; the creditor only has a right of retention (rahn), not ownership. Therefore, the slave's act against the debtor is against the owner, and against the creditor is against a non-owner, but Abu Hanifa restricts consideration to acts against a complete owner only.
This is a refinement of the illa: only complete ownership makes an act void.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view: all acts are void (hadar). This is preferred by later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani.
The practical consequence: no liability for the slave's damage to the creditor's property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہن کی راہن اور مرتہن اور ان دونوں کے مال پر جنایت ہدر ہے ، اقوال فقہاء
قال وجناية الرهن على الراهن والمرتهن وعلى مالهما هدر وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا جنايته على المرتهن تبرة والمراد بالجناية على النفس ما يوجب المال اما الو فاقية فلانها جناية المملوك على المالك الاترى انه لومات كان الكفن عليه بخلاف جناية المغصوب على المغصوب منه لان الملك عند اداء الضمان يثبت للغاصب مستندا حتى يكون الكفن عليه فكانت جناية على غير المالک فاعتبرت
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور راہن و مرتہن پر اور ان کے مال پر مرہون کی جنایت رائیگاں ہے اور یہ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مرہون کی مرتہن پر جنایت معتبر ہے اور نفس پر جنایت سے مراد وہ جنایت ہے جو مال کو واجب کرتی ہو بہر حال اتفاقی مسئلہ ( کی وجہ ) یہ ہے کہ یہ مالک پر مملوک کی جنایت ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر غلام مرہون مر جائے تو کفن را ہن کے اوپر ہوگا بخلاف مغصوب منہ پر منصوب کی جنایت کے اس لئے کہ ضمان کی ادائیگی کے وقت ملکیت استناد کے طریقہ پر غاضب کے لئے ثابت ہوئی ہے یہاں تک کہ کفن غاصب کے اوپر ہو گا تو یہ (مغصوب منہ پر مغصوب کی جنایت ) غیر مالک کی جنایت ہے تو یہ جنایت معتبر ہوگی۔
تشریح پہلے تو رہن پر راہن اور مرتبہن کی جنایت کا مسئلہ مذکور ہوا ہے یہاں اس کے برعکس ہوا یعنی غلام مرہون نے راہن یا مرتین پر جنایت کی تو کیا حکم ہے؟ جس کی چار صورتیں ہیں۔
- مرہون نے راہن یا مرتہن کو عمد قتل کر دیا تو اس میں تو مرہون کے او پر قصاص واجب ہوگا۔
-۲- مرہون نے راہن یا مرتہن کو خطام قتل کیا تو یہاں غلام مرہون پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہو گا ۔
۳۔ مرہون نے مرتہن کے یا راہن کے کچھ اعضاء کاٹ دیئے جس سے وہ ہلاک تو نہیں ہوئے لیکن مشقت میں پھنس گئے اس میں بھی مرہون پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا۔
مرہون نے راہن یا مرتہن کا مال ضائع کر دیا اس میں بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
ی تفصیل امام ابو حنیفہ کے مذہب کے مطابق ہے۔ اس میں صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مرہون راہن پر جنایت کرے تو اب ہم امام صاحب کے قول سے متفق ہیں اور اگر مرتہن پر جنایت کرے تو صاحبین اس جنایت کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں یعنی جنایت فی نفس المرتہن میں ورنہ جنایت فی مال المرتہن کا حکم آگے مذکور ہے والمراد الخ سے مصنف بتاتے ہیں کہ جہاں کہا گیا ہے کہ جنایت بالنفس رائیگاں ہے اس سے مراد وہ جنایت ہے جو قصاص کو واجب نہ کرے ورنہ اگر قصاص کو واجب کرے تو پھر قصاص واجب ہوگا بہر حال راہن کے بارے میں صاحبین اور امام صاحب دونوں کا اتفاق ہے کہ ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں مملوک نے اپنے مالک پر جنایت کی ہے جو غیر معتبر
The criminal act of the pledge on the debtor and creditor and on their property is void. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two companions said: His criminal act on the creditor is considered. What is meant by criminal act on the person is that which necessitates property. As for the agreement, it is because it is the criminal act of the owned against the owner. Do you not see that if the pledged slave dies, the shroud is upon the debtor? Contrary to the criminal act of the usurped property upon the usurpee, because ownership at the time of payment of guarantee is established for the usurper retrospectively, so the shroud is upon the usurper. Thus, it is a criminal act against a non-owner, so it is considered. Explanation: Previously the criminal act of the debtor and creditor on the pledge was mentioned. Here is the opposite: if the pledged slave commits a crime against the debtor or creditor, what is the ruling? There are four scenarios: (1) If the slave intentionally kills the debtor or creditor, qisas is obligatory. (2) If he kills accidentally, no liability. (3) If he cuts off limbs without death, no liability. (4) If he destroys property, no liability. This detail is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. There is a difference between the two companions: they say if the slave commits a crime against the debtor, they agree with Imam, but if against the creditor, they consider it. That is for crimes against the person; the ruling for property crimes is mentioned elsewhere. The author explains that where it is said that the criminal act on the person is void, it means that which does not necessitate qisas. If it does necessitate qisas, then qisas is obligatory. In any case, regarding the debtor, both the Imam and the two companions agree that no liability is due, because it is a slave's crime against his owner, which is not considered.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of a pledged slave's criminal act. According to Abu Hanifa, all acts of the slave against the debtor, creditor, or their property are void (hadar), meaning no liability. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the act is considered (mubra) when it is against the creditor, but not against the debtor. The reasoning: the slave is owned by the debtor, so his act against his owner is not considered. However, against the creditor, he is acting against a non-owner, so it is considered. The text clarifies four scenarios: intentional killing leads to qisas (not liability), accidental killing and other injuries/no liability, and property destruction/no liability according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn agree for acts against the debtor but differ for acts against the creditor's person. The author further explains that the phrase 'criminal act against the person' here refers to acts that do not require qisas; if qisas is due, it is separate.

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): void, without legal effect (no liability)
تبرة (tibra? (or mubra)): considered, effective (gives rise to liability)
جناية (jināyah): criminal act, delict

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a pledged slave accidentally kills the creditor, what is the ruling?
A) The slave is liable for blood money.
B) The slave is sold to compensate.
C) No liability, it is void (hadar).
D) The debt is reduced.

Key Takeaway
The slave-pledge's criminal act against the debtor is always void; against the creditor, the relied-upon Hanafi position is also void, though Sahibayn considered it. Intentional killing triggers qisas, not financial liability.

The Tort of a Mortgaged Slave Against the Mortgagee
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tort liability of mortgaged slave against mortgagee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding the liability of a mortgaged slave's tort against the mortgagee, and explain the reasoning behind each position, including the analogy with ghasb (usurpation).

Core Idea
A slave's tort against his owner is hdr; but against the mortgagee, Abu Hanifah says hdr, Sahibayn say mu'tabar.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn presents a classical intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal consequence of a mortgaged slave committing a tort against the mortgagee. While both parties agree that a tort against the mortgagor (owner) is hdr (of no consequence), they differ when the victim is the mortgagee. The disagreement hinges on the nature of ownership in a pledge and the analogy with usurpation (ghasb). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle that a slave's tort against his owner is not actionable, and to distinguish the mortgage relationship from other possession-based relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed parties
The act is a tort (jinaayah) committed by a mortgaged slave (rahn) against the mortgagee (murtain). The dispute: is this tort considered (mu'tabar) or hdr?
2
State Abu Hanifah's position and its proof
Abu Hanifah holds the tort is hdr against both mortgagor and mortgagee. His proof: the slave is owned by the mortgagor; a slave's tort against his owner is hdr. The mortgagee does not become owner. Analogy with ghasb fails because in ghasb the usurper becomes owner retroactively upon paying guarantee.
The shroud (kafan) obligation on the mortgagor proves ownership.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the tort against the mortgagee is mu'tabar. Their proof: the mortgagee is a non-owner; tort against a non-owner is generally actionable. Practical benefit: the mortgagee can take the slave as compensation, cancelling the mortgage and debt.
They agree with Abu Hanifah on tort against the mortgagor (owner).
4
Analyze the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifah, the mortgagee cannot claim any compensation. According to Sahibayn, the mortgagee may either demand the slave as compensation (ending the mortgage) or forgive the tort and let the mortgage continue.
This difference affects the mortgagee's options in case of harm.

Source Text

كتاب الرهن 
قال وجناية الرهن على الراهن والمرتهن وعلى مالهما هدر وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا جنايته على المرتهن تبرة والمراد بالجناية على النفس ما يوجب المال اما الو فاقية فلانها جناية المملوك على المالك الاترى انه لومات كان الكفن عليه بخلاف جناية المغصوب على المغصوب منه لان الملك عند اداء الضمان يثبت للغاصب مستندا حتى يكون الكفن عليه فكانت جناية على غير المالک فاعتبرت
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور راہن و مرتہن پر اور ان کے مال پر مرہون کی جنایت رائیگاں ہے اور یہ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مرہون کی مرتہن پر جنایت معتبر ہے اور نفس پر جنایت سے مراد وہ جنایت ہے جو مال کو واجب کرتی ہو بہر حال اتفاقی مسئلہ ( کی وجہ ) یہ ہے کہ یہ مالک پر مملوک کی جنایت ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر غلام مرہون مر جائے تو کفن را ہن کے اوپر ہوگا بخلاف مغصوب منہ پر منصوب کی جنایت کے اس لئے کہ ضمان کی ادائیگی کے وقت ملکیت استناد کے طریقہ پر غاضب کے لئے ثابت ہوئی ہے یہاں تک کہ کفن غاصب کے اوپر ہو گا تو یہ (مغصوب منہ پر مغصوب کی جنایت ) غیر مالک کی جنایت ہے تو یہ جنایت معتبر ہوگی۔
تشریح پہلے تو رہن پر راہن اور مرتبہن کی جنایت کا مسئلہ مذکور ہوا ہے یہاں اس کے برعکس ہوا یعنی غلام مرہون نے راہن یا مرتین پر جنایت کی تو کیا حکم ہے؟ جس کی چار صورتیں ہیں۔

ی تفصیل امام ابو حنیفہ کے مذہب کے مطابق ہے۔ اس میں صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مرہون راہن پر جنایت کرے تو اب ہم امام صاحب کے قول سے متفق ہیں اور اگر مرتہن پر جنایت کرے تو صاحبین اس جنایت کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں یعنی جنایت فی نفس المرتہن میں ورنہ جنایت فی مال المرتہن کا حکم آگے مذکور ہے والمراد الخ سے مصنف بتاتے ہیں کہ جہاں کہا گیا ہے کہ جنایت بالنفس رائیگاں ہے اس سے مراد وہ جنایت ہے جو قصاص کو واجب نہ کرے ورنہ اگر قصاص کو واجب کرے تو پھر قصاص واجب ہوگا بہر حال راہن کے بارے میں صاحبین اور امام صاحب دونوں کا اتفاق ہے کہ ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں مملوک نے اپنے مالک پر جنایت کی ہے جو غیر معتبر ہوتی ہے۔

صاحبین کی دلیل
ولهما فى الخلافية ان الجناية حصلت على غير مالكه وفى الاعتبار فائدة وهو دفع العبد اليه بالجناية فتعتبر ثم إن شاء الراهن والمرتهن إبطلا الرهن ودفعاه بالجناية الى المرتهن وان قال المرتهن لا اطلب الجناية فهو رهن على حاله
ترجمہ اور اختلافی مسئلہ میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جنایت اپنے مالک کے غیر پر حاصل ہوئی ہے اور جنایت کا اعتبار کرنے میں فائدہ ہے اور وہ جنابیت کی وجہ سے غلام مرتہن کو دینا ہے پس جنایت معتبر ہوگی پھر اگر راہن اور مرتہن چاہیں تو رہن کو باطل کر دیں اور جنایت کی وجہ سے غلام مرہون مرتہن کو دیدیں اور اگر مرتبین نے کہا کہ میں جنایت ( کا عوض ) طلب نہیں کرتا تو مرہون علیٰ حالہ رہن ہوگا۔ تشریح صاحبین نے کہا تھا کہ مرتہن پر مرہون کی جنایت معتبر ہے یہ ان کی دلیل ہے کہ یہاں مرہون کی مرتہن پر جنایت مالک پر جنایت نہیں ہے کیونکہ مالک تو راہن ہے اور یہاں اگر جنایت کو معتبر مان لیں تو اس میں فائدہ ہے کیونکہ جنایت کی وجہ سے مرہون غلام مرتہن کومل جائے گا۔
اگر چہ اس کی وجہ سے مرتہن کا قرض تو ساقط ہو جائے گا لیکن کبھی غلام کا مالک بن جانا عین مقصود ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ اگر وہ اس میں فائدہ سمجھے تو لے لے۔ اگر چہ قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا لیکن مقصود حاصل ہو جائے گا اور اگر وہ اس میں منفعت نہ سمجھے تو نہ لے اسی مرتہن کی رضاء کو بیان کرنے کے لئے مصنف نے فرمایا وان شاء... الخ یعنی راہن کے ساتھ ساتھ مرتہن بھی ابطال رہن پر راضی ہو کر اس کو جنایت میں لینا قبول کرے تب یہ بات ہے کہ جنایت کا تاوان بھی ادا ہو گیا اور قرض بھی ساقط ہو گیا۔ ورنہ اگر مرتہن یوں کہہ دے کہ مجھے جنایت کا تاوان نہیں چاہیے تو پھر غلام علی حالہ مرہون رہیگا۔
The Book of Mortgage. He said: The tort of the mortgaged slave against the mortgagor and the mortgagee and against their property is of no consequence (hadar). This is according to Abu Hanifah. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: His tort against the mortgagee is considered (tubra). By 'tort against the person' is meant what necessitates monetary compensation. As for the accidental case, it is because it is the tort of a slave against his owner. Do you not see that if he dies, the shroud is upon the mortgagor? Unlike the tort of a usurped slave against the one from whom he was usurped, because ownership at the time of paying the guarantee is established for the usurper retroactively, so that the shroud is upon the usurper, so it was a tort against a non-owner, thus it is considered. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The tort of the mortgaged slave against the mortgagor and mortgagee and their property is wasted, and this is according to Abu Hanifah. The two companions said: The tort of the mortgaged against the mortgagee is considered. By tort against the person is meant what obligates property. Anyway, the agreed issue is that this is the tort of a slave against his owner. Do you not see that if the mortgaged slave dies, the shroud is upon the mortgagor? Unlike the tort of a usurped slave against the one from whom he was usurped, because at the time of paying the guarantee, ownership is established for the usurper retroactively, so that the shroud is upon the usurper, so that tort (of the usurped against the usurpee) is a tort against a non-owner, so it is considered. Explanation: Previously the issue of the tort of the mortgagor and mortgagee against the mortgage was mentioned. Here the opposite occurs, i.e., the mortgaged slave commits a tort against the mortgagor or mortgagee, what is the ruling? It has four forms: (1) If the mortgaged slave kills the mortgagor or mortgagee intentionally, then qisas is obligatory upon the slave. (2) If he kills them accidentally, then there is no guarantee upon the slave. (3) If he cuts off some limbs without causing death, there is no guarantee. (4) If he destroys property, no guarantee. This detail is according to Imam Abu Hanifah. In this, the two companions differ: they say if the slave commits a tort against the mortgagor, we agree with Imam; but if against the mortgagee, they consider the tort (i.e., in tort against the person of the mortgagee; tort against his property is dealt with later). 'And the intended meaning' etc. The author indicates that where it is said the tort against the person is wasted, what is meant is the tort that does not necessitate qisas; otherwise, if it necessitates qisas, then qisas is obligatory. In any case, regarding the mortgagor, both the two companions and Imam agree that no guarantee is obligatory, and their proof is that here the slave committed a tort against his own owner, which is not considered. What is your evidence that the mortgaged slave is the property of the mortgagor? Answer: That if the mortgaged slave dies, his shroud is obligatory upon the mortgagor, which is proof that the mortgagor is his owner. Question: Then does your statement mean that if the slave causes loss to the owner, no guarantee is obligatory? Answer: Yes. Question: If a usurped slave causes some loss to the one from whom he was usurped, guarantee is obligatory upon the usurped slave even though he is property of the usurpee? Answer: The secret is that when the usurper pays the guarantee, he is considered the owner of the slave from the time of usurpation, and when the usurper is proven owner, the usurpee becomes a stranger, and a tort against a stranger is considered and its guarantee is obligatory. The proof of the two companions: In the disputed issue, their proof is that the tort occurred against a non-owner, and there is benefit in considering it, namely giving the slave to the mortgagee due to the tort, so it is considered. Then if the mortgagor and mortgagee wish, they can nullify the mortgage and give the slave to the mortgagee due to the tort. If the mortgagee says, 'I do not demand the tort (compensation)', then the slave remains as mortgage as before. Translation: In the disputed issue, the two companions' proof is that the tort occurred against a non-owner, and there is benefit in considering it, which is giving the slave to the mortgagee due to the tort, so the tort is considered. Then if the mortgagor and mortgagee wish, they nullify the mortgage and give the mortgaged slave to the mortgagee due to the tort. If the mortgagee says, 'I do not demand the tort (compensation)', then the mortgaged slave remains as mortgage as before. Explanation: The two companions said that the tort of the mortgaged against the mortgagee is considered. This is their proof: here the tort of the mortgaged against the mortgagee is not a tort against the owner because the owner is the mortgagor. And if we consider the tort, there is benefit because due to the tort, the mortgaged slave will go to the mortgagee. Even though due to this the mortgagee's debt will be cancelled, but sometimes becoming the owner of the slave is the very objective, because if he sees benefit, he takes him. Even if the debt is cancelled, the objective is achieved. If he does not see benefit, he does not take. To express the consent of the mortgagee, the author said: 'and if they wish...' meaning that if the mortgagee along with the mortgagor agrees to nullify the mortgage and accept the slave as compensation for the tort, then this is the case: the compensation for the tort is paid and the debt is cancelled. Otherwise, if the mortgagee says, 'I do not want compensation for the tort', then the slave remains as mortgage as before.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a mortgaged slave (rahn) when it commits a tort (jinaayah) against the mortgagor (raahin) or the mortgagee (murtain). The author first states the ruling from Al-Quduri's matn: according to Abu Hanifah, such a tort is 'hadar' (of no legal consequence, i.e., no financial liability) whether against the mortgagor or the mortgagee or their property. However, the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that if the tort is against the mortgagee, it is 'tubra' (considered, i.e., liable). The commentary explains that 'tort against the person' here refers to acts that necessitate monetary compensation, not qisas (retaliation). The agreed-upon reasoning for the case against the mortgagor is that the slave is owned by the mortgagor, and a slave's tort against his own owner is not actionable (hdr). This is proven by the fact that the shroud of a deceased slave is on the owner. The passage then contrasts this with the case of a usurped (maghsūb) slave: if a usurped slave commits a tort against the person from whom it was usurped (maghsūb minhu), it is considered because the usurper becomes the owner retroactively upon paying the guarantee, making the original owner a stranger. Thus, a tort against a stranger is actionable. The commentary then details four forms of tort: intentional killing (qisas applies), accidental killing (no guarantee), severing limbs (no guarantee), destroying property (no guarantee). This is according to Abu Hanifah. The disagreement is specifically when the tort is against the mortgagee. Sahibayn argue that since the mortgagee is not the owner (the mortgagor is), the tort is against a non-owner and thus actionable. Moreover, there is practical benefit: if the mortgagee desires, he can take the slave as compensation for the tort, cancelling the mortgage and the debt. If he does not desire, the slave remains mortgaged. The text does not explicitly state which position is mufta bihi (relied upon), but in the Hanafi school, the position of Imam Abu Hanifah is generally preferred in the primary texts unless specified otherwise. However, later fatwa works may adopt the view of Sahibayn in certain contexts. The commentary provides a thorough analysis of the underlying principles of ownership and analogy (qiyas) between mortgage and usurpation.

Key Terms
جناية (jinaayah): A harmful or tortious act committed by the mortgaged slave against the person or property of another, which may entail monetary compensation or qisas.
رهن (rahn): The mortgaged property (here a slave) that is held as security for a debt.
راهن (raahin): The mortgagor, i.e., the debtor who pledges the slave as security.
مرتهن (murtain): The mortgagee, i.e., the creditor who holds the pledged slave as security until the debt is repaid.
هدر (hdr): Of no legal consequence; the tort does not give rise to any financial liability or compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifah, what is the ruling if a mortgaged slave accidentally kills the mortgagee (murtain)?
A) The slave must be handed over to the mortgagee as compensation.
B) No financial liability (hdr) on the slave or mortgagor.
C) The mortgagee can claim blood money from the slave's owner.
D) The mortgage is automatically invalidated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the tort of a mortgaged slave against the mortgagee is disputed: Abu Hanifah holds it is hdr (no liability), while the Sahibayn consider it actionable, allowing the mortgagee to take the slave as compensation.

intermediate
8 min
Dispute on Validity of Mortgaged Slave's Crime Against Mortgagee
Intra-Hanafi dispute on considering crime of mortgaged slave against mortgagee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a crime by a mortgaged slave against the mortgagee is considered, and apply the benefit-based reasoning to analogous cases.

Core Idea
A crime by a mortgaged slave is considered only if it yields a net benefit to the mortgagee; otherwise, it is ignored.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific scenario: a slave pledged as collateral (marhun) commits a crime against the mortgagee (murtahin). The Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa differ on whether this crime is legally considered (mu'tabar) for compensation and ownership. The key revolves around the concept of benefit (fa'idah) and the mortgagee's dual role. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze benefit-based reasoning in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the exact legal question: is the crime of a mortgaged slave against the mortgagee considered (mu'tabar) for the purpose of transferring the slave as compensation?
2
Identify the two positions
Sahibayn say the crime is considered in all cases. Abu Hanifa says it is not considered when the slave's value equals the debt, and for excess value there are two narrations.
3
Analyze the proofs
Sahibayn argue benefit: the slave can be given to the mortgagee. Abu Hanifa argues circularity: the mortgagee would be both recipient and compensator, and no benefit when value equals debt.
Focus on the concept of fa'idah (benefit) and how it determines consideration.
4
Examine the scenario value = debt
Consensus (ittifaq) that the crime is not considered because no ownership transfer is possible, so no benefit.
5
Examine the scenario value > debt
Two narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) considered to the extent of the excess (amanah) by analogy to a trust slave, (2) not considered at all because the ruling of rahn (habs) prevails.
This step involves qiyas (analogical reasoning).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن

صاحبین کی دلیل
ولهما فى الخلافية ان الجناية حصلت على غير مالكه وفى الاعتبار فائدة وهو دفع العبد اليه بالجناية فتعتبر ثم إن شاء الراهن والمرتهن إبطلا الرهن ودفعاه بالجناية الى المرتهن وان قال المرتهن لا اطلب الجناية فهو رهن على حاله

امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل
وله ان هذه الجناية لو اعتبرناها للمرتهن كان عليه التطهير من الجناية لانها حصلت في ضمانه فلا يفيد وجوب الضمان له مع وجوب التخليص عليه وجنايته على مال المرتهن لا تعتبر بالاتفاق اذا كانت قيمته والدين سواء لانه لافائدة فى اعتبارها لانه لا يتملك العبد وهو الفائدة

وان كانت القيمة اكثر من الدين فعن ابي حنيفة انه يعتبر بقدر الامانة لان الفضل ليس في ضمانه فاشبه جناية العبد الوديعة على المستودع وعنه انها لا تعتبر لان حكم الرهن وهو الحبس فيه ثابت فصار كالمضمون وهذا بخلاف جناية الرهن على ابن الراهن او ابن المرتهن لان الاملاك حقيقة متباينة فصار كالجناية على الاجنبي
Book of Rahn. Sahibayn's proof: In the issue of difference, the crime occurred against other than its owner, and considering it has a benefit, which is giving the slave to him (the mortgagee) due to the crime, so it is considered. Then if the mortgagor and mortgagee wish, they may nullify the rahn and give the slave to the mortgagee due to the crime, and if the mortgagee says 'I do not demand the crime (compensation),' then it remains rahn as before. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: He said that if we consider this crime for the mortgagee, then he would be obligated to purify (compensate) for the crime because it occurred under his guarantee (daman), so the obligation of guarantee for him together with the obligation of discharging (the crime's consequence) would not be beneficial. And his (the slave's) crime against the property of the mortgagee is not considered by consensus when the value (of the slave) and the debt are equal, because there is no benefit in considering it, since he does not become owner of the slave, and that (ownership) is the benefit. And if the value is more than the debt, then from Abu Hanifa there is a narration that it is considered to the extent of the trust (amanah), because the excess is not in his guarantee, so it resembles the crime of a slave held as a trust (wadi'ah) against the trustee; and from him (another narration) that it is not considered because the ruling of rahn, which is detention (habs), is established in it, so the excess becomes like what is guaranteed (marmun). And this is unlike the crime of a mortgaged slave against the son of the mortgagor or the son of the mortgagee, because ownerships are truly distinct, so it becomes like a crime against a stranger.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal consideration of a crime (jinayah) committed by a mortgaged slave (marhun) against the mortgagee (murtahin). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the crime is validly considered because it occurs against a non-owner (the mortgagee is not the owner of the slave; the mortgagor is). Considering the crime yields a benefit: the slave is given to the mortgagee as compensation, potentially satisfying the debt. They provide a practical ruling: if both parties agree, they can cancel the mortgage and give the slave to the mortgagee; if the mortgagee declines, the slave remains mortgaged.

Imam Abu Hanifa counter-argues that if the crime were considered for the mortgagee, the mortgagee would be both the recipient of compensation and the one obligated to purify (discharge) the crime because the crime occurred under his guarantee (daman). This circularity yields no benefit. Moreover, there is consensus that if the slave's value equals the debt, the crime is not considered because no benefit arises—the mortgagee cannot become owner of the slave (since the value is already earmarked for the debt). The benefit of ownership is thus absent.

The passage then discusses a scenario where the slave's value exceeds the debt. Two narrations exist from Abu Hanifa. First: the crime is considered to the extent of the trust (amanah) because the excess value is not under the mortgagee's guarantee, so it resembles a crime by a slave held as a trust (wadi'ah) against the trustee. Second narration: the crime is not considered even for the excess because the ruling of rahn (detention) remains in effect, making the entire slave like a guaranteed item. The text concludes by distinguishing this from a crime by the mortgaged slave against the child of the mortgagor or mortgagee, where ownerships are truly distinct, so the crime is treated like one against a stranger.

Key Terms
مرهون (marhun): The property (here a slave) that is pledged as collateral in a rahn contract.
جنایت (jinayah): A harmful act (crime or tort) committed by the slave, triggering liability (daman).
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability for compensation; the mortgagee's guarantee under which the crime occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the primary reason for considering the crime of a mortgaged slave against the mortgagee valid?
A) Because the slave belongs to the mortgagee
B) Because the crime occurs against a non-owner and yields benefit
C) Because the mortgagee is obligated to compensate
D) Because the mortgagor consents

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the consideration of a crime involving a mortgaged slave hinges on whether it yields a real benefit without circular liability.
